Qada When Only One Rak'ah Has Recitation in Nafal
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for missed recitation in nafal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi positions on qada when recitation is missed in one rak'ah of a four-rak'ah nafal and apply the underlying principle of tahrima breakage.

Core Idea
Missing recitation in one rak'ah of a nafal pair invalidates the tahrima of that pair, requiring qada of that pair only.

In this passage, the Hanafi masters differ on whether missing recitation in a single rak'ah of a four-rak'ah nafal requires qada of all four or just the affected pair. The dispute centers on how the deficiency affects the tahrima (sanctity) of the prayer. Understanding this helps you see how the school derives rulings from the hadith requiring recitation in every rak'ah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
The passage presents two scenarios: (1) recitation in only one rak'ah of the first pair (first two rak'ahs), and (2) recitation in only one rak'ah of the last pair (last two rak'ahs). For each, there is disagreement among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.
In nafal, the prayer of four rak'ahs is performed as two separate pairs (tahrima per pair).
2
State the positions for case 1
In case 1, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (shaykhayn) say qada of four rak'ahs. Muhammad says qada of two rak'ahs (the first pair).
The shaykhayn consider the tahrima of both pairs broken; Muhammad only the first pair.
3
State the positions for case 2
In case 2, Abu Yusuf alone says qada of four rak'ahs. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (tarafayn) say qada of two rak'ahs (the last pair).
Abu Yusuf's reasoning is that the deficiency in the last pair affects the first pair as well because the two pairs are connected by the overall intention of four rak'ahs.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The disagreement is based on whether missing a wajib (recitation) in one rak'ah of a pair invalidates the tahrima of only that pair or of the entire four-rak'ah unit. Muhammad holds that the deficiency is limited to the pair where the omission occurred.
The hadith: 'لا صلاة إلا بقراءة' is interpreted to mean recitation is required in every rak'ah, but the effect on tahrima is disputed.
5
Apply to real practice
The mufta bihi (operative view) in the later school leans towards Muhammad's two-rak'ah qada in both cases, as it aligns with the principle that each pair is an independent unit.
This ruling applies to any four-rak'ah nafal (e.g., chasht, tahajjud) where recitation is omitted in one rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قرأ في احدى الأوليين لا غير قضى اربعا عندهما و عند محمد قضى ركعتين ولو قرا في احد الاخريين لا غير قضى اربعا عند ابی یوسف و عندهما ركعتين قال و تفسير قوله عليه السلام لا يصلى و يصلى الـ صلواة مثلها یعنی ركعتين بقرأة و ركعتين بغير قرأة فيكون بيان فرضية القرأة في ركعات النفل كلها
If he recited in one of the first two only, he should perform qada of four according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Muhammad he should perform qada of two rak'ahs. If he recited in one of the last two only, he should perform qada of four according to Abu Yusuf, and according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) he should perform qada of two rak'ahs. He (Muhammad) said: The interpretation of his saying (peace be upon him) 'Do not pray and pray the prayer like it' means two rak'ahs with recitation and two rak'ahs without recitation. Thus it is a statement of the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs of nafal.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage addresses two cases where recitation is performed in only one rak'ah of the prayer, either in the first pair or the last pair. For the first case (one rak'ah of the first two), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rule qada of four rak'ahs because the missing recitation in all other rak'ahs invalidates the tahrima of both pairs? Actually, the reasoning is that the first pair is deficient because only one rak'ah had recitation, so the tahrima is broken, and the second pair's start is invalid; thus all four need qada. Muhammad says only the first pair (two rak'ahs) need qada because the tahrima is broken only after the first deficiency, and the second pair never properly began. For the second case (one rak'ah of the last two), Abu Yusuf alone says qada of four, while Abu Hanifa and Muhammad agree on qada of two. The hadith quoted by Muhammad (interpreted) shows that the Prophet's statement 'Do not pray and pray the prayer like it' refers to two rak'ahs with recitation and two without, meaning recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah of nafal. This supports the view that missing recitation in any rak'ah requires compensation.

Key Terms
شیخین (shaykhayn): Refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf together; in this passage, they hold the same view on the first case.
طرفین (tarafayn): The two sides; in this passage, it refers to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad in the second case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Muhammad (Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani), if a person prays four rak'ahs of nafal (two pairs) and recites only in one rak'ah of the first pair, how many rak'ahs of qada are required?
A) Four rak'ahs
B) Two rak'ahs (the first pair)
C) Two rak'ahs (the last pair)
D) No qada required

Key Takeaway
In nafal prayer of four rak'ahs, missing recitation in one rak'ah of a pair requires qada of that pair only, per the preferred Hanafi view (Muhammad).

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Qada for Omitted Recitation in Four-Rak'ah Nafl Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for omitted recitation in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the intra-Hanafi positions on qada when recitation is missed in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer and apply the correct number of rak'ahs based on the scenario.

Core Idea
Missing recitation in nafl: the number of rak'ahs to repeat depends on which pair and which imam's principle.

In this lesson, we delve into a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute about qada when recitation is omitted in some rak'ahs of a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. The three eponymous imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad—differ on whether omission in one rak'ah invalidates the tahrimah, leading to different numbers of rak'ahs requiring qada. This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies the scenarios and the reasoning behind each view, including a reliance on the hadith 'la yusalla ba'da salatin mithliha'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two scenarios: recitation omitted in the first pair (shaf' awwal) vs. the last pair (shaf' thani).
In scenario 1, recitation is done in only one of the first two rak'ahs. In scenario 2, recitation in only one of the last two.
2
State each imam's position
For each scenario, note the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on the number of rak'ahs requiring qada.
Use the two-by-two table from the passage.
3
Trace the underlying principle
Understand how each imam's view on whether omission in one rak'ah invalidates tahrimah leads to their qada ruling.
Abu Hanifa: only omission in both of first pair invalidates; Abu Yusuf: never invalidates; Muhammad: omission in even one of first pair invalidates.
4
Examine the hadith interpretation
Imam Muhammad interprets the hadith 'la yusalla ba'da salatin mithliha' to require recitation in all rak'ahs.
The hadith is used to support the obligation of recitation in every rak'ah of nafl.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is the number of rak'ahs to repeat: 2 or 4, depending on the scenario and which imam's view is followed.
This affects whether the second pair (shaf' thani) requires qada.

يصلى بعد صلوۃ مثلھا سے اس بات پر استدلال کیا ہے کہ نفل کی تمام رکعات میں قرآت فرض ہے۔ حضرت امام محمد نے کہا کہ حدیث کی مراد یہ ہے کہ فرض کے مثل ایسی چار رکعات اس ے بعد نہ پڑھے کہ دو بقرات ہوں اور دو بغیر قرآت ہوں ، تا کہ فرض کے مثل ہو جائے بلکہ چاروں رکعت قرآت کے ساتھ ہوں ۔ پس اس حدیث سے نقل کی تمام رکعات میں فرضیت قرآت کا ثبوت ہو گیا۔
Chapter of Nafl Prayers. Recitation causes invalidation of tahrima. When tahrima becomes invalid, starting the second pair (shaf' thani) is not valid, and if it is not valid, its qada is not obligatory. Only qada of the first pair is obligatory. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, because recitation in one rak'ah does not invalidate tahrima, for him starting the second pair is valid. And when starting the second pair is valid, since recitation was omitted in one rak'ah of both pairs, qada of both pairs, i.e., four rak'ahs, is obligatory. And [the text mentions] 'wa qad ankara Abu Yusuf hadhihi al-riwayah' etc. From this, the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa is transmitted via Imam Abu Yusuf: that even in four rak'ahs, omitting [recitation] is wajib. But Imam Muhammad, after completing al-Jami' al-Saghir, when he presented it to Imam Abu Yusuf, Imam Abu Yusuf said: 'I did not relate this from Imam [Abu Hanifa] in your presence; rather, I related to you from Abu Hanifa that qada of two rak'ahs is obligatory.' Imam Muhammad said: 'That is not correct; rather you related to me that Imam said that starting the second pair is not valid, so qada of four rak'ahs is obligatory.' Imam Muhammad relied on his memory and did not retract despite Abu Yusuf's denial. The commentator (khādim) opines that Imam Muhammad's view is correct, because previously the principle of Imam Abu Hanifa was stated that omitting recitation in both rak'ahs of the first pair invalidates tahrima, but omitting in one rak'ah does not. In the mentioned case, he recited in one of the first and one of the last, omitted in one each. Since omitting in one rak'ah of the first does not invalidate tahrima, starting the second pair is valid, and since he omitted in one rak'ah of both pairs, qada of four rak'ahs is obligatory. 'Wallahu A'lam jameel.' How many rak'ahs of qada are required when he did not recite except in the first rak'ah? Statements of the jurists: 'And if he recited in one of the first two only, he performs qada of four according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and according to Muhammad, qada of two. And if he recited in one of the last two only, he performs qada of four according to Abu Yusuf, and according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), qada of two.' He said: 'The interpretation of his statement (peace be upon him) 'la yusalla ba'da salatin mithliha' is that he should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two without recitation, thus it becomes a statement of the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs of nafl.' Translation: And if he recited in only one of the first two rak'ahs, then according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) he performs qada of four, and according to Imam Muhammad qada of two. And if he recited in one of the last two, then according to Abu Yusuf qada of four, and according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) qada of two. Imam Muhammad said: The interpretation of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) statement 'la yusalla ba'da salatin mithliha' is that he should not pray two rak'ahs with recitation and two without recitation. So this hadith indicates the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs of nafl. Explanation of the issue: If he recited in one of the first two rak'ahs and omitted in the rest, then according to the two shaykhs qada of four, and according to Imam Muhammad qada of two. Second issue: If he recited in one of the last two and omitted in the others, then according to Imam Abu Yusuf qada of four, and according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad qada of two. Explanation: In the first issue, the proof of the two shaykhs is that in their view the tahrima remains. For Imam Abu Hanifa, because omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first pair does not invalidate tahrima. As for Imam Abu Yusuf, in his view tahrima never invalidates. So when tahrima is not invalidated, starting the second pair is valid. But since recitation was omitted in one rak'ah of the first pair and in both of the second? (text unclear), qada of four is obligatory. According to Imam Muhammad, since omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first invalidates tahrima, starting the second pair is not valid, so only qada of the first pair is obligatory. In the second issue, Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that in his view tahrima never invalidates. So when tahrima is not invalidated, starting the second pair is valid. But since he omitted recitation in both of the first and one of the last, qada of both pairs, i.e., four, is obligatory. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), since omitting recitation in both rak'ahs of the first invalidates tahrima, starting the second pair is not valid, so only qada of the first pair is obligatory. The author of Badai' indicated this issue with eight aspects, and the commentator (khadim) has summarized them. Now the author of Hidayah has adduced Imam Muhammad's statement and interpretation of the hadith 'la yusalla ba'da salatin mithliha' as evidence that recitation is obligatory in all rak'ahs of nafl. Imam Muhammad said: The meaning of the hadith is that one should not pray after a fard prayer four rak'ahs like it, with two with recitation and two without, so that it becomes like the fard; rather all four should be with recitation. Thus this hadith proves the obligation of recitation in all rak'ahs of nafl.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the qada (makeup) of missed recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl prayer. The problem arises when a person omits recitation in some rak'ahs. The core difference is whether omitting recitation in a single rak'ah invalidates the tahrima (prohibition of speaking/breaking the prayer) or not. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that omitting recitation in both rak'ahs of the first pair (shaf' awwal) invalidates tahrima, but omitting in only one does not. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that tahrima is never invalidated by missing recitation. Imam Muhammad holds that omitting recitation in even one rak'ah of the first pair invalidates tahrima. The practical effect is on the number of rak'ahs requiring qada. The passage narrates a historical disagreement between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding what was heard from Imam Abu Hanifa. The commentator (khadim) sides with Imam Muhammad. Then the text presents two scenarios: (1) recitation only in one of the first two rak'ahs: according to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) qada of four rak'ahs, according to Muhammad qada of two. (2) recitation only in one of the last two: according to Abu Yusuf qada of four, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) qada of two. The passage then explains the reasoning: for scenario 1, the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa through his principle, Abu Yusuf absolutely) preserve the tahrima, so the second pair is validly started, but since recitation was omitted in one rak'ah of each pair, qada of all four is wajib. For Muhammad, tahrima is invalidated by omission in the first pair, so only the first pair needs qada. For scenario 2, Abu Yusuf preserves tahrima, so both pairs valid; the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that omission in both first rak'ahs invalidates tahrima, so only first pair requires qada. Finally, Imam Muhammad's interpretation of the hadith 'la yusalla ba'da salatin mithliha' is cited: it means one should not pray four rak'ahs like the fard with two with recitation and two without; rather all should have recitation. This supports the view that recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah of nafl. The passage underscores the importance of recitation in nafl and the Hanafi position that missing it obligates sajdah sahw or, if multiple omissions, may affect validity.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening takbir that makes the prayer sacred, prohibiting worldly acts. Its invalidation means the prayer is no longer valid.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ahs. In four-rak'ah nafl, there are two shaf': shaf' awwal (first two) and shaf' thani (last two).
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed obligatory or wajib element of the prayer after the prayer is completed. Here, it refers to repeating the entire prayer or specific rak'ahs due to omission of recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person prays a four-rak'ah nafl and recites only in the first rak'ah, according to Imam Muhammad, how many rak'ahs of qada are required?
A) Two rak'ahs
B) Four rak'ahs
C) One rak'ah
D) No qada required

Key Takeaway
The number of rak'ahs to repeat after omitting recitation in a four-rak'ah nafl depends on which rak'ah(s) were omitted and which Hanafi imam's position is followed.

Sitting in Nafl Prayer: Permissibility and Posture
Establishing the permissibility and method of sitting in nafl prayer when able to stand.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting in nafl prayer, cite the primary evidence, and distinguish the conditions from those of fard prayer.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer sitting is permissible and valid, but reward is halved.

This lesson examines a specific leniency in nafl (supererogatory) prayers: the option to pray sitting even when one is perfectly able to stand. We will analyse the hadith evidence, the rationale behind the ruling, and the correct sitting posture according to the Hanafi school. The distinction from fard prayer is also highlighted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act is performing a nafl prayer while sitting, despite physical ability to stand. The hukm in the Hanafi school is permissible (mubah) but with reduced reward.
This applies only to nafl prayers, not to fard or wajib prayers.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The key evidence is the hadith: 'The prayer of the one sitting is half the prayer of the one standing.' This is a hadith ahad, thus zanni al-thubut. Analyse how the phrase indicates permissibility.
The phrase 'صلوة القاعد على النصف من صلوة القائم' is cited.
3
Understand the wisdom (hikmah) behind the ruling
The text mentions that prayer is a good action, and standing may become burdensome. The permission preserves continuity in worship — avoiding complete abandonment.
This rationale is specific to nafl; fard requires standing as a rukn.
4
Examine the difference on sitting posture
Scholars differed on the proper sitting form. The relied-upon (mukhtar) Hanafi view is to sit as in tashahhud (muftarishan), because that is the established sunnah posture in prayer.
Other postures may be permissible but less reward.
5
Distinguish from fard prayer
In fard prayers, standing (qiyam) is a rukn; omitting it without excuse invalidates the prayer. In nafl, standing is not a pillar, so sitting is valid. This distinction is crucial.
The ruling does not apply to fard or wajib prayers.

Source Text

Ruling on praying nafl sitting down despite ability to stand: One may pray the nafl prayer sitting down despite ability to stand because of his statement (peace be upon him): 'The prayer of the one sitting is half the prayer of the one standing.' And because the prayer is a good action, and sometimes standing may be difficult for him, so he is allowed to omit it so that he is not cut off from it. They differed about the manner of sitting. The chosen method is that he sits as he sits in the state of tashahhud, because that is the established practice in prayer. Translation: And despite ability to stand, he may pray nafl sitting because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Praying sitting is half the degree of praying standing.' And because prayer is a good action, and sometimes standing becomes difficult for him, so omitting qiyam is permissible for him, so that this good action is not cut off from him. The scholars differed about the manner of sitting. The chosen view is that he sits as he sits in the state of tashahhud, because this is what is legislated and known in prayer. A sub-issue: For one able to stand, sitting in nafl is permissible. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The prayer of the one sitting is half.'

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the permissibility of praying nafl prayers while sitting, even if one is physically able to stand. The primary evidence is the hadith: 'The prayer of the one sitting is half the prayer of the one standing.' This indicates that sitting reduces the reward by half, but it remains valid and permissible. The rationale given is that prayer is a 'good action' (khair mawdu'), and to prevent a person from abandoning it entirely due to occasional difficulty of standing, Islam allows sitting. This shows leniency to encourage consistency in worship. The passage then addresses a difference of opinion regarding the proper sitting posture. The relied-upon (mukhtar) position is to sit as in tashahhud, i.e., sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright, because that is the established sunnah posture in prayer. The passage concludes that for someone able to stand, sitting in nafl prayer is permissible, and the proof is the hadith mentioned. This ruling is specific to nafl prayers; for fard prayers, sitting without excuse is not valid if able to stand. The passage does not discuss fard. The Hanafi position is clear: nafl can be offered sitting even with ability to stand, but the reward is reduced.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary, supererogatory prayers beyond the obligatory (fard) and confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah). They are highly recommended but not required.
قاعد (qa'id): Sitting posture in prayer. The text specifies sitting as in tashahhud (muftarishan).
تشهد (tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in the second and final rak'ah. The posture associated with it is the model for sitting in nafl.

B) Half the reward
C) No reward
D) Double the reward

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, nafl prayer can be performed sitting even if able to stand; the reward is halved but the prayer is valid.

Qada for Missed Recitation in Nafil: Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for missed qira'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on qada for missed recitation in nafl prayer and state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad regarding nullification of tahrimah and the number of rak'ats requiring compensation.

Core Idea
Omission of recitation in a single rak'ah of nafl may nullify tahrimah, affecting validity of subsequent rak'ats.

The Hanafi school recognizes a subtle but impactful dispute among its founding imams regarding the effect of missing recitation (qira'ah) in optional (nafl) prayers. This lesson unpacks the disagreement, focusing on whether the omission nullifies the tahrimah (opening sanctity) and how that determines the number of rak'ats that must be compensated (qada). By understanding each imam's reasoning, you will learn to apply the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa)
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling in both scenarios: He holds that omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first shaf' does not nullify tahrimah, so the second shaf' is valid, but qada of all four rak'ats is wajib. However, if recitation is omitted in both rak'ats of the first shaf', tahrimah is nullified, making the second shaf' invalid and only the first shaf' requires qada.
Abu Hanifa differentiates based on the number of rak'ats where recitation is missed within the first shaf'.
2
Identify the opposing views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad
Abu Yusuf holds that tahrimah is never nullified by omission of recitation in any nafl rak'ah, so the second shaf' is always valid, and qada of all four rak'ats is wajib whenever recitation is missed. Muhammad holds that omitting recitation in even one rak'ah nullifies tahrimah, so the second shaf' is invalid and only the first shaf' requires qada.
These positions are based on different views of the role of recitation in nafl.
3
Analyze the response: Muhammad's hadith proof
Muhammad cites the hadith 'لا يصلى بعد صلاة مثلها' (Do not pray after a prayer like it) to support that all rak'ats of nafl must include recitation. He interprets 'مثلها' as four rak'ats where two have recitation and two do not, resembling the fard prayer where each rak'ah has recitation. Thus, the hadith prohibits such a prayer and implies that recitation is fard in every nafl rak'ah.
This interpretation strengthens Muhammad's position that omission in any single rak'ah nullifies tahrimah.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence is the number of rak'ats for which qada is wajib. Under Abu Hanifa's first scenario: all four rak'ats; under his second scenario: only the first shaf'. Under Abu Yusuf: always all four. Under Muhammad: only the first shaf' (since the second is invalid).
This difference impacts the worshiper's obligation to make up missed rak'ats.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The passage indicates that Imam Muhammad's position is supported by his hadith interpretation. Later Hanafi authorities often follow Muhammad's view as it harmonizes with the principle that recitation is fard in every rak'ah of nafl. However, some may follow Abu Hanifa's nuanced differentiation.
For fatwa, the mufta bihi may vary; consult reliable later texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
پہل مسئلہ میں شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں بزرگوں کے نزدیک تحریمہ باقی ہے امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ اولین کی ایک رکعت میں ترک قرآت ان کے نزدیک تحریمہ باطل نہیں کرتا اور رہے امام ابو یوسف تو ان کے نزدیک کسی صورت میں بھی تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوتا بہر حال جب ان دونوں کے نزدیک تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا تو شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا صحیح ہوا مگر چونکہ شفع اول کی ایک رکعت میں اضع پانی کی دونوں میں قرآت ترک کر دی گئی اس لئے چاروں کی قضاء واجب ہوگی اور امام محمد کے نزدیک چونکہ اول کی ایک رکعت م ابھی ترک قرآت تحریمہ کو باطل کر دیتا ہے اس لئے ان کے نزدیک شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا صحیح نہیں ہوگا اور جب شلع ثانی کا شروع کرنا ن نہ ہو تواس کی قضاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی البتہ یشفع اول کی ایک رکعت میں ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے اس کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔ وسرے مسئلہ میں امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک تحریمہ مطلقا باطل نہیں ہوتا پس جب تحریمہ باطل نہیں ہوا تو شفع انی کا شروع کرنا بھی صحیح ہو گیا مگر چونکہ اس نے اولین کی دونوں میں اور اخرین کی ایک رکعت میں قرآت نہیں کی اس لئے دونوں شفعوں تین چاروں کی قضاء واجب ہو گی ۔ طرفین کے نزدیک چونکہ اولین کی دونوں رکعتوں میں ترک قرآت سے تحریمہ باطل ہو جاتا ہے اس کے ضلع پانی کا شروع کرنا صحیح نہ ہوا اور جب شفع ثانی کا شروع کرنا صحیح نہ ہوا تو اس کی قضاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی البتہ شفع اول کی دونوں امنوں میں ترک قرآت کی وجہ سے شفع اول کی قضاء واجب ہوگی۔
صاحب بدايه ني هذه المسئلة على ثمانية اوجه کہہ کر جن آٹھ مسائل کی طرف اشارہ کیا تھا اور خادم نے بالا جمال ان کا کر کیا تھا ان کی توضیح و تشریح مع الدلائل ذکر کر دی گئی۔ اب صاحب ہدایہ نے امام محمد کے قول و تفسیر قوله عليه السلام ال يصلى بعد صلوۃ مثلھا سے اس بات پر استدلال کی ہے کہ نفل کی تمام رکعات میں قرآت فرض ہے۔ حضرت امام محمد نے کہا کہ حدیث کی مراد یہ ہے کہ فرض کے مثل ایسی چار رکعات اس ے بعد نہ پڑھے کہ دو بقرات ہوں اور دو بغیر قرآت ہوں ، تا کہ فرض کے مثل ہو جائے بلکہ چاروں رکعت قرآت کے ساتھ ہوں ۔ پس اس حدیث سے نقل کی تمام رکعات میں فرضیت قرآت کا ثبوت ہو گیا۔
In the first issue, the proof of the two Shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that according to both of them the tahrimah remains. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, because in the first rak'ah omitting recitation does not nullify the tahrimah in his view. And as for Imam Abu Yusuf, in his view the tahrimah is never nullified in any case. In any case, when according to both of them the tahrimah is not nullified, then starting the second shaf' was valid. But since in one rak'ah of the first shaf' recitation was omitted in both [rak'ats], therefore qada of all four is wajib. And according to Imam Muhammad, since omitting recitation in the first rak'ah nullifies the tahrimah, therefore in his view starting the second shaf' is not valid. And when starting the second shaf' is not valid, then its qada is also not wajib. However, due to omitting recitation in one rak'ah of the first shaf', its qada is wajib. In the second issue, the proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that in his view the tahrimah is absolutely not nullified. So when the tahrimah is not nullified, starting the second shaf' also became valid. But since he did not recite in the two [rak'ats] of the first [shaf'] and in one rak'ah of the last [shaf'], therefore qada of both shaf's, i.e., all four, is wajib. According to the two [Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad], since omitting recitation in both rak'ats of the first [shaf'] nullifies the tahrimah, starting the second shaf' was not valid. And when starting the second shaf' is not valid, its qada is also not wajib. However, due to omitting recitation in both rak'ats of the first shaf', qada of the first shaf' is wajib.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the qada (compensation) for missed recitation in optional (nafl) prayers when the tahrimah (opening sanctity) is nullified. The discussion revolves around two specific scenarios. In the first scenario, the worshiper omitted recitation in one rak'ah of the first shaf' (pair of rak'ats). The two Shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the tahrimah is not nullified (Abu Yusuf says it is never nullified; Abu Hanifa's position is that omitting recitation in one rak'ah does not nullify it). Therefore, starting the second shaf' is valid, but since recitation was missed in one rak'ah of the first shaf', qada is wajib for all four rak'ats. Imam Muhammad, however, holds that omitting recitation in one rak'ah nullifies the tahrimah, so starting the second shaf' is invalid, and only the first shaf' requires qada. In the second scenario, the worshiper omitted recitation in both rak'ats of the first shaf' and one rak'ah of the second shaf'. Abu Yusuf again says the tahrimah is not nullified, so both shaf's are valid but qada is wajib for all four rak'ats. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) say the tahrimah is nullified, so the second shaf' is invalid and only the first shaf' requires qada.

Key Terms
تحریمہ (tahrimah): The opening sanctity of prayer that renders the prayer valid and prohibits nullifying actions.
شفع (shaf'): A pair of rak'ats in prayer, typically referring to two-rak'ah units in nafl.
قضاء (qada): Compensatory prayer performed to make up for an obligation that was missed or performed defectively.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a nuanced intra-madhhab dispute on whether omitting recitation in a single nafl rak'ah nullifies the tahrimah and how many rak'ats require qada, with Imam Muhammad's hadith-based position often carrying weight.

Sitting in Nafil Prayer Despite Ability to Stand
Ruling with proof on sitting in nafl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting in nafl prayer without excuse, cite the textual and rational proofs, and identify the preferred sitting posture according to Al-Hidayah.

Core Idea
Sitting in nafl prayer is permissible because it is a good act that should not be discouraged by requiring standing.

This lesson clarifies that in the Hanafi school, one may perform voluntary (nafl) prayer while sitting even if physically capable of standing. The evidence includes a hadith indicating reward is halved for sitting, and a rational principle that nafl is an easily accessible good (khairun mauḍū'). The passage also addresses the proper sitting posture, noting an intra-madhhab difference resolved in favor of the tashahhud sitting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Determine the legal status of sitting in nafl for one able to stand. The passage states it is permissible (ja'iz), not obligatory to stand.
The ruling applies to nafl (sunna or nafila) prayers, not fard.
2
Analyze the hadith proof
Examine the hadith: 'The prayer of the sitting person is half the prayer of the standing person.' Understand the author's inference that this permission applies to nafl even without excuse, because with excuse the reward would be equal.
The hadith is ahad with zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Understand the rational proof
The concept of 'khairun mauḍū'' means prayer is an accessible good. Imposing standing as a condition could deter people from praying altogether, so it is not required.
This rational proof (istidlal) complements the textual evidence.
4
Determine the preferred posture
Review the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on how to sit: Abu Hanifa (any way), Abu Yusuf (ihtiba'), Muhammad (on knees), Zufar (tashahhud). The author selects tashahhud as the preferred mufta bihi position because it is the legislated posture in prayer.
The fatwa is upon sitting as in tashahhud.

Ruling on performing nafil prayer sitting despite ability to stand: He may perform nafil prayer sitting even if able to stand, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The prayer of the sitting person is half the prayer of the standing person.' And because prayer is a good act that has been placed (as an easy good), and sometimes standing may be difficult for him, so he is allowed to leave it so that he does not become cut off from it. And they (scholars) differed regarding the manner of sitting. The chosen view is that he should sit as he sits in the state of tashahhud, because that is what has been legislated and known in prayer. Commentary: Detailed issue: It is permissible for one able to stand to pray nafl sitting. The proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The prayer of the sitting person is half the prayer of the standing person.' Meaning, compared to praying standing, sitting prayer has half the reward. The deduction from this hadith is that the Prophet's intent is either to pray sitting due to an excuse or without an excuse. The first (with excuse) cannot be, because with an excuse, sitting and standing are equal in reward. So it is determined that it means sitting without excuse. As for whether the hadith is intended like this or not, we say: It is not intended for fard prayer by consensus, because without excuse sitting in fard prayer is not permissible. So it is established that one can pray nafl sitting without excuse, but the reward is half compared to standing. The rational proof is that nafl prayer is 'khairun mauḍū' (a good act placed easily), meaning this good has been made readily available for the servant in all times. It is narrated from Abu Dharr that the Prophet said: 'Prayer is a good act placed; whoever wishes may take little and whoever wishes may take much.' The established conclusion is that nafl prayer is not obligatory. And for something that is like this, no condition should be imposed that causes leaving it, because that which causes leaving good cannot be good. Requiring standing could cause leaving nafl because sometimes standing is difficult for him. So if standing were made a condition for nafl prayer, sometimes due to the difficulty of standing, he might leave the nafl entirely, whereas nafl is a good act available at all times. Therefore standing is not made a condition for nafl prayer. The author of Hidayah said that scholars differed regarding the manner of sitting for nafl. Imam Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa that one may sit in whatever manner he wishes, because when leaving standing itself is permissible, the manner is even more permissible. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that he should sit in ihtiba (sitting on the buttocks with knees raised and hands wrapped), because the Prophet in his later life used to pray in ihtiba. From Muhammad it is narrated that he should sit with knees folded. Imam Zufar said he should sit in the tashahhud posture. The author (al-Marghinani) considers this the preferred position, and the fatwa is upon it because this manner is legislated and known.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on sitting in nafl prayer. It establishes the permissibility based on the hadith that sitting prayer has half the reward of standing. The author clarifies that this applies even without excuse, because with excuse the reward would be equal. A rational proof follows: nafl is a good act (khairun mauḍū') intended to be easily accessible; imposing standing as a condition could cause people to abandon it altogether. The passage then discusses the preferred posture: the chosen view is to sit as in tashahhud, which is the legislated manner, though other valid views exist.

Key Terms
خیر موضوع (khairun mauḍū'): A good act that has been placed easily and accessibly for believers to perform at any time.
احتباء (ihtiba'): A sitting posture with knees raised and arms wrapped around them, resting on the buttocks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sitting on knees
C) Any way one wishes
D) Sitting as in tashahhud

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, sitting in nafl prayer without excuse is permissible with half reward; the preferred posture is sitting as in tashahhud.

Starting Nafl Standing Then Sitting Without Excuse: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of sitting after starting nafl standing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of sitting without excuse after starting nafl prayer standing, and apply the concepts of istihsan and qiyas.

Core Idea
Starting nafl standing does not make standing obligatory unless explicitly vowed — istihsan allows sitting, but qiyas to nadhr requires completion.

This passage presents a key intra-Hanafi disagreement: if a person begins a voluntary (nafl) prayer in the standing position, then sits down without any valid excuse, is the prayer valid? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, based on juristic preference (istihsan), while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, say no, based on analogy (qiyas) to a vow (nadhr). Understanding this dispute reveals how different legal methods — istihsan and qiyas — can lead to divergent rulings within the same school.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the dispute
Identify the specific act: someone starts a nafl prayer standing, then sits without excuse. What are the two positions?
Abu Hanifa: permissible; Sahibayn: invalid.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's dalil
They use qiyas: starting an act standing is analogous to making a vow (nadhr) to pray standing. In a vow, the condition becomes obligatory. So here, standing becomes obligatory and sitting invalidates.
This is strict analogy based on the similarity of 'commencement' (shuru').
3
Identify Abu Hanifa's dalil and method
He uses istihsan (juristic preference) to depart from strict analogy. His reasoning: the worshiper did not explicitly stipulate standing (unlike a vow), and the part performed while standing was valid. Sitting does not invalidate the entire prayer.
Istihsan overrides qiyas because of the difference in explicit stipulation.
4
Analyze the response to the opposing proof
Abu Hanifa distinguishes between a vow (where standing is explicitly made obligatory) and starting a nafl (where it is not). The text notes that even in vows, some mashayikh hold standing is not obligatory if not specified.
This weakens the analogy's foundation.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
The practical consequence: Under Abu Hanifa, the nafl prayer is valid; under Sahibayn, it is invalid and must be repeated if one sits without excuse.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice tends to follow Abu Hanifa's istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و ان افتتحها قائما ثم قعد من غير عذر جاز عد ابي حنيفة و هذا استحسان و عندهما لا يجزيه را جا لان الشروع معتبر بالنذر له انه لم يباشر القيام فيما بقى ولما باشر صحة بدونه بخلاف النذرلان نصا حتى لو لم ينص على القيام لا يلزمه القيام عند بعض المشائخ اس سے ترجمہ اور اگر نفل کو کھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا پھر بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور یہ استحسان ہے ہیں ۔ او کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے اور یہی قیاس ہے کیونکہ شروع کرنا نذر پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ متحفل نے نیا گا نا شرہ نہیں کیا اور (جس میں قیام ) کیا وہ بغیر قیام کے صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف نذر کے کیونکہ اس نے صراحت قیام کو لازم کر لیاحتی کہ اگر ہا ہے کہ نہ نہ کی ہوتی تو بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک اسپر قیام لازم نہ ہوتا ۔ تشریح
And if he starts it (nafl) standing, then sits without an excuse, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and this is istihsan. But according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not valid for him, and this is qiyas, because commencement is considered analogous to a vow. His (Abu Hanifa's) proof is that he (the one who sat) did not perform standing in the remaining part, and he did perform what is valid without standing. Contrary to a vow, because he explicitly made standing obligatory. So much so that if he did not specify standing, some mashayikh say standing is not obligatory upon him. Commentary: Translation: And if he starts nafl standing then sits without excuse, it is permissible according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and this is istihsan. According to them (the Sahibayn) it is invalid, and this is qiyas because commencement is analogized to a vow. Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the worshiper did not explicitly stipulate standing, and what he performed (the standing part) is valid without (continued) standing. Unlike a vow, because there he explicitly obligated standing. So much so that if he had not specified standing, according to some mashayikh standing would not be obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where a person begins a nafl prayer standing and then sits down without any valid excuse. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that this is permissible (ja'iz) based on istihsan (juristic preference). His reasoning is that since the worshiper did not explicitly vow to stand, and the part performed standing was valid, there is no harm in sitting. In contrast, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is invalid (not permissible) based on qiyas (analogy) to a vow (nadhr): just as one who vows to pray standing must stand, so too starting a nafl standing creates an obligation to complete it standing. Abu Hanifa responds that in a vow, the obligation of standing is explicit, whereas in nafl prayer it is not explicitly stipulated. The text notes that even some mashayikh hold that in a vow, if standing is not specified, it is not required.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict analogy (qiyas) in favor of a more suitable ruling.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship with specific conditions, making those conditions obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis of the Sahibayn's ruling that sitting after starting nafl standing is invalid?
A) Because the hadith prohibits sitting in nafl
B) Because commencement is analogous to a vow, making standing obligatory
C) Because sitting invalidates the tahrimah
D) Because nafl must be performed entirely standing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, starting a nafl prayer standing does not obligate standing throughout unless explicitly vowed; istihsan permits sitting, while qiyas to nadhr would require standing.

Sitting in Nafl Prayer: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Beginning Standing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on beginning nafl standing then sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) on beginning a nafl prayer standing and then sitting without an excuse, and explain the role of istihsan and qiyas in the dispute.

Core Idea
Beginning a nafl prayer standing does not obligate standing for the entire prayer; Abu Hanifa permits sitting based on istihsan.

In Hanafi fiqh, voluntary (nafl) prayer is a greatly encouraged act of worship, but its rules are more flexible than obligatory prayers. A well-known hadith states that sitting in nafl prayer yields half the reward of standing, but does this mean one must always stand if able? A specific scenario arises when a person begins a nafl prayer standing and then, without any excuse, decides to sit. The Hanafi school has an internal difference on this very point, and understanding it reveals the interaction between two important proofs: istihsan (juristic preference) and qiyas (analogy).

Guided Path
1
Recognize the general rule on sitting in nafl prayer
First, understand that sitting in nafl prayer without an excuse is generally permissible but reduces the reward by half compared to standing. This is derived from the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) and rational evidence that standing should not be made a condition that discourages prayer.
2
Identify the specific disputed scenario
Focus on the case: a person begins a nafl prayer standing, then sits down without any excuse (e.g., no illness or difficulty). The question is whether the prayer remains valid or becomes invalid.
The scenario is distinct from one who begins sitting from the start, which is unanimously permissible.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa rules that the prayer is valid (ja'iz) based on istihsan. His reasoning: beginning the prayer standing does not obligate standing for the entire prayer; the first rak'ah was valid standing, and its validity does not depend on the second rak'ah being standing. In contrast to a vow (nazr), where standing is explicitly obligated, here the intention is general.
The key difference is the lack of explicit specification of standing in the intention.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and their proof
The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the prayer is invalid (la yujzi'uhu) based on qiyas (analogy) to a vow. They analogize: just as one who vows to pray standing must stand, similarly, beginning a prayer standing implies an obligation to continue standing for the entire prayer.
Their analogy treats the commencement of prayer as implicitly binding the same conditions as a vow.
5
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf and the tarjih
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is critical: according to Abu Hanifa, the prayer is valid with reduced reward; according to Sahibayn, the prayer must be repeated. The author of Al-Hidayah and Ashraf al-Hadaya side with Abu Hanifa, giving precedence to istihsan over qiyas in this context. The fatwa is thus on Abu Hanifa's view.
This is a classic example of istihsan overriding qiyas when strict analogy would lead to hardship or contradict the spirit of encouraging voluntary worship.

Source Text

کر پڑھ سکتا ہے البتہ کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے کی بہ نسبت ثواب آدھا ہے دلیل عقلی یہ ہے کہ نفل نماز خیر موضوع ہے یعنی بندے کے لئے یہ نیکی اس طرح مہیا کر دی گئی کہ جمیع اوقات میں حاصل کر سکے حضرت ابوذر سے روایت چیز اس انداز پر ہو اس میں اس طرح کی کوئی شرط نہیں لگائی جاتی جو اس کے ترک کا سبب ہو کیونکہ جو ترک خیر کا سبب ہو گا وہ خیر نہیں ہوسکتا اور قیام کی شرط لگانا نفل کو چھوڑنے کا سبب ہو سکتا ہے اس لئے کہ بسا اوقات قیام شاق ہوتا ہے پس اگر قیام کو نفل نماز کے لئے شرط قرار دے دیا جائے تو بسا اوقات قیام کے شاق ہونے کی بنا پر نفل ہی کا ترک کر دیا جائے گا۔ حالانکہ نفل خیر موضوع ہے یعنی جمیع اوقات میں حاصل کرنے کی نیکی ہے اس لئے نفل نماز کے لئے قیام کی شرط نہیں لگائی گئی۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ علماء نے بیٹھنے کی کیفیت میں اختلاف کیا ہے۔ چنانچہ امام محمد نے امام ابوحنیفہ سے روایت کیا کہ نفل پڑھنے والا جس طرح چاہے بیٹھ کر نفل نماز پڑھے کیونکہ جب اس کے لئے اصل قیام کا چھوڑ دینا جائز ہے تو صفت قعود کیسے جائز نہ ہوگی۔ امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ جبوءا بنا کر بیٹھے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم آخری عمر میں بحالت احتباء نماز پڑھا کرتے تھے اور احتباء بیٹھنا یہ ہے کہ دونوں زانوں کھڑے رکھے اور سرین زمین پر ٹکا دے پھر دونوں ہاتھ باندھ لے۔ امام محمد سے مروی ہے کہ دونوں زانوں کو کھڑا کر کے بیٹھے۔ امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ تشہد کی کیفیت پر بیٹھے۔ مصنف کے نزدیک یہی پسندیدہ مذہب ہے۔ اس پر فتوی ہے کہ والیہی طریقہ مشروع ہو کر معلوم ہوا ہے ۔

و ان افتتحها قائما ثم قعد من غير عذر جاز عند ابي حنيفة و هذا استحسان و عندهما لا يجزيه را جا لان الشروع معتبر بالنذر له انه لم يباشر القيام فيما بقى ولما باشر صحة بدونه بخلاف النذرلان نصا حتى لو لم ينص على القيام لا يلزمه القيام عند بعض المشائخ
ترجمہ اور اگر نفل کو کھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا پھر بغیر عذر کے بیٹھ گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے اور یہ استحسان ہے ۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ناجائز ہے اور یہی قیاس ہے کیونکہ شروع کرنا نذر پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ متحفل نے شروع تو کیا لیکن شرہ نہیں کیا اور جس میں قیام کیا وہ بغیر قیام کے صحیح ہے۔ برخلاف نذر کے کیونکہ اس نے صراحت قیام کو لازم کر لیا حتی کہ اگر اس نے قیام کی صراحت نہ کی ہوتی تو بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک اس پر قیام لازم نہ ہوتا ۔

باب النوافل
مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے نفل نماز کھڑے ہو کر شروع کی پھر بلا عذر بیٹھ گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے حکم اول استحسانی ہے اور ثانی قیاسی ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل قیاس ہے یعنی نفل نماز شروع کرنا قیاس کیا گیا ہے نذر پر طور پر کہ اگر کسی نے کھڑے ہو کر نفل پڑھنے کی نذر کی تو اس کے لئے بیٹھ کر پڑھنا جائز نہ ہوگا اسی طرح اگر کھڑے ہو کر نفل نماز شروع کی تو بیٹھ کر پڑھنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ شروع کرنا اس چیز کو لازم کرتا ہے جس کو شروع کیا گیا ہے اور جس پر ما شرع ا بحت موقوف ہے تو نفل شروع کرنے سے رکعت اولی اور ثانیہ دونوں واجب ہوں گی ۔ رکعت اولی تو اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ اس کو شروع کیا گیا ہے اور رکعت ثانیہ اس لئے کہ اس پر رکعت اولی کی صحت موقوف ہے کیونکہ صلوة بتیر ا ممنوع ہے ۔ مگر مسئلہ مذکورہ میں رکعت اولی کھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا گیا ہے لیکن اس کی صحت اس پر موقوف نہیں کہ رکعت ثانیہ کو بھی کھڑے ہو کر پڑھا جائے۔ پس رکعت اولی کو کھڑے ہو کر شروع کرنے سے رکعت ثانیہ میں قیام لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف نذر ہے کیونکہ نذر کی صورت میں اس نے صراحتہ اپنے اوپر قیام لازم کر لیا ہے لہذا کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے سے نذر پوری ہوگی چنانچہ اگر کسی نے قیام کی صراحت نہیں کی، بلکہ یہ کہا کہ میں نفل نماز پڑھوں گا تو بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک اس پر قیام لازم نہیں ہے۔
Chapter of Voluntary Prayers. From the prayer of the standing person, meaning compared to standing, sitting has half the reward. This hadith is used as evidence that the Prophet's (peace be upon him) intent in the hadith is either to pray sitting due to an excuse or without excuse; the first cannot be because prayer with excuse and standing are equal in reward, so it is determined that it means sitting without excuse. As for whether the hadith means this or not, we say: obligatory prayer is not intended by consensus because without excuse, it is not permissible to pray obligatory prayer sitting. So it is determined that one can pray voluntary prayer sitting without excuse, but compared to standing, the reward is half. The rational evidence is that voluntary prayer is 'goodness placed' (khayr mawdu'), meaning that this goodness is made available for the servant to obtain at all times. It is narrated from Abu Dharr that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Prayer is a goodly gift; whoever wishes may take little, and whoever wishes may take much.' The conclusion is that voluntary prayer is not obligatory. And for something that is on this basis, no condition is placed that would cause it to be abandoned, because that which causes the abandonment of goodness cannot be good. And making standing a condition for voluntary prayer can cause its abandonment because sometimes standing is difficult. So if standing is made a condition for voluntary prayer, sometimes due to its difficulty one might abandon the voluntary prayer altogether, whereas it is a goodly gift. Therefore standing is not a condition for voluntary prayer. The author of Hidayah said that scholars differed regarding the manner of sitting. Imam Muhammad narrated from Abu Hanifa that one may sit in voluntary prayer however he wishes, because when it is permissible to abandon standing entirely, then the manner of sitting is even more permissible. From Abu Yusuf it is narrated that one should sit in ihtiba (sitting on the heels with knees upright and hands folded) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) in his later years prayed in ihtiba. And ihtiba is to keep both knees raised and rest the buttocks on the ground then fold the hands. From Imam Muhammad it is narrated that one should sit with both knees raised. Imam Zufar said one should sit in the manner of tashahhud. According to the author, this is the preferred opinion, and the fatwa is upon it, and this method is known to be prescribed.

And if he begins it standing and then sits without an excuse, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, and this is istihsan. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is not permissible, and that is qiyas, because beginning it is compared to a vow. Abu Hanifa's proof is that the one who began it did not specify (standing in his intention), and what he performed (the first rak'ah) was valid without standing (for the second). Unlike a vow, because he explicitly obligated himself to stand, such that if he did not specify standing, according to some scholars, standing would not be obligatory upon him.

Explanation: The issue is that if someone begins voluntary prayer standing and then sits without excuse, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and impermissible according to the two companions. The first ruling is based on istihsan, the second on qiyas. The two companions' proof is qiyas: beginning voluntary prayer is analogized to a vow, i.e., if someone vows to pray standing, it is not permissible to pray sitting. Likewise, if he begins standing, it is not permissible to pray sitting. Abu Hanifa's proof is that as has passed, beginning a thing obligates what is begun and what its validity depends on. Thus beginning voluntary prayer makes the first and second rak'ahs obligatory. The first rak'ah is obligatory because it was begun, and the second because the validity of the first depends on it, since separating the prayer (with a long gap) is prohibited. But in this issue, the first rak'ah was begun standing, but its validity does not depend on the second rak'ah also being prayed standing. So beginning the first rak'ah standing does not necessitate standing in the second rak'ah. In contrast, a vow is different because in a vow one explicitly obligates himself to stand, so the vow is fulfilled by praying standing. Thus if someone did not specify standing, but said 'I will pray a voluntary prayer,' according to some scholars, standing is not obligatory upon him.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition of the rulings on sitting in voluntary (nafl) prayer, based on the text of Al-Hidayah. The author begins by presenting the general ruling: voluntary prayer can be performed sitting even without an excuse, but the reward is half that of standing. This is derived from a hadith and supported by rational argument that making standing a condition could discourage the performance of voluntary prayers altogether. The author then discusses the preferred manner of sitting, noting differences among early Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa (via Muhammad) allowed any sitting posture, Abu Yusuf preferred ihtiba (the way the Prophet sat in later years), Muhammad preferred a specific posture with knees raised, and Zufar preferred the tashahhud sitting. The author favors Zufar's view and states it is the basis for fatwa. The second part addresses a specific scenario: if one begins voluntary prayer standing and then sits without excuse. Abu Hanifa permits it based on istihsan (juristic preference), reasoning that the intention at the outset did not explicitly obligate standing for the entire prayer, and the first rak'ah was valid without standing for the second. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it invalid by qiyas (analogy) to a vow, where explicit obligation to stand binds the person. The passage clarifies that the difference hinges on whether beginning the prayer creates an obligation equivalent to a vow. Abu Hanifa holds that it does not, because the intention is general. The explanation then elaborates that, according to Abu Hanifa, beginning standing obligates only the standing of the first rak'ah, not subsequent ones, since the validity of the first does not depend on the second being also standing. This is contrasted with a vow where the obligation is explicit. The discussion underscores the Hanafi principle of istihsan overriding qiyas in cases where strict analogy would lead to hardship or contradiction of the spirit of the law.

Key Terms
قیام (qiyam): Standing posture in prayer.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a stronger evidence or to avoid hardship.
نذر (nazr): A vow to perform an act of worship with specific conditions (e.g., standing).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if someone begins a nafl prayer standing and then sits without an excuse?
A) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
B) The prayer is valid but the reward is half of standing.
C) The prayer is valid with full reward because he started standing.
D) The prayer is valid only if he had an excuse.

Key Takeaway
Beginning a nafl prayer standing does not obligate standing for the entire prayer; per Abu Hanifa's istihsan, sitting without excuse is permissible but reduces reward by half.

Ruling on Praying Voluntary Prayers on a Mount Outside the City
Explains permissibility and conditions for performing nafl on a mount while traveling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city, identify the supporting hadith, and distinguish between the positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayers on a mount outside the city are permissible with gestures; obligatory prayers require full conditions.

When traveling outside the city, one may need to perform voluntary prayers while riding. The Hanafi school provides a concession allowing this with gestures, based on prophetic practice. However, the details—such as where this applies and whether all voluntary prayers are included—differ within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? It is performing voluntary (nafl/sunnah) prayer on a mount while outside the city. The ruling is permissibility (mubah) as a concession.
Obligatory prayers are excluded; they require full conditions.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed on a donkey while heading to Khaybar, making gestures. This is the primary proof.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning (dalala) is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit action of the Prophet shows that voluntary prayer on a mount is allowed without facing the qibla or making full movements. The rationale is that voluntary prayers are not time-bound and requiring dismount would cause hardship for the traveler.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa is reported to hold that one must dismount for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized. Abu Yusuf allows the concession even inside the city. The zahir al-riwayah restricts it to outside the city.
These differences affect practice.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the zahir al-riwayah: permissible only outside the city, and one should dismount for Fajr sunnah. This is because the hadith mentions travel and the need to ride is greater outside.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شہر سے باہر چوپائے پر نفل پڑھنے کا حکم اقوال فقہاء
ومن كان خارج المصر تنفل على دابة الى اى جهة توجهت يومى ايماء، لحديث ابن عمر رضى الله عنهما لال رأیت رسول الله الا الله يصلى على حمار وهو متوجه الى خيبر يومى ايماء ولان النوافل غير مختصة بوقت قلو الزمناه النزول والاستقبال تنقطع عنه القافلة أو ينقطع هو عن القافلة اما الفرائض مختصة بوقت السنن الرواتب نوافل و عن ابي حنيفة انه ينزل لسنة الفجر لانها اكد من سائر والتقييد بخارج المصر نمى اشتراط السفر والجواز في المصر و عن ابى يوسف انه يجوز في المصر ايضا ووجه الظاهر ان النص و لخارج المصر والحاجة الى الركوب فيه اغلب
اور جو شخص شہر سے باہر ہو وہ اپنی سواری پر نفل نماز پڑھے جس طرف چاہے متوجہ ہو درانحالیکہ اشارہ کرے۔ حدیث ابن عمر کی سے فرمایا کہ میں نے رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کو دیکھا کہ آپ اشارہ کرتے ہوئے گدھے پر نماز پڑھ رہے تھے۔ درانحالیکہ آپ خیبر کی طرف تھے اور اس لئے کہ نوافل وقت کے ساتھ مختص نہیں ہیں۔ پس اگر ہم اس پر سواری سے اترنا اور قبلہ کی طرف متوجہ ہونا لازم کر دیں تو قافلہ نماز منقطع ہو جائے گی یا یہ قافلہ سے بچھڑ جائے گا۔ رہے فرائض تو وہ خاص اوقات کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں اور رات بہ منتیں بھی نفل ۔ اور ابوحنیفہ سے روایت کیا جاتا ہے کہ سنت فجر کے لئے اتر پڑے کیونکہ وہ دوسری سنتوں سے زیادہ مؤکدہ ہے اور خارج مصر کی قید اور اس کی نفی کرتا ہے۔ اور شہر میں جواز کی نفی کرتا ہے۔ اور ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ شہر میں بھی جائز ہے۔ اور ظاہر الروایہ کی وجہ یہ جانیں شہر سے باہر ہونے کی وارد ہوئی ہے۔ اور وہاں سواری کی ضرورت بھی زائد ہے۔ فاتیح مسئلہ شہر سے باہر سواری پر نفل نماز پڑھنا جائز ہے خواہ عذر کی وجہ سے ہو یا بغیر عذر کے افتتاح نماز " اقتباہ کی طرف متورہ ہو یا
Ruling on praying voluntary prayer on an animal outside the city: statements of jurists. And whoever is outside the city, he may perform voluntary prayer on a mount, facing any direction he wishes, making gestures (for bowing and prostrating), based on the hadith of Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) that he said: I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) praying on a donkey while heading to Khaybar, making gestures. And because voluntary prayers are not restricted to a specific time; if we were to obligate him to dismount and face the qibla, the caravan would become separated from him or he from the caravan. As for obligatory prayers, they are restricted to specific times. And the regular sunan (rawatib) are also voluntary. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that one should dismount for the sunnah of Fajr because it is more emphasized than others. And the restriction to outside the city negates the condition of travel (for this concession). And Abu Yusuf narrated that it is permissible even within the city. The apparent (zahir al-riwayah) is that the text (hadith) was reported about being outside the city, and the need to ride is more common there. So the conclusion is that it is permissible to pray voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city, whether due to an excuse or without excuse, regardless of the direction at the beginning of the prayer.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on performing voluntary (nafl) prayers on a riding animal while traveling outside the city. The main ruling is that it is permissible to pray nafl on a mount, facing whichever direction the animal turns, and making gestures (ima') for bowing and prostration instead of full movements. The proof is a hadith of Ibn Umar seeing the Prophet pray on a donkey while traveling to Khaybar, gesturing. The rationale is that voluntary prayers are not time-bound, and requiring one to dismount and face the qibla would cause hardship by separating the traveler from the caravan. Obligatory prayers (fard) are excluded from this concession because they are time-specific and must be performed with full conditions. The passage then discusses a sub-issue: Abu Hanifa is reported to hold that one must dismount for the sunnah of Fajr, as it is more emphasized than other sunnan. The author clarifies that the concession is specifically for outside the city (misr) and not for within. Abu Yusuf, however, permits it even within the city, but the zahir al-riwayah (prevalent transmitted opinion) restricts it to outside, where the need to ride is more common. The passage concludes that the ruling is general permission for voluntary prayer on a mount outside the city, whether one has an excuse or not, and regardless of the initial direction.

Key Terms
مصر (misr): A city or town; outside the city limits where travel begins.
ایماء (ima'): Gesturing with the head for bowing and prostration, instead of full physical movements.
ظاہر الروایہ (zahir al-riwayah): The well-known transmitted opinion from the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the prominent opinion (zahir al-riwayah), where is it permissible to perform voluntary prayer on a mount?
A) Only inside the city
B) Only outside the city
C) Both inside and outside the city
D) Only while traveling for Hajj

Key Takeaway
Voluntary prayers on a mount outside the city are permissible with gestures, but obligatory prayers and the Fajr sunnah (per Abu Hanifa) require dismounting and full conditions.

Sitting in Nafl Prayer Without Excuse: Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on sitting in nafl prayer without excuse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on sitting in nafl prayer without excuse and explain the istihsani vs qiyasi reasoning.

Core Idea
Starting nafl standing does not obligate standing throughout; only the first rak'ah is bound.

This lesson explores an important intra-Hanafi dispute: if you start a nafl prayer standing and then sit without excuse, is it permissible? Imam Abu Hanifa says yes, based on istihsan. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say no, using qiyas on a vow (nadhr). Understanding their reasoning sharpens your fiqh instincts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify both positions: Abu Hanifa's permissibility (jaa'iz) and the Sahibayn's impermissibility (naa jaa'iz).
These are transmitted in Zahir al-Riwayah.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
They use qiyas on nadhr: just as a vow to pray standing obligates standing throughout, starting nafl standing has a similar effect.
This is qiyas jali.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
He uses istihsan: starting nafl only obligates what is necessary for validity. The first rak'ah's validity does not depend on standing in the second.
The 'illa (effective cause) in nadhr is explicit intention, absent in ordinary nafl.
4
Analyze the distinction
Contrast nadhr where one explicitly vows to stand versus mere commencement of nafl. Abu Hanifa argues that without explicit intention, standing is not obligatory beyond the first rak'ah.
Some later scholars say if you just intend nafl without specifying standing, standing is not obligatory.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, one may follow Abu Hanifa and sit when tired, or follow the Sahibayn out of caution. The mufta bihi is not specified here but later Hanafi fatwa often prefers the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ناتا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے نفل نماز کھڑے ہو کر شروع کی پھر بلا عذر بیٹھ گیا تو امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز ہے۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک نا جائز ہے حکم اول استحسانی ہے اور ثانی قیاسی ہے۔ صاحبین کی دلیل قیاس ہے یعنی نفل نماز شروع کرنا قیاس کیا گیا ہے نذر پر طور که اگر کسی نے کھڑے ہو کر نفل پڑھنے کی نذر کی تو اس کے لئے بیٹھ کر پڑھنا جائز نہ ہوگا اسی طرح اگر کھڑے ہو کر نفل نماز شروع کی ان بیٹھ کر پڑھنا جائز نہ ہوگا۔
لام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سابق میں گذر چکا ہے کہ شروع کرنا اس چیز کو لازم کرتا ہے جس کو شروع کیا گیا ہے اور جس پر ما شرع ا بحت موقوف ہے تو نفل شروع کرنے سے رکعت اولی اور ثانیہ دونوں واجب ہوں گی ۔ رکعت اولی تو اس لئے واجب ہوگی کہ اس کو انا کیا گیا ہے اور رکعت ثانیہ اس لئے کہ اس پر رکعت اولی کی صحت موقوف ہے کیونکہ صلوة بتیر ا ممنوع ہے ۔ مگر مسئلہ مذکورہ میں رکعت دکھڑے ہو کر شروع کیا گیا ہے لیکن اس کی صحت اس پر موقوف نہیں کہ رکعت ثانیہ کو بھی کھڑے ہو کر پڑھا جائے۔ انذار کعت اولی کو کھڑے ہو کر شروع کرنے سے رکعت ثانیہ میں قیام لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف نذر ہے کیونکہ نذر کی صورت نہاں نے صراحتہ اپنے اوپر قیام لازم کر لیا ہے لہذا کھڑے ہو کر پڑھنے سے نذر پوری ہوگی چنانچہ اگر کسی نے قیام کی صراحت نہیں کی ، ارنا یہ کہا کہ میں نفل نماز پڑھوں گا تو بعض مشائخ کے نزدیک اس پر قیام لازم نہیں ہے۔
The issue is that if someone started nafl prayer standing then sat without excuse, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible. And according to the Sahibayn it is not permissible. The first ruling is istihsani and the second is qiyasi. The proof of the Sahibayn is qiyas, meaning starting nafl prayer is analogized to nadhr: if someone vowed to pray nafl standing, then sitting would not be permissible; similarly, if he started nafl standing, sitting would not be permissible. As for Abu Hanifa's proof, it has passed before that starting makes obligatory what was started and what the act depends on for validity. So starting nafl makes both the first and second rak'ah obligatory. The first rak'ah is obligatory because it was initiated, and the second because the validity of the first depends on it, since praying with one rak'ah is prohibited. But in the mentioned issue, the first rak'ah was started standing, but its validity does not depend on the second rak'ah also being performed standing. Starting the first rak'ah standing does not make standing in the second rak'ah obligatory. In contrast is nadhr, because in nadhr the person explicitly made standing obligatory upon himself; therefore, the vow is fulfilled by praying standing. So if someone did not explicitly mention standing, but said 'I will pray nafl,' then according to some scholars standing is not obligatory for him.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of sitting in nafl prayer without excuse after starting standing. It is an expansion of the Hidayah text. Abu Hanifa holds it permissible (jaa'iz) based on istihsan: merely starting a nafl does not make standing in every rak'ah obligatory; only the first rak'ah is bound by the posture of commencement, while the second rak'ah does not require standing for validity since the prohibition of praying a single rak'ah is not violated by sitting in the second. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it impermissible (naa jaa'iz) based on qiyas to nadhr: just as a vow to pray standing obligates standing throughout, so does the act of starting nafl standing obligate standing in all rak'ats. Abu Hanifa responds by distinguishing nadhr, where explicit intention creates obligation, from ordinary nafl where the mere commencement does not carry that implicit vow. The passage also notes that if someone simply intends to pray nafl without specifying standing, some later scholars hold standing not obligatory.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayer, not obligatory but meritorious.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a shared effective cause ('illa).
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference: departing from qiyas in favor of a more suitable ruling due to need, ease, or a stronger evidence.
نذر (nadhr): A vow by which a person obligates upon himself a specific act of worship, such as praying in a certain manner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), what is the ruling if someone starts nafl prayer standing and then sits without excuse?
A) Permissible because nafl is voluntary
B) Impermissible, by analogy to a vow (nadhr)
C) Permissible only if one recites while sitting
D) The prayer becomes invalid and must be restarted

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on sitting in nafl prayer, with Abu Hanifa permitting it via istihsan and the Sahibayn prohibiting it via qiyas on nadhr.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
12 min
Nafl Prayer on a Riding Animal Outside the City
Ruling with proof from hadith and rational argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on nafl prayer on a riding animal, identify the primary dalil, and apply the conditions and exceptions including the dispute on qiblah.

Core Idea
Nafl prayer on a riding animal is permissible outside the city; obligatory prayers require an excuse.

This lesson examines a foundational Hanafi ruling: performing nafl prayers while riding an animal outside the built-up area. Based on a clear Prophetic practice, the school permits such prayers with gestures even without an excuse, while distinguishing between nafl and obligatory prayers. We will explore the proof, the scope of the permission, and key differences within the Hanafi school and with Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing nafl prayer on a riding animal outside the city. The Hanafi ruling is that it is permissible (jaa'iz) and the prayer is valid with gestures.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith of Ibn Umar (RA) who saw the Prophet (SAW) praying on a donkey while heading to Khaybar, making gestures.
Hadith is ahad, zanni al-thubut, but qat'i al-dalalah for permissibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action directly demonstrates permissibility. Additionally, the rational proof: nafl prayers are not time-bound, so requiring dismount would cause hardship (falling behind caravan or missing prayer).
This rational proof is also cited in the text as 'li anna al-nawafil ghayr mukhtassah bi-waqt'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa: dismount for Fajr sunnah (more emphasized); a narration from Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf restricts permissibility to travelers (28 miles); the Sahibayn permit emphasized sunnahs like nafl.
The mufta bihi is the Zahir al-Riwayah: no travel condition, and Fajr sunnah may be performed on animal (though dismounting is better).
5
Identify the cross-madhhab dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i requires facing qiblah at the start of the prayer even on an animal. Hanafi position: facing qiblah is not required at the start based on the hadith.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in Hanafi, you can start facing any direction; in Shafi'i, you must start facing qiblah then may turn.
