Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Sunnah Status of Tarawih Prayer and Its Description
Ruling that Tarawih is sunnah and description of its performance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Tarawih (sunnah mu'akkadah) and describe its method of performance, distinguishing it from general nafl prayers.

Core Idea
Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard or wajib, established by the Caliphs' practice and the Prophet's excuse.

Tarawih prayer, while often grouped with supererogatory prayers, carries unique features that distinguish it from general nafl. The Hanafi school emphasizes its status as an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), supported by the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and a hadith in which the Prophet prescribed its night vigil. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the specific manner of performing Tarawih as described in al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its distinctive features
Recognize that Tarawih is a special prayer for Ramadan nights. Note the four ways it differs from general nafl: congregation, fixed number of rak'ahs, specific time, and the sunnah of completing the Quran.
These distinctions justify a separate section in the fiqh text.
2
Locate the dalil and its implication
Examine the hadith cited: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed fasting for you and I have prescribed its night vigil for you.' The operative word 'sunnantu' (I have prescribed as sunnah) indicates the ruling level.
The hadith is from Ibn Majah; its chain is ahad, so the ruling is zanni al-thubut, supporting sunnah, not fard.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that al-Quduri used the word 'mustahab' for Tarawih. The correct (asahh) view, as narrated by Hasan from Abu Hanifa, is that it is sunnah. The Prophet's excuse (fear of fard obligation) and the Caliphs' persistence strengthen the sunnah ruling.
The term 'mustahab' in the text refers to the desirability of congregation, not the ruling of the prayer itself.
4
Describe the method of performance
The text details: twenty rak'ahs (five tarwihas of four rak'ahs each? Actually, the text says 'five tarwihas each with two taslims' – twenty rak'ahs is the standard Hanafi position; the description may be interpreted as two rak'ahs per taslim, so five tarwihas of two taslims each = ten rak'ahs? Clarify: The relied-upon practice is twenty rak'ahs, but the text's phrasing may be an alternate narration. The key elements: after Isha, in congregation, imam leads, with breaks between tarwihas, then witr.
The break between tarwihas is equal to the duration of one tarwiha.
5
Recognize the tarjih and mufta bihi
Al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah declares that the view of Tarawih being sunnah is the most sound (asahh). This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah (from the core books).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في قيام رمضان
ترجمہ تراویح کی نماز چونکہ نوافل سے ایک گونہ مختلف ہے۔ اس لئے تراویح یعنی قیام لیل کو علیحدہ فصل میں ذکر کیا ہے۔ تراویح عام نوافل سے چند باتوں میں مختلف ہے اول یہ کہ عام نوافل میں جماعت نہیں اور تراویح میں جماعت ہے۔ دوم یہ کہ نوافل میں تحدید رکعات نہیں ہے اور تراویح میں تقدیر رکعات ہے۔ سوم یہ کہ نوافل کسی وقت کے ساتھ مخصوص نہیں ہوتے اور تراویح رمضان کی راتوں کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے ۔ چہارم یہ کہ تراویح میں ایک قرآن ختم کرنا مسنون ہے دوسرے نوافل میں یہ سنت نہیں ۔ (عنایہ) صاحب ہدایہ نے عنوان میں قیام رمضان کا لفظ حدیث کا اتباع کرتے ہوئے تحریر کیا ہے کیونکہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ان الله تعالى فرض عليكم صيامه وسنت لكم قيامه یعنی اللہ تعالیٰ نے تمہارے اوپر رمضان کا روزہ فرض کیا اور میں نے تمہارے لئے اس کے قیام کو مسنون کیا (ابن ماجہ) چونکہ حدیث میں قیام رمضان کا لفظ موجود ہے اس لئے فصل کا عنوان بھی اسی لفظ کے ساتھ تجویز کیا گیا۔ نماز تراویح کے لئے اجتماع مستحب ہے، نماز تراویح کی رکعات
تحب ان يجتمع الناس فى شهر رمضان بعد العشاء، فيصلى بهم امامهم خمس ترويحات كل ترويحة تسليمتين، ويجلس بين كل ترويحتين مقدار ترويحة، ثم يوتر بهم ذكر لفظ الاستحباب والاصح انها سنة كذا روى الحسن عن ابي حنيفة، لانه واظب عليها الخلفاء الراشدون والنبي عليه السلام بين العذر لتركه المواظبة، وهو خشية ان تكتب علينا
ترجمہ رمضان کے ماہ میں عشاء کے بعد لوگوں کا جمع ہونا مستحب ہے پس ان کا امام ان کو پانچ ترویحات پڑھائے۔ ہر ترویحہ دو سلام کے ساتھ اور ہر دو ترویحات کے درمیان ایک ترویحہ کی مقدار بیٹھے پھر امام ان کو وتر پڑھائے۔ قدوری نے لفظ استحباب ذکر کیا اور اصح یہ ہے کہ تراویح سنت ہے یوں ہی حسن نے بھی ابو حنیفہ سے روایت کیا ہے کیونکہ خلفاء راشدین نے اس پر مواظبت فرمائی ہے اور حضور نے تک مواظبت پر عذر بیان کر دیا تھا اور وہ ہم پر فرض ہونے کا خوف ہے۔
Section on the Night Vigil (Qiyam) of Ramadan. Translation: Since Tarawih prayer differs somewhat from supererogatory prayers, it is mentioned in a separate section. Tarawih differs from general nafl prayers in several ways: First, in general nafl there is no congregation, but in Tarawih there is congregation. Second, nafl prayers have no fixed number of rak'ahs, but Tarawih has a set number. Third, nafl are not restricted to a specific time, but Tarawih is specific to the nights of Ramadan. Fourth, completing one recitation of the Quran in Tarawih is sunnah, which is not the case in other nafl. The author of Hidayah used the phrase 'Qiyam Ramadan' following the hadith: 'Indeed Allah has prescribed fasting for you and I have prescribed its night vigil for you' (Ibn Majah). Congregation for Tarawih is mustahab. Arabic: It is desirable that people gather in the month of Ramadan after Isha, and their imam leads them in five tarwihas, each tarwiha with two taslims, and he sits between every two tarwihas for the duration of a tarwiha, then he leads them in witr. He mentioned the word istihbab (desirability), but the correct view is that it is sunnah. Thus Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa, because the Rightly Guided Caliphs persisted upon it, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave an excuse for not persisting, which was the fear that it would be prescribed upon us.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage introduces the section on Tarawih prayer. The author distinguishes Tarawih from general nafl prayers in four aspects: congregation, fixed number of rak'ahs, specific time (Ramadan nights), and the sunnah of completing the Quran. The title 'Qiyam Ramadan' is taken from a hadith where the Prophet said Allah made Ramadan fasting obligatory and he made its night vigil (qiyam) sunnah. The text then states that it is mustahab (desirable) for people to gather for Tarawih, and the imam leads them in five tarwihas (each tarwiha being two rak'ahs with two taslims), with a pause between tarwihas equal to a tarwiha, followed by witr. Al-Quduri used the word 'istihbab', but the correct (asahh) position is that Tarawih is sunnah (as narrated by Hasan from Abu Hanifa). The proof is the consistent practice of the Khulafa Rashidin. The Prophet did not continuously practice it out of fear that it would become compulsory (fard) upon the community. This establishes that Tarawih is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) in the Hanafi school. Students should note that the word 'mustahab' in the text is not contradictory to it being sunnah; it indicates the desirability of congregation, while the prayer itself is sunnah.

Key Terms
تراویح (Tarawih): The night prayer performed in congregation during the nights of Ramadan, consisting of a specific number of rak'ahs.
قیام رمضان (Qiyam Ramadan): The night vigil (prayer) specific to the month of Ramadan, synonymous with Tarawih.
ترویحة (Tarwiha): A set of two rak'ahs of Tarawih with one taslim, also the term for the rest between such sets.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon Hanafi position on the status of Tarawih prayer?
A) It is fard
B) It is mustahab only
C) It is sunnah
D) It is mubah

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is an emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) established by Prophetic hadith and the consistent practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs, performed after Isha in congregation during Ramadan nights.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
Tarawih as Sunnah Mu'akkadah: Proofs and Responses
Establishes Tarawih as sunnah mu'akkadah with proofs from caliphs and Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling of Tarawih as sunnah mu'akkadah and explain the proofs from the Caliphs' practice and the Prophet's command to follow their sunnah.

Core Idea
Tarawih is sunnah mu'akkadah — the Caliphs' persistence proves it; the Prophet's fear of obligation explains his intermittent practice.

Tarawih prayer is one of the most visible acts of worship during Ramadan. While many Muslims know it is recommended, the exact ruling in the Hanafi school is precisely sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah). This lesson unpacks the evidence from the Rightly Guided Caliphs and the Prophet's own guidance, and explains why the great scholar al-Quduri used the word 'mustahab'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the passage is about Tarawih prayer (night prayers in Ramadan) and the ruling being established is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah) for both men and women.
2
Locate the primary proof
The author cites the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs (specifically Umar and Uthman) who persisted in Tarawih with 20 rak'ahs in congregation, and the Prophet's command to follow their sunnah.
The hadith 'عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين' is the key textual evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Caliphs' continuous practice under the command to follow their sunnah elevates Tarawih to sunnah mu'akkadah. The Prophet's own action of leading 20 rak'ahs but then stopping out of fear that it become obligatory confirms it is not fard but highly recommended.
4
Address the objection
The objection that the Prophet did not always lead Tarawih is answered: he feared it would become fard upon the ummah, so he sometimes left it to prevent that. This actually supports its status as sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
5
Reconcile with Quduri's wording
Al-Quduri used 'mustahab' for Tarawih, but the author clarifies that either Quduri meant the congregation (not the prayer) is mustahab, or early scholars used 'mustahab' broadly to include even wajib. The relied-upon view is sunnah mu'akkadah.

Source Text

صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ ترویحہ چار رکعت کا نام ہے کیونکہ چار رکعتیں راحت و آرام تک پہونچا دیتی ہیں یعنی چار رکنا بعد راحت و آرام کی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔
نماز تراویح سنت مؤکدہ ہے: قدوری کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تراویح کی نماز مستحب ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں بات یہ ہے کہ تراویح سنت مؤکدہ ہے مردوں کے لئے بھی اور عورتوں کے لئے بھی امام ابو حنیفہ سے بھی یہی مروی ہے کہ تراویح مؤکدہ ہے۔ مؤکدہ ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ خلفاء راشدین نے تراویح کی نماز پر مواظبت اور مداومت فرمائی ہے اور ان راشدین کا کسی [؟] مواظبت فرمانا اس کے مسنون ہونے کی دلیل ہے کیونکہ نبی کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے علیکم بسنتی وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين من بعدى یعنی تم پر میری اور میرے بعد خلفاء کی سنت لازم ہے۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جریان آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کے معمول بہا طریق کو سنت کہتے ہیں اسی طرح خلفاء راشدین کے طریقہ کو بھی سنت کہتے ہیں۔ لیکن یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ ہدایہ کی عبارت میں خلفاء کا لفظ تغلیبا استعمال کیا گیا ہے ورنہ یہاں خلفاء سے حضرت عمر ، عثمان علی مراد ہیں کیونکہ ان جماعت کے [؟] رکعات تراویح کا آغاز فاروق اعظم کے عہد خلافت سے ہوا ہے ورنہ اس سے پہلے لوگ فرادی فرادی پڑھتے تھے چنانچہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا تھا انى ارى ان اجمع الناس على امام واحد جمعهم على ابی بن كعب فصلى بهم عشرين ركعة میں لوگوں کو ایک امام پر اکٹھا کرنا چاہتا ہوں پس ان کو ابی بن کعب پر اکٹھا فرما یا پھر ابی بن کعب نے زوال کو پانچ ترویحوں میں عشرین رکعات نماز پڑھائی۔
اعتراض: اب ایک اعتراض ہوگا۔ وہ یہ کہ تراویح کی نماز اگر سنت مؤکدہ ہے تو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے اس پر مواظبت کیوں نہیں فرمائی ۔ جواب: صاحب ہدایہ نے جواب کی طرف اشارہ کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ آنحضرت نے ترک مواظبت پر یہ عذر فرمایا کہ میرے مواظبت کرنے سے امت پر فرض ہونے کا احتمال تھا اس لئے میں نے تراویح پر مداومت نہیں کی بلکہ کبھی کبھی چھوڑ بھی ہے۔ چنانچہ مروی ہے
انه خرج ليلية من ليال رمضان وصلى عشرين ركعة فلما كانت الليلة الثانية اجتمع الناس فخرج و صلی بهم عشرین ركعة فلما كانت الليلة الثالثة كثر الناس فلم يخرج عليه السلام و قال عرفت اجتماعكم لكني خشيت ان تكتب عليكم فكان الناس يصلونها فرادى الى زمن عمر رضى الله عنه یعنی رمضان کی راتوں میں سے ایک رات اللہ کے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم تشریف لائے اور لوگوں کو عشرین رکعات پڑھا ئیں۔ پس جو دوسری رات ہوئی اور لوگ جمع ہو گئے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم تشریف لائے اور لوگوں کو عشرین رکعت پڑھائیں پس جب تیسری رات ہوئی اور لوگ بہت ہو گئے تو آپ تشریف نہیں لائے اور یہ فرمایا کہ مجھے تمہارا جمع ہونا معلوم ہے لیکن مجھے خوف ہے کہ کہیں تم پر فرض نہ کر دی جائے ۔ پس لوگ حضرت عمرؓ کے عہد خلافت تک فرادی فرادی نماز پڑھتے رہے۔
سوال جب تراویح کی نماز سنت مؤکدہ ہے تو صاحب قدوری نے لفظ مستحب کیوں کہا؟ جواب مشائخ متقدمین لفظ مستحب کو بھی بہت خوب کے لئے استعمال کرتے ہیں۔ اور بہت خوب کا لفظ واجب تک کو شامل ہے کہ ممکن ہے کہ مستحب کا لفظ یہاں اسی معنی میں ہو یعنی تراویح کے لئے اجتماع بہت خوب اور بڑی فضیلت کی چیز ہے اور یہ سنت ہے۔
جلد دوم شرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم ياب النوافل
مجلسه سرا جواب یہ ہے کہ شیخ ابو الحسن قدوری نے لوگوں کے اجتماع کو مستحب کہا ہے نہ کہ تراویح کی نماز کو۔ پس یوں کہہ لیجئے رمضان مبارک کے اندر عشاء کی نماز کے بعد لوگوں کا اجتماع تو مستحب ہے لیکن تراویح کی نماز سنت ہے۔
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary: He makes the people pray five tarwihahs, each tarwihah with two salams, and between every two tarwihahs, he rests for the amount of one tarwihah. Then the imam leads them in witr prayer. The author of al-Inayah wrote that tarwihah is the name for four rak'ahs because four rak'ahs bring to rest and comfort, meaning after four rak'ahs rest and comfort are permitted. Tarawih prayer is an emphatic sunnah: from Quduri's text it appears that Tarawih prayer is mustahab. The author of al-Hidayah says: the correct view is that Tarawih is an emphatic sunnah for both men and women. This is also narrated from Imam Abu Hanifah that Tarawih is mu'akkadah. The proof of it being mu'akkadah is that the Rightly Guided Caliphs observed and persevered in Tarawih prayer, and the Caliphs' perseverance in something is evidence of its being sunnah because the Prophet (SAW) said: 'Hold fast to my sunnah and the sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs after me.' This hadith indicates that the practice followed by the Prophet is called sunnah, and similarly the way of the Rightly Guided Caliphs is also called sunnah. But it should be kept in mind that in the text of al-Hidayah, the word 'caliphs' is used dominantly, otherwise here by 'caliphs' is meant Umar and Uthman, because the commencement of twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih was from the reign of Umar al-Faruq; before that people prayed individually. Thus Umar said: 'I intend to gather the people behind one imam.' So he gathered them behind Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and he led them in twenty rak'ahs. Then Ubayy ibn Ka'b led the people in twenty rak'ahs in five tarwihahs. Objection: Now there will be an objection: If Tarawih is an emphatic sunnah, why did the Prophet not persevere in it? Answer: The author of al-Hidayah indicated the answer: The Prophet made the excuse for not persevering that if he persevered, there was a fear that it might become obligatory upon the ummah, so he did not continue Tarawih constantly but sometimes left it. It is narrated that he came out one night of Ramadan and prayed twenty rak'ahs. When the second night came, people gathered, so he came out and prayed twenty rak'ahs. Then when the third night came, people increased, so he did not come out and said: 'I knew of your gathering, but I feared that it might be prescribed as obligatory upon you.' So people prayed individually until the time of Umar (RA). Question: When Tarawih is an emphatic sunnah, why did Quduri use the word 'mustahab'? Answer: The early scholars used the word 'mustahab' for something very good, and the word 'very good' includes even wajib, so it is possible that the word 'mustahab' here is used in that sense, meaning that gathering for Tarawih is a very good and virtuous thing, and it is sunnah. Volume 2 of Sharh al-Bidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers. Another answer: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri called the congregation of people 'mustahab', not the Tarawih prayer itself. So say: The gathering of people after Isha prayer in blessed Ramadan is mustahab, but Tarawih prayer is sunnah.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah establishes the ruling of Tarawih prayer as an emphatic sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) for both men and women, in contrast to the view of al-Quduri who considered it mustahab. The author first defines Tarawih: it consists of five tarwihahs (each tarwihah being four rak'ahs with two salams), with rest between tarwihahs, followed by Witr. The term 'tarwihah' comes from 'raha' (rest) because four rak'ahs bring rest. The core ruling is stated: 'Tarawih prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah.' A proof is adduced: the Rightly Guided Caliphs (specifically Umar and Uthman) persisted in it, and the Prophet's hadith commands following their sunnah. The author notes that although the hadith says 'the Caliphs', it refers mainly to Umar and Uthman because the twenty-rak'ah Tarawih with congregation was initiated by Umar. Before that, people prayed individually. Umar gathered the people behind Ubayy ibn Ka'b, who led twenty rak'ahs in five tarwihahs. An objection is raised: if it is sunnah mu'akkadah, why did the Prophet himself not persevere in congregational Tarawih? The answer: he feared it would become fard (obligatory), so he sometimes left it to prevent that. A narration is cited: the Prophet led twenty rak'ahs on two nights, then stopped on the third night fearing prescription. Then a question about Quduri's use of 'mustahab' is addressed. Two answers are given: (1) early scholars used 'mustahab' broadly for any commendable act, even wajib; (2) Quduri actually considered the congregation as mustahab, not the prayer itself. Thus the prayer remains sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms
تراویح (tarawih): The name for the night prayers of Ramadan, typically performed in congregation, consisting of 20 rak'ahs in 5 tarwihahs (sets of 4 rak'ahs).
سنت مؤکدہ (sunnah mu'akkadah): An emphatic sunnah; an act that the Prophet performed regularly and persistently, and that is highly recommended but not obligatory.
مستحب (mustahab): Recommended; an act that is commendable but not as strongly emphasized as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Hidayah, what is the ruling of Tarawih prayer?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Mustahab
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
Tarawih prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatic sunnah) in the Hanafi school, proven by the Caliphs' practice and the Prophet's command to follow their sunnah.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Number of Rak'ahs in Tarawih: Reconciling 11 and 20
Reconciling conflicting hadiths on Tarawih rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on Tarawih rak'ahs, identify the two conflicting hadiths, and explain the reconciliation method used by Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs sunnah; the 11-rak'ah hadith reflects the Prophet's private practice, not the sunnah for the community.

This passage tackles a well-known apparent contradiction: the hadith of Aisha (RA) reports the Prophet prayed only 11 rak'ahs in Ramadan, while the hadith of Ibn Abbas (RA) reports 20 rak'ahs. How does the Hanafi school reconcile these? The answer lies in distinguishing the Prophet's personal devotion from the sunnah he established for the Ummah through the practice of the Caliphs. Let's examine the evidence and the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two conflicting hadiths
Find the hadith from Aisha (11 rak'ahs including Witr) and the hadith from Ibn Abbas (20 rak'ahs excluding Witr). Note their sources.
Aisha's hadith is in Sahih al-Bukhari; Ibn Abbas's hadith is reported by al-Tahawi.
2
Understand the apparent conflict
One hadith says 11, the other says 20. How can both be authentic? Recognise that the 11 includes Witr, so Tarawih proper would be 8; the 20 is exclusively Tarawih.
Some reconcile by saying 8 is sunnah, 20 is mustahabb, but the Hanafi position is that 20 is sunnah mu'akkadah.
3
Analyse the Hanafi reconciliation method
The Hanafi school holds that the Prophet's 11 rak'ahs were his personal tahajjud, not the congregational Tarawih. The 20 rak'ahs were established by the Caliphs with the Prophet's implicit approval, and thus become the sunnah for the community.
The tarjih relies on the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs as a source of sunnah.
4
State the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs, sunnah mu'akkadah. The congregation for it is mustahabb, not the prayer itself.
Al-Quduri's statement about mustahabb refers to the gathering, not the prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مجلسه سرا جواب یہ ہے کہ شیخ ابو الحسن قدوری نے لوگوں کے اجتماع کو مستحب کہا ہے نہ کہ تراویح کی نماز کو۔ پس یوں کہہ لیجئے رمضان مبارک کے اندر عشاء کی نماز کے بعد لوگوں کا اجتماع تو مستحب ہے لیکن تراویح کی نماز سنت ہے۔
ت کے نیر ا جواب یہ ہے کہ بعض صحیح روایتوں سے ثابت ہے کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے وتر سمیت تراویح کی گیارہ رکعت پڑھی ہیں اور بعض سے نہیں رکعت کا ثبوت ملتا ہے۔ گیارہ رکعت ابو سلمہ بن عبد الرحمن کی حدیث سے ثابت ہیں حدیث کے الفاظ یہ ہیں مالت عائشة
ل كيف كانت صلوة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في رمضان فقالت ما كان يزيد في رمضان ولا غيره على احدى عشرة ركعة انت الحدیث ۔ (فتح القدیر ( ابوسلمہ بن عبد الرحمن کہتے ہیں کہ میں نے حضرت عائشہ سے دریافت کیا کہ رمضان میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی نماز القاء کس طرح تھی۔ آپ نے فرمایا کہ آپ گارمضان اور غیر رمضان میں گیارہ رکعات سے زما د نہیں پڑھتے تھے یعنی آٹھے تراویح کی اور تین سنة ار کی ۔ اور ابن عباس کی حدیث سے بیس رکعات کا ثبوت ملتا ہے انه كان يصلى في رمضان عشرين ركعة سوى الوتر رحمان عباس نے کہا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم رمضان المبارک میں علاوہ وتر کے ہیں رکعت پڑھتے تھے (فتح القدیر ) اب بعض حضرات نے ان دونوں این حدیثوں میں تطبیق دینے کی کوشش کی ہے۔ انہوں نے فرمایا کہ آٹھ رکعت وتر کے علاوہ سنت ہے اور میں رکعات مستحب ہیں ۔ پس ہو سکتا مرہ ہے کہ صاحب قدوری نے اس قول پر عمل کرتے ہوئے مستحب کہا ہو یعنی ہیں رکعات پانچ ترویحوں میں مستحب ہیں
The answer from the gathering: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said that the gathering of people is mustahabb, not the prayer of Tarawih. So say: In blessed Ramadan, after Isha prayer, the gathering of people is mustahabb, but the prayer of Tarawih is Sunnah. The answer from the discussion: It is established from some authentic narrations that the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed eleven rak'ahs of Tarawih including Witr, and from some, twenty rak'ahs are proven. Eleven rak'ahs are proven from the hadith of Abu Salama ibn Abd al-Rahman: I asked Aisha how the Prophet's prayer in Ramadan was, and she said he did not exceed eleven rak'ahs in Ramadan or otherwise. That is, eight Tarawih and three Witr. And from the hadith of Ibn Abbas, twenty rak'ahs are proven: He used to pray twenty rak'ahs in Ramadan apart from Witr. Some people attempted to reconcile these two hadiths. They said: Eight rak'ahs apart from Witr are Sunnah, and twenty rak'ahs are mustahabb. So it is possible that al-Quduri acted on this opinion and called them mustahabb, i.e., twenty rak'ahs in five tawarih are mustahabb.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof discussing the number of rak'ahs in Tarawih. The author presents two hadiths: one from Aisha (RA) stating the Prophet prayed 11 rak'ahs including Witr, and another from Ibn Abbas (RA) stating he prayed 20 rak'ahs excluding Witr. The Hanafi school follows the 20-rak'ah position, reconciling the hadiths by considering the 11 rak'ahs as the Prophet's personal practice and the 20 rak'ahs as the sunnah established by the caliphs. Here, some scholars reconcile by saying 8 rak'ahs are sunnah and 20 are mustahabb. However, the relied-upon Hanafi position is that 20 rak'ahs is sunnah mu'akkadah. The mention of al-Quduri's view that the gathering is mustahabb is clarified: the congregation for Tarawih is mustahabb, not the prayer itself.

Key Terms
تراویح (tarāwīḥ): The supererogatory night prayers in Ramadan, performed after Isha, consisting of 20 rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended but not obligatory; here used for the congregation, not the prayer itself.
تطبیق (taṭbīq): Reconciliation or harmonization between apparently conflicting textual evidences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the reason al-Quduri called Tarawih 'mustahabb'?
A) He considered the prayer itself mustahabb, not sunnah.
B) He referred to the gathering of people for Tarawih, not the prayer.
C) He followed the hadith of Aisha over Ibn Abbas.
D) He considered 20 rak'ahs to be bid'ah.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih is 20 rak'ahs sunnah mu'akkadah; the 11-rak'ah hadith describes the Prophet's private practice, while the 20-rak'ah practice was established by the Caliphs and is the operative sunnah for the community.

Congregation for Tarawih is Sunnah Kifayah
Ruling on congregation in Tarawih and proof from Sahaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that congregation for Tarawih is sunnah kifayah, explain the evidence from the Companions' practice, and distinguish between sunnah kifayah and sunnah 'ayn.

Core Idea
Congregation for Tarawih is sunnah kifayah: if some establish it, others lose only virtue, not incur sin.

This lesson examines a key ruling from Al-Hidayah: the nature of congregation for Tarawih. The author establishes it as sunnah kifayah (communal sunnah), meaning if some people perform it, others are absolved of sin but miss the virtue. We will explore the evidence from the Companions who prayed alone, the rebuttal of the view that it is sunnah 'ayn, and the practical implications of this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The passage states that congregation for Tarawih is sunnah, but as kifayah (sufficiency). This means it is a communal sunnah, not an individual obligation. Understand the consequence: if all people of a mosque refrain, they are sinful; if some establish it, those who abstain are 'tārik al-faḍīlah' (forsakers of virtue).
Sunnah kifayah is similar to fard kifayah but with reward instead of obligation.
2
Locate the primary proof
The proof is that some Companions (e.g., Ibn Umar and Urwa) are reported to have not joined the Tarawih congregation, indicating it is not individually obligatory. This is recorded by Imam Tahawi.
The hadith cited by Abu Yusuf is also discussed and rebutted.
3
Analyze the debate with the opposing view
Some scholars consider Tarawih congregation sunnah 'ayn (individual obligation). The passage rebuts this by noting the Prophet's excuse for not attending and the Caliphs' practice, which establishes the congregation as sunnah kifayah.
The practical difference: if sunnah 'ayn, missing it is a sin; if kifayah, missing it loses virtue.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi nuance
Imam Abu Yusuf reportedly allowed praying at home if recitation is maintained, but the majority of mashayikh (including the author of Hidayah) hold that congregation is sunnah kifayah and should not be abandoned without excuse.
The tarjih (preferring majority) is based on the practice of the Caliphs.
5
Synthesize the muftā bihi position
The operative ruling for fatwa is that congregation for Tarawih is sunnah kifayah. It is better to attend in the mosque, but if some establish it, others may pray at home without sin, though they lose virtue.
This balances the evidence from the Companions and the Caliphs.

ترجمہ اور سنت تراویح میں جماعت ہے لیکن بطور کفایہ حتی کہ اگر ایک مسجد والے ( سب لوگ ) قیام جماعت سے باز رہیں تو سب گنہگار ہوں گے اور اگر بعض نے جماعت قائم کر لی تو جو شخص جماعت سے پیچھے رہاوہ فضیلت کو چھوڑنے والا ہوا۔ کیونکہ افرادصحابہ کا پیچھے ربنا مروی ہے اور دو ترویحوں کے درمیان ایک ترویحہ کی مقدار بیٹھنا مستحب ہے۔ اور یوں ہی پانچویں ترویحہ اور وتر کے درمیان بھی کیونکہ اہل حرمین کی عادت ہے۔
تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اکثر مشائخ کے نزدیک تراویح کی جماعت سنت علی الکفایہ ہے چنانچہ ایک مسجد سے متعلق تمام لوگوں نے اگر جماعت تراویح کو ترک کر دیا تو سب گنہگار ہوں گے اور اگر بعض نے جماعت کو قائم کیا اور بعض نے ترک کر دیا تو جماعت میں شریک نہ ہونے والے تارک فضیلت ہوں گے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعض صحابہ ایسے ہیں جن سے تراویح کی جماعت میں شریک نہ ہونا مروی ہے۔ یعنی یہ حضرات صحابہ جماعت میں شریک نہیں ہوئے بلکہ تنہا پڑھی ہے۔ چنانچہ امام طحاوی نے ابن عمر اور عروہ سے اس کو روایت کیا ہے۔
بعض علماء نے تراویح کی جماعت کو سنت علی العین کہا ہے۔ لہذا ان کے نزدیک اگر کوئی شخص تنہا تر اویح کی نماز ادا کرے تو ترک سنت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ہو گا امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر سنت قرآت کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے گھر میں تراویح پڑھنا ممکن ہو تو جائز ہے کہ وہ گھر میں اکیلا تراویح کی نماز پڑھتے لیکن اگر کوئی شخص فقیہ کبیر ہو جس کے عمل کی لوگ اقتداء کرتے ہیں تو یہ فقیہ کبیر گھر میں تراویح ادا نہ کرے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل حضور گا یہ قول ہے عليكم بالصلوة في بيوتكم فان خير صلوة المرد في بيته الا المكتوبة یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم پر اپنے گھر میں نماز پڑھنا لازم ہے کیونکہ آدمی کی بہترین نماز اس کے گھر میں ہے علاوہ فرض نماز کے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ قیام رمضان اس حکم سے مستفی ہے کیونکہ پہلے معلوم ہو چکا کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مسجد میں آکر تراویح کی نماز ادا کی ہے اور جب تشریف نہیں لائے تو اس کا عذر بیان فرمایا اور خلفاء راشدین کا عمل بھی یہی رہا ہے کہ تاراویح کی نماز با جماعت مسجد میں ادا کی ہے اس لئے بلا عذر تراویح کی جماعت چھوڑنے کی اجازت نہیں دی جائے گی۔
And the Sunnah in it (Tarawih) is congregation, but in the manner of kifayah (sufficiency), so if the people of the mosque refrain from establishing it, they are sinful, and if some establish it, then the one who abstains from the congregation leaves off virtue, because individuals from the Companions are reported to have abstained. Translation: And in Tarawih, congregation is Sunnah but as kifayah, such that if the people of a mosque all refrain from congregation, they all sin; and if some establish it, the one who stays behind from congregation is a forsaker of virtue, because individuals from the Companions are reported to have abstained. Explanation: The author of Hidayah said that according to most scholars, congregation for Tarawih is sunnah ala al-kifayah. So if all people of a mosque abandon Tarawih congregation, they all sin; if some establish it and some leave it, those not joining are forsakers of virtue. The proof is that some Companions are reported to have not joined Tarawih congregation; they prayed alone. Imam Tahawi narrated this from Ibn Umar and Urwa. Some scholars said Tarawih congregation is sunnah ala al-ayn. In their view, if someone prays Tarawih alone, he sins for abandoning the sunnah. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if it is possible to pray Tarawih at home while observing the sunnah recitation, then it is permissible to pray alone at home. But if one is a great jurist whose actions are imitated by people, he should not pray at home. Abu Yusuf's proof is the Prophet's saying: 'Hold fast to prayer in your houses, for the best of a person's prayer is in his house except the obligatory prayer.' Our response: Qiyam Ramadan is excluded from this ruling because it is known that the Prophet came to the mosque to pray Tarawih, and when he did not come, he gave an excuse, and the practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was to pray Tarawih in congregation in the mosque. Therefore, without excuse, leaving the congregation for Tarawih is not permitted.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the nature of congregation for Tarawih. It states that congregation for Tarawih is sunnah kifayah, meaning if some people establish it, others are not sinful for missing it, but they miss out on virtue. The proof is that some Companions (like Ibn Umar and Urwa) are reported to have not joined the Tarawih congregation, yet their practice is not condemned. The passage then handles the opposite view that it is sunnah 'ayn (obligatory for every individual) and rebuts it. It presents Abu Yusuf's position allowing praying alone at home if the sunnah recitation can be maintained, but for a great scholar, it is better to attend to encourage others. The final Hanafi position is that Tarawih congregation is sunnah kifayah and should not be abandoned without excuse, following the practice of the Caliphs.

Key Terms
سنة الكفاية (sunnat al-kifāyah): A communal sunnah; if some perform it, others are absolved of sin.
تارك الفضيلة (tārik al-faḍīlah): One who abandons a virtuous act, missing reward but incurring no sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on congregation for Tarawih?
A) Sunnah 'ayn (individual obligation)
B) Sunnah kifayah (communal sunnah)
C) Wajib
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Congregation for Tarawih is a communal sunnah (sunnah kifayah); missing it when others perform it loses virtue but is not sinful.

Recommended Sitting in Tarawih
Ruling on sitting between tarwihas and its basis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sitting between tarwihas and explain the preferred practice.

Core Idea
Sitting between tarwihas is mustahabb, not wajib; its duration and manner follow Prophetic practice and local custom.

Tarawih prayer includes rest periods between sets of rak'ahs. The Hanafi school details what is recommended during these breaks. This lesson focuses on the ruling for sitting between tarwihas, its duration, and the preferences of early Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act in question is sitting between sets of Tarawih (tarwihas). Determine what the text says about it.
The text mentions sitting between two tarwihas and between the fifth and witr.
2
Determine the hukm level
Identify the legal ruling: fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, etc. The text uses 'mustahabb'.
Mustahabb means recommended, not obligatory.
3
Find the recommended duration
The text states the sitting should be for the measure of a tarwiha (four rak'ahs). This is the recommended length.
Some opinions suggest shorter rests; the Hanafi school prefers this duration.
4
Note the basis of the ruling
The ruling is based on the custom (urf) of the people of Makkah and Madinah. The text explicitly mentions their practice.
This is a legitimate source of law in Hanafi fiqh when not contradicting primary texts.
5
Consider the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis prefer silent sitting, others prefer dhikr or nafl. Identify both views and the relied-upon position.
The text records the view of Ibn al-Humam (silence) and the objection of al-Khadim (active worship).

والمستحب في الجلوس بين الترويحتين مقدار الترويحة، وكذا بين الخامسة وبين الوتر لعادة اهل الحرمين، واستحسن البعض الاستراحة على خمس تسليمات، وليس بصحيح، وقوله ثم يوتر بهم يشير إلى ان وقتها بعد العشاء قبل الوتر، وبه قال عامة المشائخ والاصح ان وقتها بعد العشاء الى آخر الليل قبل الوتر ،وبعده لانها نوافل سنت بعد العشاء، ولم يذكر قدر القراءة، واكثر المشائخ على ان السنة فيها الختم مرة، فلا يترك لكسل القوم بخلاف ما بعد التشهد من الدعوات حيث يتركها، لانها ليست بسنة
ترجمہ اور دو ترویحوں کے درمیان ایک ترویحہ کی مقدار بیٹھنا مستحب ہے۔ اور یوں ہی پانچویں ترویحہ اور وتر کے درمیان بھی کیونکہ اہل حرمین کی عادت ہے۔ اور بعض نے پانچ تسلیمات پر استراحت کو مستحسن سمجھا ہے اور یہ میچ نہیں ہے اور مصنف کا قول ثم يـوتـر بهم اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے کہ تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد اور وتر سے پہلے ہے اور اس کے قائل عامتہ المشائخ ہیں اور اصح یہ ہے کہ زاویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد ہے آخر رات تک پوتر سے پہلے ہو یا بعد میں کیونکہ تراویح بھی نوافل ہیں جو عشاء کے بعد مقرر کی گئی ہے اور مصنف نے قرآت کی مقدار کو ذکر نہیں کیا اور اکثر مشائخ اس قول پر ہیں کہ تراویح میں ایک بار ختم کرنا سنت ہے پس ایک ختم قوم کی کاہلی کی وجہ سے نہ چھوڑ ا جائے۔ بخلاف التحیات کے بعد کی دعاؤں کے کہ ان کو ترک کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ وہ سنت نہیں ہیں۔
و المستحب في الجلوس ..... الخ ، اس عبارت میں بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ دوتر وبچوں کے درمیان اور پانچویں ترویحہ اور وتر کے درمیان بیٹھنا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل ، اہل حرمین یعنی اہل مکہ اور اہل مدینہ کی عادت ہے اہل مکہ دو ترویحوں کے درمیان بیت اللہ کا طواف کرتے تھے اور اہل مدینہ اس کے عوض چار رکعت نفل نماز پڑھتے تھے اور ہر شہر کے لوگوں کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ دوتر و یحوں کے درمیان تیچ کریں یا کلمہ طیبہ کا ورد کریں یا خاموشی کے ساتھ انتظار کریں۔
علامہ ابن الہمام صاحب فتح القدیر، اور صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ رہ دوتر وبچوں کے درمیان خاموشی کے ساتھ انتظار کرنا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ تراویح اور ترویحہ ، راحت سے ماخوذ ہے لہذا ایسا کام کرنے جس میں راحت پائی جائے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ راحت خاموش بیٹھے رہنے میں ہے۔ اس لئے خاموشی کے ساتھ بیٹھے رہنا اولیٰ اور مستحب ہے۔
لیکن خادم کو اس پر اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ تراویح بلا شبہ راحت سے ماخوذ ہے مگر راحت فقط دنوی ہی مطلوب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ بسا اوقات اخروی راحت بھی مطلوب ہوتی ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ اخروی راحت خاموش بیٹھنے میں نہیں ہے بلکہ نیک عمل کرنے میں ہے لہذا اس وقت میں تسبیح پڑھے یا کلمہ طیبہ کا ورد کرے یا نفل پڑھے۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم جمیل احمد
And the mustahabb in sitting between the two tarwihas is the measure of a tarwiha, and similarly between the fifth and the witr due to the custom of the people of the two sanctuaries. Some considered resting on five taslims as good, but it is not correct. And his saying 'then he leads them in witr' indicates that its time is after Isha before Witr, and that is the view of the generality of the mashayikh. The most correct is that its time is after Isha until the end of the night, whether before or after Witr, because they are nawafil prescribed after Isha. He did not mention the amount of recitation, and most mashayikh hold that the sunnah in it is to complete the Qur'an once, so it should not be left due to the laziness of the people, unlike the supplications after the tashahhud which can be left because they are not sunnah. Translation: And sitting between two tarwihas for the measure of a tarwiha is mustahabb, and similarly between the fifth and witr due to the custom of the people of the two sanctuaries. Some considered resting on five taslims as good, but it is not correct. The author's statement 'then he leads them in witr' indicates that its time is after Isha before Witr, and that is the view of most mashayikh. The most correct is that its time is after Isha until the end of the night, whether before or after Witr, because Tarawih are nawafil prescribed after Isha. The author did not mention the amount of recitation, and most mashayikh hold that the sunnah in it is to complete the Qur'an once, so it should not be left due to laziness of the people, unlike the supplications after tashahhud which can be left because they are not sunnah. And the mustahabb in sitting... the expression states that sitting between two tarwihas and between the fifth and witr is mustahabb. The proof is the custom of the people of the two sanctuaries: the people of Makkah used to circumambulate the Kaaba between two tarwihas, and the people of Madinah used to pray four rak'ahs of nafl instead. And the people of every city have the choice to make dhikr, recite the kalima, or wait in silence. Allamah Ibn al-Humam, author of Fath al-Qadir, and the author of Inayah wrote that waiting in silence between two tarwihas is mustahabb because tarwih is derived from comfort, and comfort is found in sitting silently. Therefore, sitting silently is better and mustahabb. But al-Khadim objected that tarwih is certainly derived from comfort, but comfort is not only worldly; sometimes otherworldly comfort is desired, and that comfort is not in silent sitting but in good deeds, so one should recite tasbih, kalima, or pray nafl. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a statement of rulings on recommended actions in Tarawih and its timing. It covers three topics: (1) Sitting between Tarawihs: It is mustahabb to sit for the duration of one tarwiha (four rak'ahs) between each set, and also between the fifth tarwiha and Witr, following the practice of Meccans (tawaf) and Medinans (nafl prayer). The opinion of resting after five taslims is rejected. (2) Timing of Tarawih: The preferred opinion is that Tarawih time extends from after Isha until the end of the night, whether performed before or after Witr, because Tarawih are nawafil linked to Isha. (3) Recitation: The sunnah is to complete one full recitation of the Quran during the month's Tarawih, and it should not be abandoned due to laziness. The passage also records a later objection by al-Khadim against the view that silent sitting is best, arguing that doing dhikr or nafl is more rewarding. However, the relied-upon Hanafi practice is to sit quietly or engage in tawaf or nafl prayer as per local custom.

Key Terms
ترویحہ (tarwīḥah): A set of four rak'ahs of Tarawih; also the rest period between them.
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended; not obligatory but reward-worthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The measure of two rak'ahs
C) The measure of ten minutes
D) No specific duration

Key Takeaway
Sitting between tarwihas is mustahabb for the duration of a tarwiha, based on the custom of the early Muslims, and one may spend this time in silence, dhikr, or nafl.

Timing and Recitation in Tarawih
Ruling on timing of Tarawih and sunnah of completing the Quran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the correct time for Tarawih and explain the sunnah of completing the Quran once.

Core Idea
Tarawih time extends from after Isha until the end of the night, and completing the Quran once is a sunnah that should not be neglected.

The timing of Tarawih and the practice of completing the Quran are key aspects of this prayer. This lesson clarifies the correct time window and the recommendation to complete one full recitation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time reference
Look at the author's phrase 'then he leads them in witr' which is used as an indicator. The text explains that this implies Tarawih is before witr, but the most correct view includes after witr.
The phrase is from the hadith describing the Prophet's practice.
2
Understand the preferred time
The majority of mashayikh say the time is after Isha before witr. The most correct (asah) opinion is that it extends until the end of the night, both before and after witr.
The reasoning: Tarawih are nawafil prescribed after Isha, so they can be prayed any time in the night.
3
Note the sunnah of recitation
The text says most mashayikh hold that the sunnah is to complete the Quran once during the month's Tarawih.
This should not be abandoned due to laziness of the people.
4
Distinguish from other supplications
The text contrasts with supplications after tashahhud, which are not sunnah and can be left. This highlights the importance of the khatm.
The recitation in Tarawih has a special status.

Source Text

والمستحب في الجلوس بين الترويحتين مقدار الترويحة، وكذا بين الخامسة وبين الوتر لعادة اهل الحرمين، واستحسن البعض الاستراحة على خمس تسليمات، وليس بصحيح، وقوله ثم يوتر بهم يشير إلى ان وقتها بعد العشاء قبل الوتر، وبه قال عامة المشائخ والاصح ان وقتها بعد العشاء الى آخر الليل قبل الوتر ،وبعده لانها نوافل سنت بعد العشاء، ولم يذكر قدر القراءة، واكثر المشائخ على ان السنة فيها الختم مرة، فلا يترك لكسل القوم بخلاف ما بعد التشهد من الدعوات حيث يتركها، لانها ليست بسنة
ترجمہ اور دو ترویحوں کے درمیان ایک ترویحہ کی مقدار بیٹھنا مستحب ہے۔ اور یوں ہی پانچویں ترویحہ اور وتر کے درمیان بھی کیونکہ اہل حرمین کی عادت ہے۔ اور بعض نے پانچ تسلیمات پر استراحت کو مستحسن سمجھا ہے اور یہ میچ نہیں ہے اور مصنف کا قول ثم يـوتـر بهم اس بات کی طرف اشارہ کرتا ہے کہ تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد اور وتر سے پہلے ہے اور اس کے قائل عامتہ المشائخ ہیں اور اصح یہ ہے کہ زاویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد ہے آخر رات تک پوتر سے پہلے ہو یا بعد میں کیونکہ تراویح بھی نوافل ہیں جو عشاء کے بعد مقرر کی گئی ہے اور مصنف نے قرآت کی مقدار کو ذکر نہیں کیا اور اکثر مشائخ اس قول پر ہیں کہ تراویح میں ایک بار ختم کرنا سنت ہے پس ایک ختم قوم کی کاہلی کی وجہ سے نہ چھوڑ ا جائے۔ بخلاف التحیات کے بعد کی دعاؤں کے کہ ان کو ترک کر سکتا ہے کیونکہ وہ سنت نہیں ہیں۔
و المستحب في الجلوس ..... الخ ، اس عبارت میں بیان کیا گیا ہے کہ دوتر وبچوں کے درمیان اور پانچویں ترویحہ اور وتر کے درمیان بیٹھنا مستحب ہے۔ دلیل ، اہل حرمین یعنی اہل مکہ اور اہل مدینہ کی عادت ہے اہل مکہ دو ترویحوں کے درمیان بیت اللہ کا طواف کرتے تھے اور اہل مدینہ اس کے عوض چار رکعت نفل نماز پڑھتے تھے اور ہر شہر کے لوگوں کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ دوتر و یحوں کے درمیان تیچ کریں یا کلمہ طیبہ کا ورد کریں یا خاموشی کے ساتھ انتظار کریں۔
علامہ ابن الہمام صاحب فتح القدیر، اور صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ رہ دوتر وبچوں کے درمیان خاموشی کے ساتھ انتظار کرنا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ تراویح اور ترویحہ ، راحت سے ماخوذ ہے لہذا ایسا کام کرنے جس میں راحت پائی جائے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ راحت خاموش بیٹھے رہنے میں ہے۔ اس لئے خاموشی کے ساتھ بیٹھے رہنا اولیٰ اور مستحب ہے۔
لیکن خادم کو اس پر اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ تراویح بلا شبہ راحت سے ماخوذ ہے مگر راحت فقط دنوی ہی مطلوب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ بسا اوقات اخروی راحت بھی مطلوب ہوتی ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ اخروی راحت خاموش بیٹھنے میں نہیں ہے بلکہ نیک عمل کرنے میں ہے لہذا اس وقت میں تسبیح پڑھے یا کلمہ طیبہ کا ورد کرے یا نفل پڑھے۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم جمیل احمد
And the mustahabb in sitting between the two tarwihas is the measure of a tarwiha, and similarly between the fifth and the witr due to the custom of the people of the two sanctuaries. Some considered resting on five taslims as good, but it is not correct. And his saying 'then he leads them in witr' indicates that its time is after Isha before Witr, and that is the view of the generality of the mashayikh. The most correct is that its time is after Isha until the end of the night, whether before or after Witr, because they are nawafil prescribed after Isha. He did not mention the amount of recitation, and most mashayikh hold that the sunnah in it is to complete the Qur'an once, so it should not be left due to the laziness of the people, unlike the supplications after the tashahhud which can be left because they are not sunnah. Translation: And sitting between two tarwihas for the measure of a tarwiha is mustahabb, and similarly between the fifth and witr due to the custom of the people of the two sanctuaries. Some considered resting on five taslims as good, but it is not correct. The author's statement 'then he leads them in witr' indicates that its time is after Isha before Witr, and that is the view of most mashayikh. The most correct is that its time is after Isha until the end of the night, whether before or after Witr, because Tarawih are nawafil prescribed after Isha. The author did not mention the amount of recitation, and most mashayikh hold that the sunnah in it is to complete the Qur'an once, so it should not be left due to laziness of the people, unlike the supplications after tashahhud which can be left because they are not sunnah. And the mustahabb in sitting... the expression states that sitting between two tarwihas and between the fifth and witr is mustahabb. The proof is the custom of the people of the two sanctuaries: the people of Makkah used to circumambulate the Kaaba between two tarwihas, and the people of Madinah used to pray four rak'ahs of nafl instead. And the people of every city have the choice to make dhikr, recite the kalima, or wait in silence. Allamah Ibn al-Humam, author of Fath al-Qadir, and the author of Inayah wrote that waiting in silence between two tarwihas is mustahabb because tarwih is derived from comfort, and comfort is found in sitting silently. Therefore, sitting silently is better and mustahabb. But al-Khadim objected that tarwih is certainly derived from comfort, but comfort is not only worldly; sometimes otherworldly comfort is desired, and that comfort is not in silent sitting but in good deeds, so one should recite tasbih, kalima, or pray nafl. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a statement of rulings on recommended actions in Tarawih and its timing. It covers three topics: (1) Sitting between Tarawihs: It is mustahabb to sit for the duration of one tarwiha (four rak'ahs) between each set, and also between the fifth tarwiha and Witr, following the practice of Meccans (tawaf) and Medinans (nafl prayer). The opinion of resting after five taslims is rejected. (2) Timing of Tarawih: The preferred opinion is that Tarawih time extends from after Isha until the end of the night, whether performed before or after Witr, because Tarawih are nawafil linked to Isha. (3) Recitation: The sunnah is to complete one full recitation of the Quran during the month's Tarawih, and it should not be abandoned due to laziness. The passage also records a later objection by al-Khadim against the view that silent sitting is best, arguing that doing dhikr or nafl is more rewarding. However, the relied-upon Hanafi practice is to sit quietly or engage in tawaf or nafl prayer as per local custom.

Key Terms
تراویح (tarāwīḥ): Night prayers performed in Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs in the Hanafi school.
سنة (sunnah): Prophetic practice; here, the sunnah of completing the Quran once in Tarawih.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the most correct opinion regarding the timing of Tarawih according to the passage?
A) Only before Witr
B) After Isha until the end of the night, before or after Witr
C) Only after Witr
D) Only between Maghrib and Isha

Key Takeaway
Tarawih can be prayed any time from after Isha until dawn, and completing the Quran once is a sunnah that should not be left due to laziness.

Tarawih Congregation: Communal Sunnah or Individual Obligation?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the ruling of Tarawih congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on Tarawih congregation, distinguish between sunnat ala al-kifaya and sunnat ala al-ayn, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Tarawih congregation is a communal sunnah, not an individual obligation, but abandoning it without excuse is blameworthy.

The Hanafi school has a mild internal difference on the legal status of congregating for Tarawih. While most mashayikh consider it a communal sunnah (sunnat ala al-kifaya), some scholars, including a narration from Imam Abu Yusuf, view it as individually recommended (sunnat ala al-ayn) or permit praying at home. This lesson unpacks the evidence, the rebuttal, and the practical consequences so you can correctly advise in your community.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions and their hukm levels
List the majority view (sunnat ala al-kifaya) and the minority view (sunnat ala al-ayn). Note that the first makes congregation a communal responsibility; the second makes it an individual sunnah.
The difference affects whether a person is sinful for praying alone.
2
Locate the proof for each position
The majority relies on the practice of some Sahaba (Ibn Umar, Urwah) who prayed alone. The minority relies on the hadith 'Upon you is to pray in your homes except the obligatory.'
Both proofs are from the Sunnah, but they lead to different interpretations.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
The commentator argues that Tarawih is exempted from the general command to pray at home because the Prophet himself prayed it in congregation and the Caliphs continued it.
The response uses the Prophet's own practice to qualify the general hadith.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference)
Under the majority view, if some establish congregation, others can pray alone without sin. Under the minority view, each individual must join or be sinful for abandoning a sunnah.
This directly impacts fatwa and community practice.
5
Identify the mufta bihi and why
The mufta bihi is the majority view (sunnat ala al-kifaya) because it aligns with the consistent practice of the early community and is supported by stronger evidence.
This is the relied-upon position in fatwa today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب النوافل
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم تشریح صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ اکثر مشائخ کے نزدیک تراویح کی جماعت سنت علی الکفایہ ہے چنانچہ ایک مسجد سے متعلق تمام لوگوں نے اگر جماعت تراویح کو ترک کر دیا تو سب گنہگار ہوں گے اور اگر بعض نے جماعت کو قائم کیا اور بعض نے ترک کر دیا تو جماعت میں شریک نہ ہونے والے تارک فضیلت ہوں گے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ بعض صحابہ ایسے ہیں جن سے تراویح کی جماعت میں شریک نہ ہونا مروی ہے۔ یعنی یہ حضرات صحابہ جماعت میں شریک نہیں ہوئے بلکہ تنہا پڑھی ہے۔ چنانچہ امام طحاوی نے ابن عمر اور عروہ سے اس کو روایت کیا ہے۔ بعض علماء نے تراویح کی جماعت کو سنت علی العین کہا ہے۔ لہذا ان کے نزدیک اگر کوئی شخص تنہا تر اویح کی نماز ادا کرے تو ترک سنت کی وجہ سے گنہ گار ہو گا امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے کہ اگر سنت قرآت کی رعایت کرتے ہوئے گھر میں تراویح پڑھنا ممکن ہو تو جائز ہے کہ وہ گھر میں اکیلا تراویح کی نماز پڑھتے لیکن اگر کوئی شخص فقیہ کبیر ہو جس کے عمل کی لوگ اقتداء کرتے ہیں تو یہ فقیہ کبیر گھر میں تراویح ادا نہ کرے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل حضور گاہ یہ قول ہے عليكم بالصلوة في بيوتكم فان خير صلوة المرد في بيته الا المكتوبة یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم پر اپنے گھر میں نماز پڑھنا لازم ہے کیونکہ آدمی کی بہترین نماز اس کے گھر میں ہے علاوہ فرض نماز کے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ قیام رمضان اس حکم سے مستفی ہے کیونکہ پہلے معلوم ہو چکا کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے مسجد میں آکر تراویح کی نماز ادا کی ہے اور جب تشریف نہیں لائے تو اس کا عذر بیان فرمایا اور خلفاء راشدین کا عمل بھی یہی رہا ہے کہ تاراویح کی نماز با جماعت مسجد میں ادا کی ہے اس لئے بلا عذر تراویح کی جماعت چھوڑنے کی اجازت نہیں دی جائے گی۔
Chapter of Nawafil. Commentary on Al-Hidayah: The author of Al-Hidayah said that according to most mashayikh, the congregation for Tarawih is sunnat ala al-kifaya. Thus if all people of a mosque abandon the congregation for Tarawih, they all become sinful; if some establish it and some abandon it, those who do not join are merely abandoners of virtue. The proof is that there are some Sahaba from whom it is narrated that they did not join the congregation for Tarawih; rather they prayed alone. Imam al-Tahawi narrated this from Ibn Umar and Urwah. Some scholars said that the congregation for Tarawih is sunnat ala al-ayn, so if someone prays Tarawih alone, he is sinful for abandoning the sunnah. It is narrated from Imam Abu Yusuf that if it is possible to pray Tarawih at home while observing the sunnah recitation, it is permissible, but if a person is a great scholar whom people follow, he should not pray at home. Imam Abu Yusuf's evidence is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Upon you is to pray in your homes, for the best prayer of a person is in his home except the obligatory prayer.' Our response is that Qiyam Ramadan is exempted from this ruling because the Prophet (peace be upon him) came to the mosque and prayed Tarawih, and when he did not come, he gave an excuse. The practice of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was also to pray Tarawih in congregation in the mosque. Therefore, without an excuse, one is not permitted to abandon the congregation for Tarawih.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the legal ruling on performing Tarawih in congregation. The author states the position of the majority of mashayikh: it is sunnat ala al-kifaya (a communal sunnah). If everyone in a locality abandons it, all are sinful. But if some establish it, others are not sinful for not joining, though they miss virtue. The proof is that some Companions, like Ibn Umar and Urwah, prayed Tarawih alone at home, not in congregation. This shows it is not individually obligatory. However, some scholars said it is sunnat ala al-ayn (individually sunnah), meaning leaving it without excuse is sinful. Imam Abu Yusuf allowed praying at home if one can maintain the sunnah recitation, but a leading scholar should pray in congregation. His proof is the hadith that the best prayer is in one's home except the obligatory. The commentator responds that Tarawih is exempted because the Prophet himself prayed it in congregation and the Caliphs continued that practice. Therefore, without excuse, leaving the congregation is not allowed. The mufta bihi is the majority view: congregation is sunnat ala al-kifaya.

Key Terms
جماعة التراويح (jamā'at al-tarāwīḥ): Performing the Tarawih prayer in congregation behind an imam in the mosque.
سنت علی الکفایہ (sunnat ʿalā al-kifāyah): A communal sunnah: if some people in a community perform it, the obligation is fulfilled for all; if none do, all are sinful.
سنت علی العین (sunnat ʿalā al-ʿayn): An individually recommended sunnah; leaving it without excuse is makruh but not sinful according to majority.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars, what is the ruling on performing Tarawih in congregation?
A) It is fard al-ayn on every Muslim.
B) It is sunnat ala al-kifaya (communal sunnah).
C) It is makruh to perform in congregation.
D) It is haram to perform in congregation.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih congregation is a communal sunnah: if the community establishes it, individuals are not sinful for praying alone, but abandoning it collectively is sinful.

The Recommended Pause Between Tarawih Cycles
Critical refinement of a textual imprecision and clarification of the recommended act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended action between Tarawih cycles according to the Hanafi school, explain the proof from the practice of Ahl al-Haramayn, and identify the textual imprecision in Al-Hidayah's phrasing.

Core Idea
The recommended act between Tarawih cycles is waiting (intizar), not necessarily sitting; any act of worship fulfills it.

In this passage, the commentator Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a common misunderstanding regarding the pause between Tarawih cycles. While the matn of Al-Hidayah states that 'sitting' is recommended, the commentator shows that the actual practice of the people of Makkah and Madinah was to engage in worship—Tawaf or prayer—and therefore the essence is waiting, not merely sitting. This lesson traces the proof, the internal Hanafi discussion, and the critical refinement of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? Between tarwihahs (units of 4 rak'ahs) and before Witr. The ruling according to the Hanafi school is that waiting (intizar) is mustahab (recommended).
The original matn says 'sitting' but the commentator corrects to 'waiting'.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the practice of the people of the Two Sanctuaries (Ahl al-Haramayn: Makkah and Madinah). Their habit during the pause was to perform Tawaf (Makkah) or offer nafl prayer (Madinah).
This is a transmitted practice ('urf), not a hadith text.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this practice prove the ruling? The people of Makkah and Madinah did not merely sit; they engaged in active worship. Therefore, the sunnah is waiting (intizar), which can be fulfilled by any virtuous act, not necessarily sitting.
The commentator argues that the evidence shows waiting, not sitting specifically.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Ibn al-Humam and the author of al-'Inayah favor silent waiting, arguing that Tarawih derives from rest (rahat). Al-Khadim objects that spiritual rest comes from worship, not silence.
Both views are based on the same root word but different emphases.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The commentator sides with the practice of Ahl al-Haramayn over linguistic derivation. He refines the matn to read 'al-mustahabbu fi al-intizar' (recommended is waiting) rather than 'fi al-julus' (sitting), and allows any worship.
The mufta bihi is flexible: waiting for the duration of a tarwihah, engaging in any supererogatory act.

علامہ ابن الہمام صاحب فتح القدیر، اور صاحب عنایہ نے تحریر کیا ہے کہ رہ دوتر وبچوں کے درمیان خاموشی کے ساتھ انتظار کرنا مستحب ہے۔ کیونکہ تراویح اور ترویحہ ، راحت سے ماخوذ ہے لہذا ایسا کام کرنے جس میں راحت پائی جائے اور یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ راحت خاموش بیٹھے رہنے میں ہے۔ اس لئے خاموشی کے ساتھ بیٹھے رہنا اولیٰ اور مستحب ہے۔
لیکن خادم کو اس پر اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ تراویح بلا شبہ راحت سے ماخوذ ہے مگر راحت فقط دنوی ہی مطلوب نہیں ہوتی بلکہ بسا اوقات اخروی راحت بھی مطلوب ہوتی ہے اور یہ ظاہر ہے کہ اخروی راحت خاموش بیٹھنے میں نہیں ہے بلکہ نیک عمل کرنے میں ہے لہذا اس وقت میں تسبیح پڑھے یا کلمہ طیبہ کا ورد کرے یا نفل پڑھے۔ واللہ تعالیٰ اعلم جمیل احمد
بعض حضرات نے پانچ سلاموں یعنی نصف تراویح پر استراحت کو مستحسن کہا ہے لیکن یہ قول صحیح نہیں ہے۔
یہ بات ذہن نشین رہے کہ صاحب ہدایہ کی عبارت والمستحب في الجلوس میں قدرے تسامح ہے کیونکہ عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دوتر وبیجوں کے درمیان بیٹھنا مستحب ہے اور دلیل میں اہل حرمین کی عادت کو پیش کیا ہے۔ اور اہل حرمین کی عادت یہ تھی کہ اہل مکہ طواف کرتے تھے اور اہل مدینہ نماز پڑھتے تھے۔ پس معلوم ہوا کہ ان حضرات کی عادت بیٹھنے کی نہ تھی بلکہ انتظار کرنے کی تھی، انتظار بیٹھ ک ہو یا بغیر بیٹھے ہو۔ اس لئے مناسب یہ تھا کہ یوں کہتے ۔ والمستحب في الانظار بين الترويحتين مقدار الترويحة . (عنایه، فتح القدیر، کنایه )
And the recommended in sitting etc. In this expression it is stated that sitting between two tarwihahs and between the fifth tarwihah and Witr is mustahab. The proof is the practice of the people of the Two Sanctuaries (Makkah and Madinah). The people of Makkah used to perform Tawaf of the Ka'bah between two tarwihahs, and the people of Madinah used to pray four rak'ahs of nafl in its place. The people of every city have the choice to recite takbir or kalimah tayyibah or wait in silence. Allamah Ibn al-Humam (author of Fath al-Qadir) and the author of Al-'Inayah wrote that to wait in silence between two tarwihahs is mustahab because Tarawih is derived from rest (rahat). Therefore an action in which rest is found is appropriate, and rest is clearly in sitting silently. So sitting silently is superior and mustahab. However, al-Khadim has an objection: Tarawih is indeed derived from rest, but rest is not only worldly; sometimes spiritual rest is desired, and spiritual rest is not in silent sitting but in performing good deeds. So one should recite tasbih or kalimah or offer nafl during that time. And Allah knows best. Some people considered resting after five salam (half of Tarawih) as good, but this statement is not correct. It should be kept in mind that the author of Al-Hidayah's expression 'wa al-mustahabbu fi al-julus' has some imprecision, because from the expression it seems sitting between two tarwihahs is mustahab, and the evidence is the practice of the people of the Two Sanctuaries. Their practice was that the people of Makkah performed Tawaf and the people of Madinah prayed. So it is known that their practice was not sitting but waiting, whether sitting or not. Therefore it would have been appropriate to say: 'wa al-mustahabbu fi al-intizar bayna al-tarwihatai miqdara al-tarwihah.' (Al-'Inayah, Fath al-Qadir, Kanz al-Daqa'iq).
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the recommended act between the Tarawih cycles (tarwihahs). The author of Hidayah originally stated that sitting (julus) is mustahab. The commentator clarifies that the evidence is the practice of the people of Makkah and Madinah. However, they did not merely sit; they engaged in Tawaf or prayer. Therefore, the essence is waiting (intizar), not necessarily sitting. Ibn al-Humam and the author of Al-'Inayah favored silent waiting, but al-Khadim objects that spiritual benefit comes from dhikr or prayer, not merely silence. The commentator also notes that the phrasing of the Hidayah should be corrected to 'al-mustahabbu fi al-intizar' (waiting) rather than 'al-julus' (sitting). The preferred view is that one may engage in any supererogatory act of worship during the pause, but waiting is recommended.

Key Terms
ترویحہ (tarwīḥah): A unit of four rak'ahs of Tarawih; the pause between two such units.
استراحت (istirāḥah): Taking rest; here referring to a longer break after half the Tarawih (after 5 salams).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator in Ashraf al-Hidayah, what is the more precise description of the recommended action between Tarawih cycles?
A) Sitting quietly.
B) Performing Tawaf.
C) Waiting (intizar), whether sitting or not.
D) Reciting the entire Quran.

Key Takeaway
The recommended act between Tarawih cycles is waiting (intizar) of approximately the duration of a tarwihah; any supererogatory worship is permissible, and the textual phrasing 'sitting' is imprecise.

Time for Tarawih Prayer
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Tarawih time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the time of Tarawih, identify the most correct (asahh) view, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
Tarawih time extends from after Isha until the end of the night, before or after Witr; delaying to the last third is more virtuous.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah examines the time for Tarawih prayer, presenting three views within the Hanafi school: the majority view of the early mashayikh, the later Balkh scholars' broader view, and the preferred asahh qawl. Understanding this dispute helps us correctly observe Tarawih in Ramadan and avoid common misconceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three Hanafi views
Read the passage and list the three positions: (1) early mashayikh: after Isha before Witr only; (2) later Balkh scholars: entire night (before and after Isha); (3) asahh qawl: after Isha until end of night, before or after Witr.
The asahh qawl is attributed to the commentator of Ashraf al-Hidayah.
2
Analyze the proof for each view
For each view, find the dalil cited: early mashayikh rely on the practice of the Sahaba; Balkh scholars argue Tarawih is qiyam al-layl, so its time is the whole night; the asahh qawl combines subordination to Isha with the virtue of the last part of the night.
Note that the passage uses 'Qiyam al-layl' as a key term.
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Determine the practical consequence: under the early view, Tarawih before Isha or after Witr is invalid; under the Balkh view, any time at night is valid; under the asahh qawl, it must be after Isha but can be before or after Witr, and delaying to the end of the night is mustahab.
4
Examine the tarjih reasoning
The commentator declares the asahh qawl as the most correct. He refutes the claim that Tarawih after midnight is makruh by citing that night prayer (qiyam al-layl) is best at the end of the night.
5
Apply the mufta bihi ruling
State the operative ruling: Tarawih time is from after Isha until the end of the night; it is valid before or after Witr; delaying to the last third is mustahab, not makruh.
This is the position for fatwa according to Ashraf al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و قوله ثم يوتر بهم الخ ، اس عابرت میں تراویح کا وقت بیان کیا گیا ہے۔ چنا نچہ فرمایا کہ تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد اور روتر سے پہلے ہے۔ عامۃ المشائخ اسی کے قائل ہیں ۔ حتی کہ اگر عشاء سے پہلے یا وتر کے بعد تراویح کی نماز پڑھی تو وہ تراویح نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ زادی کا علم صحابہ کے فعل سے ہوا ہے لہذا صحابہ نے جس وقت میں تراویح کی نماز پڑھی ہے وہی تراویح کا وقت ہوگا۔ اور یہ بات مسلم ہے کہ صحابہ نے عشاء کے بعد اور وتر سے پہلے تراویح کی نماز پڑھی ہے لہذا تراویح کا یہی وقت مشروع ہوگا۔ اور متاخرین مشائخ بلخ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ پوری رات صبح صادق تک تراویح کا وقت ہے عشاء سے پہلے بھی اور عشاء کے بعد بھی کیونکہ نماز تراویح کا نام قیام لیل ہے۔ پس اس کا وقت بھی لیل یعنی رات ہوگی۔
اصح قول یہ ہے کہ تراویح کا وقت عشاء کے بعد سے آخر رات تک ہے وتر سے پہلے بھی اور وتر کے بعد بھی ۔ کیونکہ تراویح نوافل میں جوعشاء کے بعد مقرر کئے گئے ہیں۔ پس تراویح کی نماز عشاء کی نماز کے تابع ہوئی اور تابع ممتبوع سے بعد ہوتا ہے لہذا تراویح کی نماز عشاء کے بعد ہوگی نہ کہ پہلے اور تراویح کو تہائی رات تک مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے بعض نے کہا کہ نصف رات تک مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے لیکن اگر آدھی رات کے بعد تراویح پڑھی تو بعض کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے کیونکہ تراویح عشاء کے تابع ہے۔ اور عشاء کو آدھی رات کے بعد ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے لہذا تراویح بھی آدھی رات کے بعد مکروہ ہوگی اور صحیح قول یہ ہے کہ آدھی رات کے بعد مکروہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ تراویح صلوۃ لیل ہے اور صلوۃ لیل میں آخر رات افضل ہے لہذا اتر اویج میں آخر رات تک تاخیر افضل ہے نہ کہ مکروہ ۔
And his statement 'then he leads them in Witr' etc. In this expression the time of Tarawih is stated. He said: The time of Tarawih is after Isha and before Witr. The majority of scholars (ummat al-mashayikh) hold this view. Even if one prays Tarawih before Isha or after Witr, it will not be considered Tarawih. Because knowledge of this is derived from the practice of the Sahaba; the time they prayed Tarawih is the time of Tarawih. It is agreed that the Sahaba prayed Tarawih after Isha and before Witr, so this time is prescribed. The later scholars of Balkh hold that the entire night until true dawn is the time for Tarawih, both before Isha and after Isha, because Tarawih is called qiyam al-layl, so its time is the night. The most correct view is that the time for Tarawih is after Isha until the end of the night, both before Witr and after Witr. Because Tarawih is among the nawafil prescribed after Isha; thus Tarawih prayer is subordinate to Isha, and the subordinate comes after the primary. So Tarawih will be after Isha, not before. It is mustahab to delay Tarawih until the last third of the night. Some said delaying until midnight is mustahab. But if one prays Tarawih after midnight, some consider it makruh because Tarawih is subordinate to Isha, and it is makruh to pray Isha after midnight. However, the correct view is that it is not makruh after midnight, because Tarawih is the prayer of the night, and the best time for night prayer is the end of the night. So delaying Tarawih until the end of the night is better, not makruh.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the time for Tarawih. The author of Hidayah states the view of the majority of mashayikh: Tarawih time is after Isha and before Witr, based on the practice of the Sahaba. The later scholars of Balkh said the whole night (from maghrib? Actually it says 'puri raat subh sadiq tak' meaning from night onset to dawn) is time, both before and after Isha, because Tarawih is qiyam al-layl. The commentator then gives the 'asahh qawl' (most correct view): Tarawih time is after Isha until the end of the night, whether before or after Witr. This is because Tarawih is a nafl attached to Isha, so it follows Isha. However, it is mustahab to delay until the last third of the night. Some scholars said delaying until midnight is mustahab, and some said after midnight is makruh. The correct view is that it is not makruh; rather the end of the night is more virtuous because Tarawih is a night prayer.

Key Terms
قیام لیل (qiyām al-layl): Night vigil prayer; Tarawih is considered qiyam al-layl in Ramadan.
تابع (tābiʿ): Subordinate; Tarawih is subordinate to Isha in time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the most correct view (asahh qawl) in Ashraf al-Hidayah, what is the time for Tarawih?
A) Only after Isha and before Witr.
B) After Isha until the end of the night, both before and after Witr.
C) The entire night including before Isha.
D) Only the last third of the night.

Key Takeaway
Tarawih time is after Isha until dawn, and it is valid whether prayed before or after Witr; delaying to the last third is more virtuous and not makruh.

The Recommended Recitation in Tarawih: Ten Verses per Rak'ah
Discussion of the recommended amount of Quranic recitation per rak'ah in Tarawih

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the amount of recitation per rak'ah in Tarawih and explain why the analogy to Maghrib is rejected.

Core Idea
Ten verses per rak'ah ensures completing the Quran once in Tarawih, which is sunnah.

The amount of Quranic recitation in Tarawih is not specified in the early matn, leading to differing opinions. Some scholars analogized Tarawih to the lightest fard (Maghrib), while others preferred a longer recitation to achieve the sunnah of completing the Quran once in Ramadan. This lesson examines the evidence and the Hanafi position established by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The matn did not specify the quantity of recitation per rak'ah in Tarawih. This created a need for ijtihad.
2
Examine the first analogy (to Maghrib)
Some scholars analogized Tarawih to Maghrib because both are prayers and Tarawih is nafl, which is lighter. They suggested reciting a short amount similar to Maghrib.
This qiyas is mentioned but rejected.
3
Understand the refutation
The analogy to Maghrib would prevent completing the Quran once in Ramadan, which is a sunnah. Hence, it is not acceptable.
The goal of completing the Quran (khatm) is a key proof.
4
Present the Hanafi position
Imam Abu Hanifa, as narrated by Hasan ibn Ziyad, prescribed ten verses per rak'ah. This allows for one complete recitation of the Quran in the 200 rak'ahs of Tarawih.
This is the mufta bihi position.
5
Note the additional virtue
Completing the Quran twice is considered more virtuous, but the minimum sunnah is once.
Mentioned in Al-Kifayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لم يذكر قدر القرأة الخ ، صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ ماتن نے یہ بیان نہیں کیا کہ تراویح کی بیس رکعات میں کتنا قرآن پڑھے۔ سو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے۔ بعض لوگوں نے کہا کہ تراویح کے ہر شع میں اتنی مقدار قرأت کرے جتنی کہ مغرب کی نماز میں قرآت کرتا ہے کیونکہ تراویح کی نماز نفل ہے اور نفل یہ نسبت فرض کے اخف ہوتا ہے لہذا مقدار قرأت میں تراویح کو اخف المکتوبات پر قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ اور اخف المکتوبات مغرب کی نماز ہے لیکن یہ قول صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ اس مقدار سے پورے ماہ مبارک کی تراویح میں ایک ختم نہیں ہو سکے گا۔ حالانکہ تراویح میں ایک مرتبہ کلام پاک ختم کرنا سنت ہے۔ بعض نے کہا کہ تراویح کے ہر شفع میں اس قدر قرآت کرے جس قدر کہ عشاء میں کرتا ہے کیونکہ تراویح عشاء کے تابع ہے۔ حسن بن زیاد نے امام اعظم سے روایت کی ہے کہ ہر رکعت میں دس آیات کی مقدار قرآت کرے۔ یہی صحیح ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں لوگوں پر آسمانی بھی ہے اور ختم قرآن کی سنت بھی ادا ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ میں راتوں میں تراویح کی چھ سور کعات ہوتی ہیں اور قرآن پاک کی کل آیات چھ ہزار کچھ ہیں پس جب ہر رکعت میں دس آیات تلاوت کرے گا تو تراویح میں پورا قرآن ایک بار ختم ہو جائے گا اور یہی مسنون بھی ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ بھی یہی کہتے ہیں کہ تراویح میں ایک بار ختم کلام پاک مسنون ہے۔ حتی کہ اگر لوگ مستی کرنے لگیں تو اس سنت کو ترک نہ کیا جائے۔ کفایہ میں مرقوم ہے کہ دو بار ختم کرنا افضل ہے۔ اور مجتہدین امت ایک عشرہ میں ایک ختم کرتے تھے اور امام الہما مقدوۃ الا نام امام ربانی حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ ماہ رمضان میں اکٹھے کلام پاک ختم فرماتے تھے۔ تمہیں رمضان کی راتوں میں اور تمہیں دن کے اجالوں میں ور
And he did not mention the amount of recitation etc. The author of Al-Hidayah said that the Matn did not state how much Quran to recite in the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih. Therefore there is disagreement. Some said that in each shaf' of Tarawih one should recite as much as one recites in Maghrib prayer, because Tarawih is nafl and nafl is lighter than fard, so in the amount of recitation Tarawih is measured by the lightest of the obligatory prayers, which is Maghrib. But this statement is not correct, because with this amount one cannot complete one full recitation of the Quran in the entire month of Ramadan, whereas completing the Quran once in Tarawih is sunnah. Some said that in each shaf' of Tarawih one should recite as much as in Isha because Tarawih is subordinate to Isha. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that one should recite ten verses per rak'ah. This is correct, because in this way the people will have ease and the sunnah of completing the Quran will be fulfilled. Since Tarawih has 200 rak'ahs in the nights of Ramadan and the total verses of the Quran are a little over six thousand, when one recites ten verses per rak'ah, the entire Quran will be completed once in Tarawih, and this is what is sunnah. The author of Al-Hidayah also says that completing the Quran once in Tarawih is sunnah. Even if people become lazy, this sunnah should not be abandoned. In Kifayah it is recorded that completing it twice is more virtuous. The mujtahids of the Ummah used to complete the Quran once in ten days, and the great Imam Abu Hanifa used to complete the Quran in Ramadan both in the nights and in the days.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses how much Quran should be recited in the Tarawih prayer. The author notes that the original matn did not specify the amount. Some scholars analogized Tarawih to Maghrib because it is the lightest obligatory prayer, but that would not allow a complete recitation of the Quran in Ramadan, which is a sunnah. Others analogized to Isha because Tarawih follows Isha. The correct view is narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa by Hasan ibn Ziyad: ten verses per rak'ah. This allows for one complete recitation of the Quran in the 200 rak'ahs of Tarawih over the month. The author of Hidayah supports this, and it is considered sunnah to complete the Quran once. Some say twice is more virtuous. The commentator mentions that Imam Abu Hanifa himself used to complete the Quran in Ramadan in both night and day prayers.

Key Terms
شفع (shafʿ): A pair of rak'ahs in Tarawih (i.e., a set of two rak'ahs).
ختم قرآن (khatm al-Qur'ān): Completing the recitation of the entire Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the recommended amount of recitation per rak'ah in Tarawih according to Imam Abu Hanifa?
A) As much as in Maghrib.
B) As much as in Isha.
C) Ten verses.
D) One complete juz'.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends reciting ten verses per rak'ah in Tarawih to fulfill the sunnah of completing the Quran once during Ramadan.
