Time of Tarawih and Recommended Recitation Quantity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Tarawih time and recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the time of Tarawih prayer and explain the recommended quantity of Quran recitation per rak'ah to achieve one khatm.

Core Idea
Tarawih time extends from after Isha to dawn; ten verses per rak'ah completes one khatm and fulfills the sunnah.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies two disputed aspects of Tarawih: when it should be performed and how much Quran to recite. While early Hanafi scholars restricted Tarawih to before Witr, later authorities permit it throughout the night. Similarly, the quantity of recitation is settled by the transmission of Hasan ibn Ziyad that ten verses per rak'ah enables a complete khatm, which is a confirmed sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two disputed issues
Recognize that the passage addresses two separate but related questions: the valid time range for Tarawih and the recommended length of recitation per rak'ah.
The time dispute involves early mashayikh vs. later Balkh scholars; recitation dispute involves three views.
2
Analyze the first dispute: time of Tarawih
Contrast the restrictive view (after Isha before Witr, based on Companions' practice) with the expanded view (entire night, because Tarawih is qiyam al-layl). Identify the tarjih (asahh) as expanded time.
The author states 'asahh qawl' for expanded time.
3
Examine the reasoning behind the tarjih
Note that Tarawih is subordinate to Isha, so it must come after Isha, but since it is night prayer, delaying it is better, even after Witr or after half the night.
The subordination argument distinguishes Tarawih from optional prayers at other times.
4
Analyze the second dispute: recitation quantity
List the three opinions: (1) analogy to Maghrib (lightest fard), (2) analogy to Isha (due to subordination), (3) ten verses per rak'ah from Hasan ibn Ziyad. Evaluate why the first two are rejected.
The Maghrib analogy fails to achieve one khatm; the Isha analogy is insufficiently specified.
5
Confirm the recommended position and its rationale
The ten-verse view is correct because it balances ease for the congregation with the sunnah of completing one khatm over 600 rak'ahs. Note that completing one khatm is sunnah muakkadah, and twice is afdal.
The text reports that Imam Abu Hanifa himself would complete the entire Quran during Ramadan.

میں ور
Chapter of Supererogatory Prayers: ...it was, whether waiting while sitting or without sitting. Therefore it was appropriate to say: The recommended waiting between two tarawihs is the length of a tarawih. (from Inayah, Fath al-Qadir, Kinayah) And his statement 'then he leads them in Witr, etc.' In this expression the time of Tarawih is mentioned. It says: The time of Tarawih is after Isha and before Witr. The general masses of the mashayikh hold this view. So much so that if one prays Tarawih before Isha or after Witr, it will not be Tarawih. Because knowledge of it is established from the action of the Companions, so the time at which the Companions prayed Tarawih is the time. And it is agreed that the Companions prayed Tarawih after Isha and before Witr, so this time is legislated. The later mashayikh of Balkh hold that the entire night until true dawn is the time for Tarawih, before Isha and after, because the name of Tarawih prayer is qiyam al-layl, so its time is the night. The most correct view is that the time of Tarawih is from after Isha until the end of the night, both before Witr and after, because Tarawih are among the nafl established after Isha. Thus Tarawih prayer is subordinate to Isha, and the subordinate comes after the master, so Tarawih is after Isha, not before. It is recommended to delay Tarawih until one-third of the night; some said until half. But if prayed after half the night, some consider it makruh because Tarawih is subordinate to Isha and it is makruh to perform Isha after half the night. The correct view is that it is not makruh after half the night because Tarawih is salat al-layl, and for salat al-layl the end of the night is best, so delay is best, not makruh. How much Quran to recite in the twenty rak'ahs of Tarawih: The author did not mention how much Quran to recite in the twenty rak'ahs. There is disagreement. Some said: In each pair of Tarawih, recite as much as in Maghrib, because Tarawih is nafl, and nafl is lighter than fard, so analogy is made to the lightest obligatory prayer, which is Maghrib. But this is not correct because with this amount, one cannot complete the Quran in the whole month, whereas completing the Quran once in Tarawih is sunnah. Some said: Recite as much as in Isha because Tarawih is subordinate to Isha. Hasan ibn Ziyad narrated from Imam A'zam that one should recite ten verses per rak'ah. This is correct because then there is ease for the people and the sunnah of completing the Quran is fulfilled, because Tarawih in the nights amount to six hundred rak'ahs, and the total verses of the Quran are slightly more than six thousand. So if one recites ten verses per rak'ah, the entire Quran will be completed once in Tarawih, and this is the sunnah. The author of Hidayah also says that completing the Quran once in Tarawih is sunnah, so much so that even if people become negligent, this sunnah should not be abandoned. In Kifayah it is recorded that completing twice is better. The mujtahids of the ummah used to complete one khatm in each ten days, and the Imam of imams, the leader of the ummah, the Imam Rabbani, Hadrat Imam Abu Hanifa, would complete the entire Quran together in the nights of Ramadan and in the lights of the day.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the time of Tarawih prayer and the quantity of Quran recitation in each rak'ah. The author begins by noting the recommended waiting period between each pair of tarawih rak'ahs, which is the duration of one tarawih unit. Then he addresses the time of Tarawih: the majority of early mashayikh hold that it is restricted to after Isha and before Witr, based on the practice of the Companions. The later mashayikh of Balkh expand it to the entire night, considering Tarawih as qiyam al-layl. The most correct view, according to the author, is that Tarawih time extends from after Isha to the end of the night, both before and after Witr, because Tarawih is subordinate to Isha. He further discusses the recommended delay: one-third or half of the night, and refutes the opinion that it becomes makruh after half, emphasizing that the end of the night is actually better for night prayer. On recitation quantity, the author rejects the analogy to Maghrib (too little to complete one khatm) and to Isha (insufficient). He presents the report from Hasan ibn Ziyad that Imam Abu Hanifa recommended ten verses per rak'ah, which allows for one complete khatm of the Quran over the month, fulfilling the sunnah. The author affirms this as correct and notes that completing one khatm is sunnah, even if people become lazy; completing twice is considered better (afdal) according to Kifayah. The passage ends with a brief mention of the practice of the righteous predecessors, including Imam Abu Hanifa, who would complete the entire Quran during Ramadan.

Key Terms
تراویح (tarawih): Supererogatory prayers performed in congregation during the nights of Ramadan, consisting of 20 rak'ahs.
قیام لیل (qiyam al-layl): Standing in prayer at night; a general term for night prayer, which includes Tarawih as a specific form.
ختم (khatm): Complete recitation of the entire Quran from beginning to end.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what quantity of Quran recitation is recommended per rak'ah in Tarawih to allow one complete khatm?
A) The amount recited in Maghrib
B) The amount recited in Isha
C) Ten verses per rak'ah
D) One juz' per night

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Tarawih may be performed throughout the night and that reciting ten verses per rak'ah is the recommended method to complete one Quran khatm, fulfilling a confirmed sunnah.

Reciting Durud after Tashahhud: Hanafi Ruling and Precaution
Clarifies the ruling on reciting Durud after Tashahhud in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on reciting Durud after Tashahhud, explain the reason of ihtiyat (precaution), and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Core Idea
Out of caution, Hanafis recite Durud after Tashahhud because the Shafi'i school deems it obligatory.

This passage addresses a difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the recitation of Durud (salutations upon the Prophet) after the Tashahhud in prayer. While the Hanafi school does not consider it obligatory (fard), it recommends reciting it as a precautionary measure (ihtiyat) to avoid conflicting with the Shafi'i view which treats it as fard. Understanding this ruling illustrates how Hanafi jurists sometimes adopt a safer position out of deference to a valid difference of opinion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its Hanafi default ruling
The act in question is reciting Durud (salutations upon the Prophet) after the Tashahhud in the sitting position of prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, this act is not fard or wajib; the default is that it is not obligatory.
2
Recognize the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) holds that reciting Durud after Tashahhud is fard (obligatory). This is based on hadith evidence that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Do not send incomplete salutations upon me' and other narrations.
The Shafi'i school considers this a requirement for the validity of prayer.
3
Understand the Hanafi response: ihtiyat
The Hanafi school acknowledges the difference and out of caution (ihtiyat) recommends reciting Durud. Even though it is not obligatory in the Hanafi school, the safer option is to recite it to avoid potential disagreement and to ensure the prayer is free from any deficiency from the Shafi'i perspective.
This is not a concession that the Hanafi ruling is weak, but a practical application of the principle 'al-khuruj min al-khilaf mustahabb' (to exit from disagreement is recommended).
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: In the Shafi'i school, omitting Durud invalidates the prayer. In the Hanafi school, the prayer remains valid even if Durud is omitted, but it is recommended to recite it.
This affects the ruling on someone who accidentally omits Durud – in Hanafi, no sajdah al-sahw is required; in Shafi'i, the prayer must be repeated or sajdah sahwi performed.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi position
The mufta bihi (operative ruling for fatwa) in the Hanafi school is that reciting Durud after Tashahhud is mustahabb (recommended). This is the position held in later Hanafi fatwa works, as mentioned in the text.
This is a later fatwa position (fatawa mutakhkhirin) that emphasizes precaution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بخلاف ما بعد التشهد کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ اگر التحیات کے بعد کی دعائیں مقتدیوں پر گراں گذریں تو ان کو ترک کرنے میں کو مضائقہ نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ مسنون نہیں ہیں لیکن التحیات کے بعد درود کا پڑھنا مناسب ہو گا اس کو ترک نہ کرے کیونکہ درود کا پڑھنا شافعی کے نزدیک فرض ہے پس ہمارے نزدیک بھی احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ اس کو پڑھے۔
In contrast to what is after Tashahhud, the gist is that if the supplications after Tashahhud are burdensome upon the followers, there is no harm in leaving them because they are not sunnah. However, reciting Durud after Tashahhud is appropriate and should not be omitted, because reciting Durud is fard in the view of Shafi'i, so according to us the precaution is to recite it.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding post-Tashahhud recitations. The author explains that the various du'as (supplications) recited after the Tashahhud in prayer are not sunnah; therefore, if they are difficult for the congregation, they can be omitted without issue. However, the recitation of the Durud (salutation upon the Prophet) is different: the Shafi'i school considers it fard (obligatory). Out of caution (ihtiyat), the Hanafi school recommends reciting it even though it is not obligatory in the Hanafi school. This reflects a principle of preferring the safer option (ihtiyat) when there is a difference of opinion.

Key Terms
التحیات (al-tahiyyat): The Tashahhud, the salutation recited in the sitting position of prayer.
درود (durud): Salutations upon the Prophet Muhammad, recited after Tashahhud.
مسنون (masnun): That which is established as sunnah; recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is reciting Durud after Tashahhud recommended?
A) Because it is explicitly commanded in the Quran
B) Out of precaution (ihtiyat) because the Shafi'i school considers it fard
C) Because it is necessary to complete the prayer
D) Because it is a sunnah that cannot be omitted

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends reciting Durud after Tashahhud as a precautionary measure (ihtiyat) due to the Shafi'i view considering it fard, while maintaining that it is not obligatory in the Hanafi school.

Witr Congregation Outside Ramadan: Ruling and Proof
States the ruling on Witr congregation outside Ramadan with ijma proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on praying Witr in congregation outside Ramadan, identify the proof (ijma), and explain the intra-Hanafi difference concerning Ramadan.

Core Idea
Outside Ramadan, Witr in congregation is makruh and not legislated; within Ramadan, permissible but scholars differ on preference.

This passage addresses a common question about the Witr prayer: can it be performed in congregation outside of Ramadan? The text provides a clear ruling based on the consensus of the Muslim community. It also touches on the special dispensation during Ramadan, where two scholarly opinions exist on whether congregation is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
The act is praying Witr (the odd-numbered night prayer) in congregation. The ruling outside Ramadan is that it is not legislated, and doing so is makruh (disliked).
The text states: 'ولا يصلى الوتر بجماعة في غير شهر رمضان' — 'Witr is not prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan.'
2
Locate the Dalil (Proof)
The proof cited is ijma (consensus of the Muslim scholars). The phrase 'عليه اجماع المسلمين' (upon it is the consensus of the Muslims) indicates unanimous agreement.
In Hanafi Usul, ijma is a binding source. Here it confirms the ruling.
3
Understand the Reasoning
The text explains that Witr is considered nafl from one aspect (min wajh) because it is not fard. Praying nafl in congregation outside Ramadan is makruh, so Witr follows the same rule.
This reasoning connects the ruling to general principles about supererogatory prayers.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf for Ramadan
Within Ramadan, the ruling changes: it is not makruh, but scholars differ on whether congregation is better. Ibn al-Humam favored congregation (following Umar), while Abu Ali Nasafi reports that the majority of Hanafi scholars prefer individual prayer (following Ubayy ibn Ka'b).
The text does not definitively choose, leaving it as a valid difference within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير رمضان میں وتر کی جماعت کا حکم
ولا يصلى الوتر بجماعة في غير شهر رمضان عليه اجماع المسلمين - والله اعلم
ترجمہ اور وتر کو جماعت کے ساتھ رمضان المبارک کے علاوہ میں نہ پڑھے۔ اسی پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع ہے۔
تشریح رمضان المبارک کے علاوہ دوسرے مہینوں میں وتر جماعت کے ساتھ مشروع نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وتر من وجہ نفل ہے۔ رمضان کے علاوہ میں نفل کو باجماعت پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ پس احتیاط اسی میں ہے کہ رمضان کے علاوہ میں وتر کو جماعت کے ساتھ نہ پڑا جائے ۔ اسی پر مسلمانوں کا اجماع ہے البتہ رمضان المبارک میں وتر کو باجماعت پڑھنا مکروہ نہیں ہے لیکن افضلیت میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ علامہ ابن الہمام نے کہا کہ رمضان کے مہینے میں وتر کو باجماعت پڑھنا افضل ہے کیونکہ حضرت عمر وتر کو با جماعت پڑھاتے تھے؟ ابو علی نسفی نے ذکر کیا ہے۔ ہمارے علماء کے نزدیک جماعت کے ساتھ نہ پڑھنا افضل ہے۔ کیونکہ حضرت ابی بن کعب وتر کی نماز با جماعت نہیں پڑھاتے تھے۔ واللہ اعلم جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
Ruling on Witr congregation outside Ramadan: And Witr is not prayed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan; upon it is the consensus of the Muslims - and Allah knows best. Translation: And do not pray Witr with congregation except in Ramadan. Upon this is the consensus of the Muslims. Explanation: In months other than Ramadan, Witr in congregation is not legislated because Witr is, from one aspect, nafl. Praying nafl with congregation outside Ramadan is makruh. So caution is that Witr should not be prayed with congregation outside Ramadan. Upon this is the consensus of the Muslims. However, in Ramadan, praying Witr with congregation is not makruh, but there is a difference of opinion regarding which is better. Allamah Ibn al-Humam said that praying Witr with congregation in Ramadan is better because Hadrat Umar used to lead Witr in congregation. Abu Ali Nasafi mentioned that according to our scholars, not praying with congregation is better because Hadrat Ubayy ibn Ka'b did not lead Witr in congregation. And Allah knows best. Jamil Ahmad, may he be forgiven.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof, specifically an ijma (consensus) proof. The text begins by stating the ruling that Witr prayer should not be performed in congregation outside the month of Ramadan, and this is supported by the consensus of the Muslim community. The explanation then clarifies the basis: Witr is considered nafl (supererogatory) in some respects, and praying nafl in congregation outside Ramadan is makruh (disliked). Therefore, caution dictates that Witr be prayed individually during non-Ramadan months. Within Ramadan, the ruling changes: it is not makruh to pray Witr in congregation, but the scholars differ on whether it is better to pray with congregation or individually. Two opinions are cited: Ibn al-Humam favors congregation (based on the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab), while Abu Ali Nasafi reports that the preferred view of the Hanafi scholars is to pray individually (based on the practice of Ubayy ibn Ka'b). The text does not decisively choose, ending with 'And Allah knows best'.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The odd-numbered prayer (usually 3 rak'ahs) performed after Isha, emphasized during Ramadan.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer; Witr is considered nafl min wajh (from one aspect) because it is not fard.
اجماع (ijma): Consensus of the Muslim scholars, considered a binding proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on praying Witr in congregation outside the month of Ramadan?
A) It is sunnah muakkadah
B) It is makruh and not legislated
C) It is permissible but not recommended
D) It is wajib

Key Takeaway
Outside Ramadan, Witr should be prayed individually; it is makruh to pray it in congregation. In Ramadan, congregational Witr is permissible, but individual prayer is preferred by many Hanafi scholars.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on One Who Has Prayed One Rak'ah of Zuhr When Congregation Begins
Ruling on completing individual fard prayer when congregation starts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has prayed one rak'ah of a fard prayer individually when the congregation starts, and explain the reasoning based on preservation of the performed act (siyanatan lil-mu'addi an al-butlan).

Core Idea
One rak'ah alone is invalid; complete a second to save it, then join the congregation for reward.

Imagine you start praying Zuhr alone, finish one rak'ah with prostration, and then hear the iqamah. Should you cut immediately or continue? The Hanafi school provides a detailed answer: you must complete a second rak'ah to preserve the validity of the first, then join the congregation. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type and current state
Recognize that the prayer is a fard (obligatory) and that only one rak'ah has been prayed with prostration (sajdah). The minimum for a valid fard is two rak'ahs.
If the prostration of the first rak'ah has not been performed, the ruling changes (see step 4).
2
Apply the principle of preservation (siyanatan lil-mu'addi)
The first rak'ah, if left alone, would be invalid because a fard prayer must consist of at least two rak'ahs. To 'save' the performed portion from being wasted, you must complete a second rak'ah.
This principle prioritizes preserving what has been done over immediate cut-off.
3
Complete two rak'ahs then join the congregation
After completing the second rak'ah, the prayer is valid as a two-rak'ah fard (e.g., for travelers or as a unit that can be completed by joining later). Then enter the congregation for the remaining rak'ahs.
Joining after completing two rak'ahs allows you to gain the virtue of congregation without nullifying your first rak'ah.
4
Exception: if prostration of first rak'ah is incomplete
If you have not yet performed the sajdah (prostration) of the first rak'ah, then cut immediately and join the Imam from the beginning. This is because the first rak'ah is not yet 'tied' (muqayyad) to the prayer, making cutting easier.
This is declared 'huwa al-sahih' (the correct view) by the author.

Source Text

باب ادراك الفريضة
ترجمہ (بی) باب فریضہ پانے (کے بیان ) میں ہے۔
تشریح گذشتہ ابواب میں فرائض، واجبات اور نوافل کا بیان تھا اب اس باب کے اندر اداے کامل کے معنی با جماعت نماز ادا کرنے
بیان ہے۔
سنت پڑھنے کے دوران فرائض کی جماعت شروع ہو جائے تو نمازی کے لئے کیا حکم ہے
و من صلى ركعة من الظهر، ثم اقيمت يصلى اخرى صيانة للمؤدى عن البطلان، ثم يدخل مع القوم احرار لفضيلة الجماعة، وان لم يقيد الاولى بالسجدة ، يقطع ويشرع مع الامام، هو الصحيح، لأنه بمحل الرفق والقطع للاكمال، بخلاف ما اذا كان فى النفل ، لانه ليس للا كمال، ولو كان فى السنة قبل الظهر والجمعة فاقيم او خطب يقطع على راس الركعتين روى ذلك عن ابي يوسف وقد قيل يتمها
ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے ظہر کی ایک رکعت پڑھی پھر جماعت شروع کر دی گئی تو یہ شخص دوسری رکعت پڑھ لے تا کہ بطلان سے
Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer. (B) Chapter on catching the obligatory prayer. Explanation: In previous chapters, the explanation of fard, wajib, and nafl was given. Now in this chapter, the meaning of complete performance is praying with congregation. Ruling: If one has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, and then the iqamah is called, he should pray another rak'ah to preserve the performed part from invalidity, then enter with the people to gain the virtue of congregation. And if he has not tied the first rak'ah with the sajdah (i.e., has not performed the prostrations), he should cut off and begin with the Imam, this is correct because it is a place of leniency and cutting for completion. Contrary to the case where he is in nafl, because there is no completion. If he is in the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah and the iqamah is called or the khutbah is given, he should cut off at the end of two rak'ahs. That is reported from Abu Yusuf, and it has been said that he completes them. Translation: And the person who has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, then congregation is started, this person should pray a second rak'ah so that from invalidity...
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on 'Idrak al-Faridah' (catching the obligatory prayer). The author explains that the chapter deals with the meaning of complete performance, specifically about praying with congregation. It then addresses the scenario: a person has started praying Zuhr individually and has completed one rak'ah when the iqamah for congregational prayer is called. The ruling is that he should complete a second rak'ah by himself to 'save' the first rak'ah from being invalid (since a prayer is invalid if less than two rak'ahs are performed without a reason). Then he should join the congregation for the remaining rak'ahs. However, if he has not yet performed the prostration of the first rak'ah, he should cut his prayer and join the Imam from the beginning. This is the correct view (huwa al-sahih). The reason given is that this is a place of leniency (rifq) and cutting for the purpose of completing the prayer with congregation. The ruling differs if he is praying nafl (supererogatory) - then he should cut immediately because there is no completion involved. For the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, there is a report from Abu Yusuf that he should cut after completing two rak'ahs, but some say he completes them. The passage ends with the beginning of the Urdu translation, which is cut off on this page.

Key Terms
ادراك الفريضة (idrak al-faridah): Catching the obligatory prayer; the chapter deals with joining congregation after having started a prayer individually.
صيانة للمؤدى عن البطلان (siyanatan lil-mu'addi 'an al-butlan): To preserve the performed (part of prayer) from invalidity; here, completing two rak'ahs ensures the first rak'ah is not wasted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately cut and join the congregation
B) Complete a second rak'ah, then join the congregation
C) Continue the prayer individually ignoring the congregation
D) Complete four rak'ahs then join

Key Takeaway
When congregation starts after one rak'ah of a fard prayer, complete a second rak'ah to preserve validity, then join; if no sajdah, cut immediately.

Ruling on Nafl and Sunnah When Congregation Begins
Ruling on nafl and sunnah when congregation starts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling for nafl and sunnah prayers when the congregation starts, and identify the internal dispute regarding the sunnah before Zuhr/Jumu'ah.

Core Idea
For nafl, cut immediately; for sunnah before Zuhr/Jumu'ah, cut after two rak'ahs (Abu Yusuf) or complete (other view).

The previous lesson covered the fard prayer. But what if you are praying a nafl (supererogatory) or the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah when the congregation begins? The rulings differ. Nafl prayers have no fixed minimum to preserve, so you cut immediately. For the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, there is a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: should you cut after completing two rak'ahs or complete the full sunnah? This lesson explores these cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of voluntary prayer
Determine if the prayer is nafl (pure supererogatory) or sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah, like the sunnah before Zuhr which is four rak'ahs).
The text specifically mentions 'sunnah before Zuhr and Jumu'ah'—these are two-rak'ah sunnah prayers (but the pre-Jumu'ah sunnah is often four?). Actually, the sunnah before Jumu'ah is two rak'ahs per some views, but the passage assumes a two-rak'ah sunnah.
2
Apply the ruling for nafl: cut immediately
For nafl, there is no 'completion' (kamaal) required—nafl prayers can be abandoned at any time. Therefore, when congregation starts, one should cut immediately and join the Imam.
The reason given in the text: 'la kamaal' (no completion) meaning there is no fixed obligation to complete a nafl prayer.
3
For sunnah before Zuhr/Jumu'ah: two views
The text mentions a report from Abu Yusuf that one should cut after completing two rak'ahs (i.e., if you have prayed one, cut after the second; if you have not started, start and cut after two). Then 'it has been said' (qil) that he completes them (the full sunnah, likely four rak'ahs).
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute; both views are transmitted. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) may vary by later fatwa.
4
Understand the reasoning
Abu Yusuf's view treats the sunnah as having a natural unit of two rak'ahs, so completing two rak'ahs preserves one complete unit and then joining the congregation is akin to the fard case. The other view says the entire sunnah should be completed because it is a sunnah mu'akkadah that should not be interrupted.
The text does not declare which view is sahih for this case, unlike the fard case where 'huwa al-sahih' was stated.

Key Takeaway
For nafl, cut immediately; for sunnah before Zuhr/Jumu'ah, the Hanafi school has two views: cut after two rak'ahs (Abu Yusuf) or complete the sunnah.

Salah — Prayer

Ruling on Starting Fard Alone When Congregation Begins
Rulings on joining congregation after starting fard alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has started a fard prayer alone when the congregation begins, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the case without sajdah.

Core Idea
Cutting a prayer for congregation is allowed only if the first rak'ah is not yet bound by sajdah.

What happens when you begin a fard prayer alone, and then the iqamah is called? Should you continue alone or join the congregation? This lesson from Al-Hidayah provides the Hanafi ruling, distinguishing between a prayer that has been 'bound' by sajdah and one that hasn't. We will also examine a key dispute within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Context
Understand the scenario: a person has started a fard prayer (e.g., Zuhr) individually. Then the congregation for that same prayer begins. The ruling depends on whether he has completed the sajdah of the first rak'ah.
The text distinguishes two sub-cases: (1) with sajdah completed, (2) without sajdah.
2
State the Ruling for Each Sub-Case
If the first rak'ah is bound by sajdah: complete two rak'ahs and give salam, then join the congregation. If not bound by sajdah: cut immediately and join the imam.
The ruling is based on protecting the performed prayer from invalidity and attaining the virtue of congregation.
3
Analyze the Proof (Dalil)
For the first case, the proof is that praying a single rak'ah is invalid (hadith prohibits it). For the second case, the text says it is a 'place of leniency' and cutting is for completion.
An analogy is drawn: like demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better.
4
Examine the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi argued that even without sajdah, one should complete two rak'ahs (by analogy with nafl). The correct madhhab (Fakhr al-Islam) holds that cutting is allowed.
The text sides with Fakhr al-Islam's position, which is the mufta bihi.
5
Apply to Sunnah and Other Cases
For sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, if iqamah or khutbah begins, complete two rak'ahs then cut (narrated from Abu Yusuf). Nafl should not be cut but completed.
This shows that cutting is not absolute; it depends on the type of prayer.

ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے ظہر کی ایک رکعت پڑھی پھر جماعت شروع کر دی گئی تو یہ شخص دوسری رکعت پڑھ لے تا کہ بطلان سے محفوظ رہے۔ جو ادا کی گئی ہے۔ پھر مقتدیوں کے ساتھ شامل ہو جائے فضیلت جماعت کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے اور اگر اس نے ظہر پہلی رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا تو فورا قطع کر دے اور امام کے ساتھ شروع کر دے یہی قول صحیح ہے کیونکہ یہ توڑے جانے کا محل اور (یہ) توڑنا مکمل کرنے کے لئے ہے بخلاف اس کے جبکہ نفل میں ہو کیونکہ نفل کا توڑنا کامل کرنے کے لئے نہیں ہے اور اگر وہ شخص کیا جمعہ سے پہلے کی سنتوں میں ہو پھر اقامت ہوئی یا خطبہ شروع کیا گیا تو دورکعت پوری کر کے قطع کرے یہ امام ابو یوسف سے روایت یا جاتا ہے اور کہا گیا ہے کہ اس کو تمام کرے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے منفرداً ظہر کی ایک رکعت پڑھی یعنی رکعت اولی کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا پھر امام نے جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ظہر شروع کر دی تو ایسی صورت میں اس شخص کو چاہئے کہ وہ دوسری رکعت ملا لے یعنی دو رکعت پڑھ کر سلام پھیرے اب رکعت پر سلام نہ پھیرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو یہ رکعت باطل وہ جائے گی کیونکہ حدیث پاک میں صلاۃ زار سے منع کیا گیا ہے پس اس رکعت ادا کی ہوئی کو باطل ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے دوسری ملانے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے اور جب دورکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو پھر امام کے ساتھ جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے تا کہ جماعت کی فضیلت حاصل ہو جائے اور یہ حکم ایسا ہے جیسے ایک شخص نے جمعہ کے دن جامع مسجد میں ظہر کی نماز شروع کر دی حتی کہ ایک رکعت پڑھ لی پھر جمعہ کی نماز شروع کی گئی تو یہ شخص اس رکعت کے بعد دوسری رکعت ملائے پھر دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر کر جمعہ کی فضیلت کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے جمعہ کی نماز میں شریک ہو جائے ۔ اعتراض: اس موقعہ پر صاحب عنایہ نے ایک اعتراض و جواب تحریر فرمایا ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز جو منفردا شروع کی گئی ہے فرض ہے اور جماعت سنت ہے پس اقامت سنت کے لئے صفت فرضیت کو باطل کرنا کس طرح جائز ہوگا۔
جواب فریضہ ظہر جو منفر د شروع کیا گیا تھا اس کو توڑنا اقامت سنت کے لئے نہیں بلکہ علی وجہ الکمال فریضہ قائم کرنے کے لئے ہے اور اکمال کے لئے توڑنا بھی اکمال ہے جیسے از سر نو مسجد تعمیر کرنے کے لئے مسجد کو منہدم کرنا باعث ثواب ہے نہ کہ باعث عذاب۔ اور یہ بات واضح ہے کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا تنہا پڑھنے کی بہ نسبت ستائیس درجہ افضل ہے۔
صاحب قدوری نے دوسری صورت یہ بیان کی ہے کہ اگر اس شخص نے ظہر کی رکعت اولی کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا اور جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو وہ شخص اس کو قطع کر کے امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے۔ یہی صحیح مذہب ہے اور اسی کے قائل فخر الاسلام ہیں ۔ بعض نفرات نے کہا کہ اس صورت میں بھی دو رکعت پر سلام پھیرے۔ پھر امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو۔ شمس الائمہ سرخسی بھی اسی کے قائل نا شمس الائمہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکعت اولی کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کرنے سے پہلے اگر چہ وہ نماز میں ہے لیکن وہ قربت اور عبادت ہے اور جماعت سنت ہے پس سنت کی رعایت کرنے کے لئے اس قربت کا باطل کرنا کیونکر جائز ہوگا۔ جیسے کسی نے نفل نماز شروع کی اور اس نے پہلی رکعت کا سجدہ بھی نہیں کیا تھا کہ فرض نماز کو باجماعت شروع کر دیا گیا تو یہ شخص اپنا نفل قطع نہ کرے بلکہ دورکعت پوری کر کے پھر اس کے بعد جماعت میں شریک ہو اس جب رکعت اولی کو سجدے کے ساتھ مقید نہ کرنے کی صورت میں نفل قطع نہیں کیا جاتا تو فرض بطریق اولی قطع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ مذہب صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکعت اولی سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کرنے سے پہلے محل رفض ہے۔ یعنی اس کو توڑا جاسکتا ہے اور نظیر اس کی...
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. Translation: Chapter on obtaining the obligatory prayer. Explanation: Previous chapters discussed fard, wajib, and nafl. Now this chapter explains the meaning of complete performance with congregation. What is the ruling when a person is praying sunnah and the congregation for fard starts? And whoever has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, then the iqamah is made, he should pray another rak'ah to protect that performed rak'ah from invalidity, then enter with the people as free to attain the virtue of congregation. And if he has not bound the first rak'ah with a sajdah, he should cut and begin with the imam; that is the correct view, because it is a place of leniency and cutting for completion, unlike when in nafl because nafl is not for completion. And if he was in the sunnah before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and iqamah is made or the khutbah begins, he should cut upon completing two rak'ahs; that is narrated from Abu Yusuf, and it was said he should complete them. Translation: And whoever has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, then the congregation is started, that person should pray a second rak'ah so that the performed rak'ah is protected from invalidity. Then he should join the congregation to gain the virtue of congregation. And if he has not bound the first rak'ah with sajdah, he should immediately cut and begin with the imam; this is the correct saying because it is a place of being cut and cutting is for completion, unlike when in nafl because nafl cutting is not for completion. And if he was in the sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah and iqamah or khutbah started, he should cut upon completing two rak'ahs; that is narrated from Abu Yusuf and it was said he should complete them. Explanation: The scenario is that a person individually prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr, i.e., he bound the first rak'ah with sajdah, then the imam started the congregation for Zuhr. In that case, that person should add a second rak'ah, i.e., pray two rak'ahs and give salam, not giving salam on one rak'ah. The proof is that if he gave salam on one rak'ah, that rak'ah would become invalid because in the pure hadith, salat al-witr [?] is prohibited. So to protect that performed rak'ah from invalidity, he is commanded to add a second. And when he gives salam on two rak'ahs, then he should join the congregation with the imam to attain the virtue of congregation. This ruling is like when a person on Friday in the congregational mosque started Zuhr prayer until he performed one rak'ah, then Jumu'ah prayer was started; that person should add a second rak'ah to that rak'ah, then give salam on two rak'ahs, then join Jumu'ah prayer to attain its virtue. Objection: On this occasion, the author of al-Inayah wrote an objection and answer. The objection is that the Zuhr prayer which was started individually is fard, and congregation is sunnah. So for the sake of sunnah, how can the attribute of fardiyyah be invalidated? Answer: Breaking the fard Zuhr prayer that was started individually is not for the sake of sunnah, but rather for establishing the fard in a complete manner. And breaking for completion is itself completion, just as demolishing a mosque to build it anew is a cause of reward, not punishment. And it is clear that praying with congregation is twenty-seven times more virtuous than praying alone. Sahib al-Quduri stated the second scenario: if that person did not bind the first rak'ah of Zuhr with sajdah and the congregation started, that person should cut it and join the imam. This is the correct madhhab, and Fakhr al-Islam holds it. Some people said that in this scenario too, he should give salam on two rak'ahs and then join the imam. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi also said this. The proof of Shams al-A'imma is that before binding the first rak'ah with sajdah, even though he is in prayer, it is an act of worship and nearness, and congregation is sunnah. So how can this nearness be invalidated for the sake of sunnah? For example, if someone started nafl prayer and had not yet done the sajdah of the first rak'ah when the fard prayer with congregation started, that person should not cut his nafl but rather complete two rak'ahs and then join the congregation. So in the case of not binding the first rak'ah with sajdah, nafl is not cut, so fard would even more not be cut! The correct madhhab's proof is that before binding the first rak'ah with sajdah, it is a place of abolishment, meaning it can be cut. And an analogy for this...
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Bab Idrak al-Faridah. It addresses the scenario where a person is praying alone (whether fard or sunnah) and the congregation for a fard prayer begins. The author presents the Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah, then provides a translation and commentary. The main ruling is divided into two cases: (1) If a person has already performed one rak'ah of Zuhr alone (with its sajdah), and the congregation starts, he should add a second rak'ah, complete two rak'ahs, and give salam, then join the congregation. This protects the first rak'ah from being invalid (as praying a single rak'ah is prohibited by hadith). (2) If he has not yet performed the sajdah of the first rak'ah (i.e., he has only done the ruku' or less), he should cut his prayer immediately and join the imam. This is because before the sajdah, the prayer is not yet firmly established and can be abandoned for a greater good (congregation). The text also distinguishes nafl prayer, which should not be cut but completed as two rak'ahs before joining. Additionally, for sunnah prayers before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, if iqamah or khutbah begins, he should complete two rak'ahs and then cut (narrated from Abu Yusuf). The commentary elaborates with an objection from Sahib al-Inayah: how can one break a fard prayer (which is obligatory) for a sunnah (congregation)? The answer is that the break is not for the sunnah per se, but to perform the fard more perfectly (with congregation), and breaking for completion is itself completion. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scenario where the first rak'ah is not bound by sajdah: the correct position (held by Fakhr al-Islam) is to cut, while Shams al-A'imma argued that it should be completed as two rak'ahs (by analogy with nafl). The relied-upon position is the first (cut).

Key Terms
اداك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): Catching the obligatory prayer; refers to joining the congregation after having begun a prayer alone.
رفض (rafḍ): Abolishment or cancellation of a prayer before completion; in this context, cutting after having performed one rak'ah without sajdah.
قطع (qaṭʿ): Cutting or terminating a prayer; distinct from rafd, it means to stop the prayer.
تقیید بالسجدہ (taqyīd bi-l-sajdah): Binding the rak'ah with the prostration; meaning completing the sajdah of that rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr alone and completed the sajdah, then the congregation for Zuhr begins, what should he do?
A) He should cut immediately and join the imam.
B) He should complete two rak'ahs, give salam, and then join the imam.
C) He should continue his prayer until the end and not join.
D) He should join the congregation in the second rak'ah without completing his first.

Key Takeaway
When congregation begins after one has started a fard prayer alone, the action depends on whether the first rak'ah is bound by sajdah: if bound, complete two; if not, cut and join.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
One Rak'ah Completed Before Congregation: Add a Second Rak'ah
Ruling with proof for completing one rak'ah alone then congregation begins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has completed one rak'ah of fard prayer alone when the congregation begins, and explain the proof from the prohibition of a single-rak'ah prayer.

Core Idea
Completing one rak'ah alone requires adding a second to avoid the invalid single-rak'ah prayer.

When you have already prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr alone and the congregation starts, should you break it or continue? This lesson explains the Hanafi position: you must add a second rak'ah before joining the imam. The key is that a single rak'ah prayed as a complete unit is invalid, so you complete two rak'ahs to validate your prayer, then join the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The person has started Zuhr alone, completed one rak'ah (with sajda), then the congregation for Zuhr begins. What should he do?
2
Understand the ruling
The Hanafi ruling: he should add a second rak'ah, say salām (making a two-rak'ah prayer), then join the congregation.
He should not say salām after one rak'ah.
3
Examine the proof
The proof is a hadith prohibiting 'salāt al-witr' (a single-rak'ah prayer). Praying one rak'ah and ending it would be invalid according to that prohibition.
The term 'witr' here does not refer to the sunnah witr prayer but to any single-rak'ah unit.
4
Address the objection
Objection: Breaking a fard prayer for a sunnah congregation seems wrong. Answer: This breaking is not for the sunnah per se, but to complete the fard in a superior manner (with congregation), and demolition for reconstruction is completion.
The analogy: demolishing a mosque to rebuild it better is rewarded.
5
Apply the principle
The same ruling applies to a similar scenario on Jumu'ah: if you start Zuhr in the Friday mosque and Jumu'ah begins, you also complete two rak'ah and join.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تفریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے منفرداً ظہر کی ایک رکعت پڑھی یعنی رکعت اولی کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کر دیا پھر امام نے جماعت کے ساتھ نماز ظہر شروع کر دی تو ایسی صورت میں اس شخص کو چاہئے کہ وہ دوسری رکعت ملا لے یعنی دو رکعت پڑھ کر سلام پھیرے اب ایک رکعت پر سلام نہ پھیرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر ایک رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو یہ رکعت باطل ہو جائے گی کیونکہ حدیث پاک میں صلاۃ وتر سے منع کیا گیا ہے پس اس رکعت ادا کی ہوئی کو باطل ہونے سے بچانے کے لئے دوسری ملانے کا حکم کیا گیا ہے اور جب دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دیا تو پھر امام کے ساتھ جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے تا کہ جماعت کی فضیلت حاصل ہو جائے اور یہ حکم ایسا ہے جیسے ایک شخص نے جمعہ کے دن جامع مسجد میں ظہر کی نماز شروع کر دی حتی کہ ایک رکعت پڑھ لی پھر جمعہ کی نماز شروع کی گئی تو یہ شخص اس رکعت کے بعد دوسری رکعت ملائے پھر دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر کر جمعہ کی فضیلت کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے جمعہ کی نماز میں شریک ہو جائے۔ اعتراض: اس موقعہ پر صاحب عنایہ نے ایک اعتراض و جواب تحریر فرمایا ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ ظہر کی نماز جو منفردا شروع کی گئی ہے فرض ہے اور جماعت سنت ہے پس اقامت سنت کے لئے صفت فرضیت کو باطل کرنا کس طرح جائز ہوگا۔ جواب: فریضہ ظہر جو منفرد شروع کیا گیا تھا اس کو توڑنا اقامت سنت کے لئے نہیں بلکہ علی وجہ الکمال فریضہ قائم کرنے کے لئے ہے اور اکمال کے لئے توڑنا بھی اکمال ہے جیسے از سر نو مسجد تعمیر کرنے کے لئے مسجد کو منہدم کرنا باعث ثواب ہے نہ کہ باعث عذاب۔ اور یہ بات واضح ہے کہ جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا تنہا پڑھنے کی بہ نسبت ستائیس درجہ افضل ہے۔
Explanation of the case: A person prayed one rak'ah of Zuhr alone, i.e., he bound the first rak'ah with the sajda (prostration). Then the imam started the Zuhr prayer with the congregation. In such a case, that person should add another rak'ah, i.e., pray two rak'ahs and say the salām. He should not say salām on one rak'ah. The proof: If he says salām on one rak'ah, that rak'ah will become invalid because in the noble hadith, prayer of one rak'ah (salāt al-witr) is prohibited. Therefore, to save this performed rak'ah from invalidity, the command is given to add another. And when he says salām on two rak'ahs, then he should join the congregation with the imam to attain the virtue of congregation. This ruling is like the case where a person started Zuhr prayer in the Friday mosque on Friday day, even if he prayed one rak'ah, then Friday prayer began. That person after that rak'ah should add another rak'ah, then say salām on two rak'ahs and join the Friday prayer to attain its virtue. Objection: At this point, the author of al-'Ināyah wrote an objection and answer. The objection is: The Zuhr prayer started individually is fard, and congregation is sunnah. So how is it permissible to invalidate the characteristic of fard for the sake of a sunnah? Answer: Breaking the fard Zuhr started individually is not for establishing a sunnah, but rather for establishing the fard in a complete manner (alā wajh al-kamāl). And breaking for completion is itself completion, just as demolishing a mosque to rebuild it is a cause of reward, not punishment. And it is clear that praying with congregation is twenty-seven times more virtuous than praying alone.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage is a detailed exposition (tafrī') of the first scenario in the Chapter of Idrāk al-Farīda. The ruling: if a person individually started Zuhr, completed one rak'ah (with its sajda), and then the congregation began, he should not finish with one rak'ah (which would be invalid as a single rak'ah prayer). Instead, he should add a second rak'ah to complete a valid two-rak'ah prayer, then say salām, and then join the congregation for the remaining rak'ahs. The proof is the hadith prohibiting the 'witr' prayer (single rak'ah) - the author uses the term 'salāt al-witr' to mean a single rak'ah prayed as a complete unit. The objection from the author of al-'Ināyah is that breaking a fard for a sunnah is problematic, but the answer clarifies that this breaking is not for the sunnah per se but to perfect the fard by achieving the superior congregation. The analogy with Friday prayer reinforces the point: a person who starts Zuhr in the Friday mosque then Friday begins should also complete two rak'ahs and join.

Key Terms
مقید (muqayyad): Bound; a rak'ah muqayyadah bi al-sajdah means the rak'ah is completed with its prostration, making it a distinct unit.
صلاۃ وتر (ṣalāt al-witr): Prayer of a single rak'ah; the Hadīth prohibits intending a single rak'ah as a complete prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main proof the Hanafi school uses for adding a second rak'ah in this case?
A) The Quranic verse on shortening prayer.
B) The hadith prohibiting a single-rak'ah prayer (salāt al-witr).
C) The principle that congregation is 27 times better.
D) The analogy with Friday prayer.

Key Takeaway
When one rak'ah of fard is completed alone and congregation begins, the Hanafi school requires adding a second rak'ah before joining, based on the prohibition of a single-rak'ah prayer.

Breaking the Fard to Join Congregation: Before Completing Sa'jda
Second sub-case: breaking fard to join congregation before completing first rak'ah sajda.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafī ruling when a person has not completed the sajda of the first rak'ah and the congregation starts, and explain why it differs from the nafil case.

Core Idea
If you haven't done the sajda, your prayer is breakable — break it to gain the virtue of congregation.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in the chapter of ṣalāh: a person begins Zuhr individually, but before he completes the prostration (sajda) of the first rak'ah, the congregation for the same prayer commences. What should he do? The Hanafī school has a clear ruling based on the concept of 'maḥall al-rafḍ' (a breakable state) and the principle of 'ikmāl' (perfection). We will explore the correct position, the counterargument by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsī, and the decisive proof that distinguishes this case from a nafil prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Read the passage carefully: a person is performing Zuhr alone but has not yet performed the sajda of the first rak'ah. When the congregation starts, what is the correct Hanafī ruling?
Al-Qudūrī states the ruling directly: he should cut off his prayer and join the congregation.
2
Recognize the breakable state (maḥall al-rafḍ)
Understand that before the sajda of a rak'ah is completed, the prayer is in a breakable state. This is a key Hanafī principle. The author gives an example: if someone inadvertently stands for a fifth rak'ah, he can return as long as he has not performed the sajda of that extra rak'ah.
The term 'maḥall al-rafḍ' literally means 'place of abandonment'; here it indicates the prayer can be validly broken.
3
Understand the opposing view and its qiyas analogy
Some scholars, including Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsī, argue that the person should complete two rak'ahs and then join. Their proof is an analogy (qiyas) with a nafil prayer: if a person is performing nafil and the congregation starts, he does not break his nafil; therefore, a fortiori, a fard should not be broken either.
This analogy is based on the idea that both are acts of worship and breaking a fard for a sunnah (congregation) seems problematic.
4
Distinguish the 'illah for breaking fard vs nafil
The correct madhhab refutes the analogy by distinguishing the effective cause ('illah). Breaking the fard is for 'ikmāl' (perfection) — i.e., to perform the fard in congregation, which is superior. Breaking a nafil does not serve any similar purpose of perfection; it would simply waste the devotion without gaining a higher reward.
Thus, the analogy fails because the 'illah differs. This is a classic example of 'talil' (reasoning based on effective cause).
5
Accept the tarjih and the mufta bihi
The correct madhhab is the one preferred by Fakhr al-Islām al-Pazdawī and the author of al-Hidāyah: break immediately and join. This is the mufta bihi (operative ruling). The minority view of Sarakhsī is not relied upon in practice.
The ruling is considered wājib because delaying could cause missing the congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب قدوری نے دوسری صورت یہ بیان کی ہے کہ اگر اس شخص نے ظہر کی رکعت اولی کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا اور جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو وہ شخص اس کو قطع کر کے امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے۔ یہی صحیح مذہب ہے اور اسی کے قائل فخر الاسلام ہیں۔ بعض نفرات نے کہا کہ اس صورت میں بھی دو رکعت پر سلام پھیرے۔ پھر امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو۔ شمس الائمہ سرخسی بھی اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ شمس الائمہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکعت اولی کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کرنے سے پہلے اگر چہ وہ نماز میں ہے لیکن وہ قربت اور عبادت ہے اور جماعت سنت ہے پس سنت کی رعایت کرنے کے لئے اس قربت کا باطل کرنا کیونکر جائز ہوگا۔ جیسے کسی نے نفل نماز شروع کی اور اس نے پہلی رکعت کا سجدہ بھی نہیں کیا تھا کہ فرض نماز کو باجماعت شروع کر دیا گیا تو یہ متکلم اپنا نفل قطع نہ کرے بلکہ دو رکعت پوری کر کے پھر اس کے بعد جماعت میں شریک ہو۔ پس جب رکعت اولی کو سجدے کے ساتھ مقید نہ کرنے کی صورت میں نفل قطع نہیں کیا جاتا تو فرض بطریق اولی قطع نہیں کیا جائے گا۔ مذہب صحیح کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ رکعت اولی سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کرنے سے پہلے محل رفض ہے۔ یعنی اس کو توڑا جاسکتا ہے اور نظیر اس کی یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص چوتھی رکعت پر بیٹھے بغیر پانچویں کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا تو جب تک پانچویں رکعت کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا جاتا تو چھوڑا جا سکتا ہے یعنی پانچویں رکعت کا سجدہ کرنے سے پہلے پہلے وہ قعدہ اخیرہ کی طرف لوٹ سکتا ہے۔ اس پر چھٹی رکعت کا ملانا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ اور رہی یہ بات کہ فرض کو باطل کرنا لازم آتا ہے تو اس کا جواب گذر چکا کہ یہ قطع اور بطلان اکمال کے لئے ہے یعنی فریضہ ظہر کی علی وجہ الکمال حاصل کرنے کے لئے ہے۔ بخلاف ما اذا كان في النفل الخ سے شمس الائمہ کے قیاس علی افضل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ ظہر کے فرض کو جماعت میں شریک ہونے کے لئے فریضہ کو علی وجہ الکمال حاصل کرنے کے لئے ہے یعنی فضیلت جماعت حاصل کرنے کے لئے اور نفل کا توڑنا اکمال کے لئے نہیں ہوتا پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے فرض کو نفل پر قیاس کرنا درست نہیں ہوگا۔
Sāhib al-Qudūrī stated the second case: If that person did not bind the first rak'ah of Zuhr with the sajda (i.e., did not complete the prostration), and the congregation stood up, then that person should cut off his prayer and join the imam. This is the correct madhhab, and Fakhr al-Islām (al-Pazdawī) subscribes to it. Some people said that in this case too, he should say salām on two rak'ahs and then join the imam. Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsī also subscribed to this. Shams al-A'imma's proof: Before binding the first rak'ah with the sajda, even though he is in prayer, it is a form of devotion and worship, and congregation is a sunnah. So how can it be permissible to invalidate this devotion for the sake of a sunnah? Just as if someone started a nafil prayer and had not yet performed the sajda of the first rak'ah when the fard prayer with congregation began, that person (performing nafil) should not cut off his nafil, but complete two rak'ahs and then join the congregation. So when in the case of not binding the first rak'ah with sajda, a nafil is not cut off, then a fortiori a fard should not be cut off. The proof of the correct madhhab: Before binding the first rak'ah with sajda, it is a place for breaking (maḥall al-rafḍ). That is, it can be broken. And an example of this: If a person stood up for a fifth rak'ah without sitting for the final tashahhud, then as long as he has not bound the fifth rak'ah with sajda, he can leave it, i.e., before performing the sajda of the fifth rak'ah, he can return to the final sitting. It is not necessary for him to add a sixth rak'ah. And as for the argument that invalidating a fard is necessary, the answer has already been given: this cutting and invalidation is for completion, i.e., to achieve the fard of Zuhr in the most complete manner. As for the analogy with nafil, the response to Shams al-A'imma's analogy is that the breaking of the fard of Zuhr to join the congregation is for achieving the fard in the most complete manner, i.e., to attain the virtue of congregation, whereas breaking a nafil is not for completion. Therefore, due to this difference, it is not correct to analogize fard with nafil.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents the second sub-case in the chapter. If a person has started Zuhr individually but has not yet performed the sajda of the first rak'ah (the rak'ah is not 'bound' with sajda), his prayer is still in a breakable state (maḥall al-rafḍ). The correct Hanafī position (the 'ṣaḥīḥ madhhab' according to Fakhr al-Islām al-Pazdawī) is that he should break his prayer immediately and join the congregation. Some scholars, including Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsī, argue that he should instead complete two rak'ahs by adding a second, because breaking a fard for a sunnah is problematic, analogous to the case of nafil prayer where one does not break even if the fard congregation starts. The text refutes this analogy by distinguishing the purpose: breaking the fard is to perfect the fard (by gaining congregational virtue), while breaking a nafil would serve no such purpose. The concept of maḥall al-rafḍ is further illustrated with the example of a person who inadvertently stands for a fifth rak'ah—he can return to the sitting as long as he hasn't performed the sajda of that extra rak'ah.

Key Terms
محل رفض (maḥall al-rafḍ): The state or place where an act of worship can be abandoned or broken; here, the prayer before completing the sajda of a rak'ah.
اکمال (ikmāl): Completion or perfection; the purpose of breaking the prayer is to achieve a more perfect form of the same obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person starts Zuhr alone and has not yet performed the sajda of the first rak'ah when the congregation for Zuhr begins, what is the correct Hanafī position?
A) Complete two rak'ahs and then join.
B) Break immediately and join the congregation.
C) Continue his prayer alone and not join.
D) Wait until the imam completes two rak'ahs then join.

Key Takeaway
Before completing the sajda of the first rak'ah, the prayer is still breakable; break it to gain the superior reward of congregation.

When to Break Sunnah Prayers Before Obligatory Prayer
Ruling for sunnah prayers before Zuhr or Jumu'ah when the fard/khutbah begins

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for interrupting the sunnah qabliyyah of Zuhr and Jumu'ah when the fard or khutbah begins, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement.

Core Idea
If the fard starts during sunnah qabliyyah, the ruling varies: complete two rak'ahs (Abu Yusuf) or add a second if one done (Abu Hanifa).

This passage addresses a practical scenario: you have begun the four-rak'ah sunnah before Zuhr or Jumu'ah, and the obligatory prayer or khutbah starts. What should you do? The Hanafi school has multiple narrations, and the later scholar Faqih al-Sa'dī changed his fatwā after discovering a narration from Imam Abū Ḥanīfa in al-Nawādir. Understanding this ikhtilaf helps appreciate how transmitted narrations can override established practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default hukm
What is the sunnah qabliyyah of Zuhr/Jumu'ah? It is a sunnah muakkadah of four rak'ahs, considered a single unit.
2
State the triggering event
The ruling applies when the fard prayer begins (iqamah for Zuhr) or the imam starts the khutbah for Jumu'ah.
3
Present the primary narration (Abu Yusuf)
According to one narration from Abu Yusuf, one should complete only two rak'ahs, say salām, and join the congregation.
4
Present the alternative narration (Abu Hanifa)
In al-Nawādir, Abu Hanifa is reported to say: if one rak'ah has been done, add a second rak'ah, then say salām and join.
This applies specifically if only one rak'ah was performed; other cases may be extrapolated.
5
Explain the tarjih and practice
Faqih al-Sa'di initially followed the view of completing all four, but after seeing Abu Hanifa's narration, he adopted it. This shows the weight given to direct transmission from the Imam.
The mufta bihi today may vary, but the Nawadir narration is considered strong in this case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور اگر کسی نے ظہر سے پہلے کی چار رکعت سنت پڑھنی شروع کر دی پھر ظہر کی نماز شروع ہو گئی یا جمعہ سے پہلے سنتوں کی نیت باندھی پھر امام نے خطبہ شروع کر دیا ان دونوں صورتوں میں حکم یہ ہے کہ دو رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیر دے اور نماز ظہر میں اور خطبہ میں شریک ہو جائے۔ یہ حکم امام ابو یوسف سے مروی ہے۔ انہوں نے کہا کہ چاروں رکعت پوری کرے پھر نماز ظہر یا خطبہ میں شرکت کرے کیونکہ ظہر اور جمعہ سے پہلے کی چار رکعت بمنزلۂ صلاة واحد ہے۔ اس لئے ان کو دو منقطوں میں تقسیم نہ کرے بلکہ چاروں کو یکبارگی پڑھے۔ فقیہ وقت سعدی کہتے ہیں کہ میں اس پر فتویٰ دیا کرتا تھا کہ اگر نماز ظہر سے پہلے سنتوں کی نیت باندھی اور پھر نماز ظہر شروع ہوگا۔ سنت کی چاروں رکعت پوری کر کے سلام پھیرے بر خلاف نفل نماز کے کہ نفل کی دو رکعت پر سلام پھیر دے لیکن جب میں نے نوادر میں امام اعظم کی یہ روایت دیکھی کہ اگر سنت جمعہ کو شروع کر دیا پھر امام خطبہ کے لئے نکلا تو امام صاحب نے فرمایا کہ اگر ایک رکعت پڑھ لی ہے تو دوسری رکعت ملا کر سلام پھیر دے تو میں نے اپنے فتویٰ سے رجوع کر لیا اور اس کا قائل ہو گیا جو امام صاحب سے مروی ہے۔
And if someone started praying the four rak'ahs of sunnah before Zuhr, then the Zuhr prayer began; or he made the intention of the sunnah before Jumu'ah, then the imam started the khutbah (sermon). In both these cases, the ruling is that he should complete two rak'ahs, say salām, and then join the Zuhr prayer or the khutbah. This ruling is narrated from Imam Abū Yūsuf. He said that he should complete all four rak'ahs and then join the Zuhr prayer or the khutbah because the four rak'ahs before Zuhr and Jumu'ah are like a single prayer. Therefore, he should not divide them into two parts, but should pray all four at once. Faqīh al-Waqt al-Sa'dī said: I used to give fatwā that if one intended the sunnah before Zuhr and then the Zuhr prayer began, he should complete the entire four-rak'ah sunnah and say salām, contrary to nafil prayer where he should say salām after two rak'ahs. But when I saw in al-Nawādir that Imam A'zam (Abū Ḥanīfa) was narrated as saying: If one started the sunnah of Jumu'ah and then the imam came out for the khutbah, the Imam (Abū Ḥanīfa) said: If he has prayed one rak'ah, he should add a second rak'ah and say salām. So I retracted my fatwā and adopted the view narrated from Imam A'zam.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage deals with the sunnah prayers performed before the obligatory Zuhr or Jumu'ah prayers. According to a narration from Imam Abū Yūsuf, if someone starts the four-rak'ah sunnah before Zuhr and then the congregation for Zuhr begins, or starts the sunnah before Jumu'ah and then the imam begins the khutbah, the person should complete only two rak'ahs, say salām, and then join the fard/khutbah. However, Abū Yūsuf's own opinion (according to a different narration) is that the four rak'ahs should be completed as they are like a single prayer unit. The text then recounts the experience of Faqīh al-Sa'dī, who initially gave fatwā based on the completion of four rak'ahs, but upon discovering a narration in al-Nawādir (a collection of non-zahir al-riwayah transmissions) from Abū Ḥanīfa that for the sunnah of Jumu'ah, if one rak'ah is done, one should add a second and then join, he changed his fatwā. This illustrates how later scholars may adopt a lesser-known transmission (riwāyah) over their own ijtihād when authentic.

Key Terms
نوادر (nawādir): Rare transmissions; here, a collection of narrations from Imam Abū Ḥanīfa that are not part of Zahir al-Riwayah.
سنن قبلية (sunan qabliyyah): The supererogatory prayers performed before an obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the narration from Imam Abū Ḥanīfa in al-Nawādir, what should a person do if he has started the sunnah of Jumu'ah and then the imam comes out for the khutbah, having already prayed one rak'ah?
A) He should complete all four rak'ahs.
B) He should break immediately and join the khutbah.
C) He should add a second rak'ah, say salām, and then join the khutbah.
D) He should continue until he finishes his sunnah then join.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains multiple narrations on interrupting sunnah qabliyyah; later muftis may adopt a lesser-known riwayah if it is found authentic.

Completing Prayer When Congregation Starts After Three Rak'ahs
A case-based ruling with ta'lil (reasoning).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr individually when the congregation begins, and distinguish it from the case where he is still in the third rak'ah before sajda.

Core Idea
Three rak'ahs is the majority; the prayer cannot be broken – complete the fourth, then join the congregation for nafil.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: you have already performed three out of four rak'ahs of Zuhr when the congregation for Zuhr starts. The Hanafi school, applying the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole, rules that you must finish the fourth rak'ah before joining. However, if you are still in the third rak'ah and have not yet performed its sajda, you are still in a breakable state and may cut the prayer. After completing your own fard, you join the congregation, and your prayer with them becomes nafil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between (a) having completed three full rak'ahs (with sajda) and (b) being in the third rak'ah without having performed its sajda.
This distinction is crucial for the ruling.
2
Apply the principle 'al-akthar ka al-kull'
Once three rak'ahs are complete, the prayer is considered comparable to having performed the whole; it cannot be broken.
This is the ta'lil (reason) for the ruling.
3
Contrast the breakable state
In the third rak'ah before sajda, the rak'ah is not yet bound; the prayer is still in a place of abandonment (maḥall al-rafḍ), so it may be cut.
Sajda is the binding element of a rak'ah.
4
Note the options when cutting
If cutting, the person has a choice: either end the prayer by sitting and saying taslim, or say takbir standing, intending to join the imam (thus converting his prayer to nafil).
The second option allows joining the congregation without delay.
5
Conclude the sequence for the three-rak'ah case
After completing the fourth rak'ah, the person joins the congregation; the prayer he prays with them is nafil because the fard has already been performed.
The same fard cannot be repeated in one time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مق و ان كان قد صلى ثلاثا من الظهر يتمها، لان للاكثر حكم الكل، فلا يحتمل النقض، بخلاف ما اذا كان لي الثالثة بعد ولم يقيدها بالسجدة حيث يقطعها، لانه بمحل الرفض، ويتخير ان شاء عاد فقعد وسلم، وان شال كبر قائما ينوى الدخول في صلاة الامام، واذا اتمها يدخل مع القوم والذى يصلى معهم نافلة لان الفرد فرض لا يتكر رفى وقت واحد۔ ترجمہ اور اگر وہ شخص ظہر کی تین رکعتیں پڑھ چکا ہے تو اس کو پورا کرے کیونکہ اکثر کے لئے کل کا حکم ہوتا ہے تو وہ قطع کو برداشت نہیں کر سکتا۔ برخلاف اس کے جبکہ وہ ابھی تک تیسری رکعت میں ہو اور اس کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید نہیں کیا ہے تو اس کو قطع کردے کیونکہ وہ محل رفض ہے اور اس کو اختیار ہے کہ اگر چاہے تو وہ لوٹ کر بیٹھ جائے اور سلام پھیر دے اور اگر چاہے تو کھڑے کھڑے تکبیر کہہ کر امام کی نماز میں داخل ہونے کی نیت کرتے ہوئے اور جب نماز ظہر کو پورا کر لیا تو مقتدیوں کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے اور جو نماز ان کے ساتھ پڑھے گا نفل ہوگی کیونکہ ایک وقت میں فرض مکرر نہیں ہوتا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص ظہر کی تین رکعت پڑھ چکا ہو پھر جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی ہو تو وہ چار رکعت پوری کرے۔
Matn: And if he has prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr, he completes them (i.e., the fourth), because the majority has the ruling of the whole, so it cannot bear breaking. Contrary to if he is still in the third rak'ah and has not bound it with the sajda, then he cuts it because he is in a place for breaking. And he has a choice: if he wishes, he returns and sits and says salām; and if he wishes, he says takbīr standing, intending to enter the imam's prayer. And when he completes it (the fourth), he enters with the people, and what he prays with them is nāfil because the individual fard does not repeat in one time. Translation: And if that person has prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr, he completes it (the fourth), because the majority has the ruling of the whole, so he cannot bear breaking. Unlike the case when he is still in the third rak'ah and has not bound it with the sajda, then he cuts it because it is a place for breaking. And he has a choice: if he wishes, he returns and sits and says salām; and if he wishes, he says takbīr standing, intending to enter the imam's prayer. And when he completes the Zuhr prayer, he joins the congregation, and whatever prayer he prays with them will be nāfil, because the fard is not repeated in one time. Explanation: The case is that if a person has prayed three rak'ahs of Zuhr, then the congregation stands up, he completes four rak'ahs.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This is a matn from al-Hidāyah with commentary. The ruling: if a person has already performed three rak'ahs of the individual Zuhr (i.e., the majority of the prayer) and then the congregation begins, he must complete the fourth rak'ah, because the majority of a prayer takes the ruling of the whole. Unlike the case where he is in the third rak'ah but has not yet performed its sajda—there he is still in a breakable state and may cut. But after three rak'ahs are complete, the prayer is too far advanced to be broken. After completing his four rak'ahs, he joins the congregation, and his prayer with them will be nāfil (supererogatory) because the same fard cannot be repeated in one time (the fard has already been performed by his own prayer). The matn adds that if he is in the third rak'ah before sajda, he has a choice: either return to the sitting and say salām (ending his prayer) or say takbīr standing and intend to enter the imam's prayer (thus converting his intention to nāfil and joining).

Key Terms
اکثر (akthar): Majority; here, three out of four rak'ahs of Zuhr take the ruling of the whole prayer.
محل رفض (maḥall al-rafḍ): A state where the act can be abandoned; before the sajda of a rak'ah, the rak'ah is not fully bound.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person has already performed three complete rak'ahs of Zuhr individually and then the congregation for Zuhr begins, according to the Hanafī school, what must he do?
A) He must break his prayer immediately and join the congregation.
B) He must complete the fourth rak'ah and then join the congregation, praying with them as nāfil.
C) He may choose to complete the fourth or cut and join.
D) He should add two more rak'ahs to make it a complete prayer and then join.

Key Takeaway
When the majority of a fard prayer is completed, the prayer cannot be broken; it must be finished, and then joining the congregation yields nafil.

Cutting Voluntary Prayer to Join the Congregation: Conditions and Rulings
Explains the hadith of joining congregation and specific rulings for Fajr, Asr, Maghrib.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting a sunnah prayer to join the congregation and apply the conditions for when it is recommended and when it is not.

Core Idea
Cutting a voluntary prayer to join the congregation is recommended when it preserves the virtue of congregation and avoids makruh times.

In this lesson, we explore a practical scenario: you have started a voluntary prayer (sunnah) and then the iqamah for the congregational prayer is called. Should you complete your voluntary prayer or join the imam? The Hanafi school provides clear guidance based on a prophetic hadith and the principles of avoiding makruh times. We will examine the general rule and its specific applications to Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act under discussion is cutting a voluntary prayer (sunnah or nafl) that has already been started in order to join a congregational prayer. The ruling is that it is recommended (mandub) to cut the voluntary prayer and join the congregation, provided certain conditions are met.
This is a recommendation, not an obligation, because the voluntary prayer itself is not obligatory.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The primary proof is the hadith where the Prophet ﷺ instructed two companions who had already prayed individually to join the congregation and consider their prayer as nafl. This establishes the principle that joining the congregation is superior to completing an individual voluntary prayer.
The hadith is from Abu Dawood, Ibn Majah, and others; it is a hadith ahad with zanni thubut and dalalah.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The Prophet's command 'pray with them and make it a supererogatory prayer' (وَاجعَلوا صلاتَكُم مَعَهُم سُبحةً) indicates that the initial prayer is not invalidated but is converted to nafl, and that joining the congregation is preferable. This is the basis for the recommendation to cut a voluntary prayer to join the congregation.
The hadith also implies that the virtue of congregation outweighs the virtue of completing a sunnah individually.
4
Apply the ruling to specific cases
The passage applies the general principle to Fajr, Asr, and Maghrib. For Fajr: if you have prayed one rak'ah of the sunnah and iqamah is called, you cut and join. If you have stood for the second rak'ah but not yet performed the sajdah, you also cut. However, if you have completed the two rak'ahs, you do not join because nafl is makruh after Fajr. Similarly after Asr. For Maghrib: after completing Maghrib alone, you do not join because joining would require either three rak'ahs of nafl (disliked) or four rak'ahs (opposing the imam).
The ruling for Maghrib is based on Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah, the authoritative transmitted position.
5
Identify the underlying rationale
The rationale is to maximize the virtue of congregation while avoiding makruh times (praying nafl after Fajr/Asr) and avoiding opposing the imam (in Maghrib). The Hanafi school balances these considerations through istihsan (juristic preference).
This shows that the Hanafi school does not rigidly follow a single textual proof but considers broader objectives.
