باب ادراك الفريضة

فقال على رسلكما فانى ابن امرأة كانت تأكل القديد ثم قال ما لكما لم تصليا فقالا كنا صلينا فى رحالنا فقال عليه السلام اذا صليتما فى رحالكما ثم اتيتما صلاة قام فصليا معهم واجعلا صلاتكما معهم سبحة اى نافلة

یعنی رسول اللہ ظہر کی نماز سے فارغ ہو گئے تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بالکل صفوں کے پیچھے دو آدمیوں کو دیکھا کہ انہوں نے آپ کے ساتھ نماز نہیں پڑھی ہے۔ آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ ان دونوں کو میرے پاس لاؤ۔ پس ان دونوں کو لایا گیا ( مارے خوف کے ) ان دونوں کے ھے تھر تھر کانپنے لگے پس آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا، کہ تم مطمئن رہو ( گھبراؤ مت ) میں ایسی عورت کا بیٹا ہوں جو سوکھا گوشت کھاتی تھی (یعنی بہت غریب گھرانے کا بیٹا ہوں ) پھر آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تم نے ہمارے ساتھ نماز کیوں نہیں پڑھی ہے، ان دونوں نے کہا کہ اپنی قیام گاہ پر نماز پڑھ چکے تھے ۔ آپ ا نے فرمایا کہ اگر تم اپنی قیام گاہ پر نماز پڑھ چکے ہوا اور پھر کسی قوم کی نماز کے وقت آگئے ہو تو ان کے ساتھ بھی پڑھ لیا کرو اور ان کے ساتھ جو نماز ہو اس کو نفل شمار کر لینا۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اگر امام نے فرض ادا کیا ہو اور مقتدی نے نفل تو اس میں کراہت نہیں ہے۔

فجر کی سنت ایک رکعت پڑھی پھر جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو کیا حکم ہے

فان صلى من الفجر ركعة ثم اقيمت يقطع ويدخل معهم، لانه لو اضاف اليها اخرى تفوته الجماعة، وكذا اذا اقام الى الثانية قبل ان يقيدها بالسجدة ، وبعد الاتمام لا يشرع في صلوة الامام لكراهية النقل بعده

وكذا بعد المغرب في ظاهر الرواية، لان التنفل بالثلاث مكروه، وفى جعلها أربعا مخالفة لإمامه. ترجمہ پس اگر فجر کی ایک رکعت پڑھ چکا ہے پھر جماعت کھڑی ہوگئی تو اس کو قطع کر کے مقتدیوں کے ساتھ شریک ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ اگر اس نے دوسری رکعت ملائی تو جماعت فوت ہو جائے گی۔ ایسے ہی اگر دوسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا قبل اس کے کہ اس کو سجدہ کے ساتھ مقید کرے اور فجر کی نماز پوری کرنے کے بعد امام کی نماز کو شروع نہ کرے کیونکہ نماز فجر کے بعد نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور یونہی عمر کے بعد اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی اور یونہی مغرب کے بعد ظاہر الرولیہ کے مطابق ، کیونکہ تین رکعت نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اور اسن کو چار کر لینے میں امام کی مخالفت ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے فجر کی ایک رکعت پڑھی ہے پھر جماعت کھڑی ہوئی تو یہ شخص اپنی یہ نماز قطع کرکے لوگوں کے ساتھ جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے کیونکہ اگر دوسری رکعت ملائے گا تو منفردا اس کی نماز پوری ہوگئی لیکن جماعت فوت ہوگئی حالانکہ جماعت سنت مؤکدہ ہے۔ پس فضیلت جماعت کو حاصل کرنے کے لئے اس نماز کو قطع کر دے جس کو منفر د ا شروع کر رکھا ہے۔ اس طرح اگر یہ شخص فجر کی دوسری رکعت کے لئے کھڑا ہو گیا لیکن دوسری رکعت کا سجدہ نہیں کیا تو اس صورت میں بھی اس کو قطع کر کے جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے۔ البتہ اگر اس نے فجر کی نماز تنہا پڑھ لی اس کے بعد جماعت کھڑی ہوئی تو اب امام کی نماز میں شرکت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں امام کے ساتھ جو نماز پڑھے گا وہ فل ہوگی۔ حالانکہ فجر کی نماز کے بعد طلوع آفتاب تک نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ یوں ہی عصر کے بعد غروب تک نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق مغرب کی نماز تنہا پڑھنے کے بعد جماعت میں شرکت نہ کرے کیونکہ اگر امام کے ساتھ شریک ہو گیا تو دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو امام کے ساتھ سلام پھیرے گا یا امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ایک رکعت اور پڑھے گا تا کہ چار رکت ہو جائیں تین امام کے ساتھ اور ایک امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد پہلی صورت میں نفل کی تین رکعت ہوں گی حالانکہ تین رکعت نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اور دوسری صورت میں امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آئے گا اور یہ بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ اگر کسی نے مغرب کی نماز تنبا ادا کر لی ، پھر جماعت کھڑی ہو گئی تو یہ شخص جماعت میں شرکت نہ کرے۔
Chapter of Perceiving the Obligatory Prayer. He said: 'Take it easy, for I am the son of a woman who used to eat dried meat.' Then he said: 'What prevented you two from praying?' They said: 'We prayed at our dwellings.' He, peace be upon him, said: 'If you have prayed at your dwellings and then come to a congregational prayer, pray with them and make your prayer with them a supererogatory prayer (nafl).' Meaning: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, had finished the Zuhr prayer and saw two men behind the rows who had not prayed with him. He said to bring them. They came trembling. He said: 'Be calm. I am the son of a woman who used to eat dried meat (i.e., from a humble background).' Then he asked why they did not pray. They said they had already prayed at their dwellings. He said: 'If you have prayed at your dwellings and then come to a people's prayer time, pray with them and consider that prayer as nafl.' From this hadith it is learned that there is no dislike if the imam performed the fard and the follower prayed nafl. The ruling on having prayed one rak'ah of the Fajr sunnah and then the congregation is established: [Arabic text] 'If he prayed one rak'ah of Fajr and then the iqamah is made, he should cut [his prayer] and enter with them, because if he adds another rak'ah he will miss the congregation. Similarly if he stands for the second rak'ah before tying it with the prostration. And after completion, he should not begin the imam's prayer due to the dislike of optional prayer after it. Similarly after Maghrib in the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah), because performing three rak'ahs as nafl is disliked, and making it four involves opposing the imam.' Translation: So if he has prayed one rak'ah of Fajr and then congregation is established, he should cut and join the followers, because if he adds the second rak'ah, the congregation will be missed. Similarly if he stands for the second rak'ah before tying it with prostration. After completing Fajr, he should not begin the imam's prayer, because praying nafl after Fajr is disliked. Likewise after Asr for the reason we stated. Likewise after Maghrib according to zahir al-riwayah, because praying three rak'ahs as nafl is disliked, and making them four entails opposing the imam. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person has prayed one rak'ah of Fajr and then congregation forms, he should cut that prayer and join the congregation, because if he adds the second rak'ah, his prayer as an individual would be completed but he would miss the congregation, whereas congregation is an emphasized sunnah. So to obtain the virtue of congregation, he should cut the prayer he started as an individual. Similarly if he stood for the second rak'ah of Fajr but did not make the prostration, he should also cut and join the congregation. However, if he completed Fajr alone and then congregation formed, he should not join the imam's prayer because then the prayer with the imam would be nafl, and praying nafl after Fajr until sunrise is disliked. Similarly after Asr until sunset. According to zahir al-riwayah, after praying Maghrib alone, he should not join the congregation because if he joins, there are two possibilities: either he says salam with the imam (making it three rak'ahs nafl, which is disliked) or he prays another rak'ah after the imam finishes to make four rak'ahs (opposing the imam, which is not correct). Therefore we say that if someone prayed Maghrib alone and then congregation forms, he should not join.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This is a combined ruling-and-proof passage. The author begins by citing a hadith from the Prophet ﷺ where he instructs two men who had already prayed individually to join the congregation and consider their prayer as nafl. This establishes the principle that it is permissible (and recommended) to join a congregation even after having performed the fard individually, with the intention of nafl. The passage then addresses the specific scenario of Fajr: if a person has started the Sunnah of Fajr and then the iqamah is called, he should cut his sunnah prayer and join the congregation. This is because the virtue of congregation (sunnah mu'akkadah) outweighs completing the sunnah individually. The same applies if he has stood for the second rak'ah but not yet performed the prostration. However, if he has completed the Fajr sunnah entirely, he should not join the imam, because any prayer after Fajr until sunrise is makruh (disliked) as a nafl. The same ruling applies to Asr. For Maghrib, according to zahir al-riwayah (the authoritative transmitted position), if one has prayed Maghrib alone, he should not join the congregation afterward. The reason is that if he joins the imam, he would either pray three rak'ahs with the imam (making it an odd-numbered nafl, which is makruh) or pray a fourth rak'ah after the imam (which opposes the imam). Thus the ruling avoids both disliked scenarios.

Key Terms
سبحة (sabḥah): In this hadith, supererogatory prayer (nafl), synonymous with نافلة.
جماعت (jamā‘ah): Congregational prayer led by an imam.
ظاہر الروایہ (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The well-known, transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school from the six books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.).
قطع (qaṭ‘): To cut or break a prayer (voluntary) intentionally.
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer; voluntary act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a person do if he has prayed one rak'ah of the Fajr sunnah and then the iqamah for Fajr is called?
A) Complete the two rak'ahs of sunnah then join the congregation.
B) Cut the sunnah and join the congregation immediately.
C) Continue the sunnah but try to finish before the imam's salam.
D) Not join the congregation because his sunnah is more virtuous.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends cutting a voluntary prayer to join the congregation, but not after completing the prayer if it entails praying nafl in a prohibited time (Fajr/Asr) or if it leads to disliked acts (Maghrib).

Leaving the Mosque After the Adhan: Ruling and Exceptions
Ruling with proof and detailed exceptions based on scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan and identify the exceptions that remove the dislike.

Core Idea
Leaving after the adhan without excuse is hypocrisy; but organized congregation needs override the dislike.

The adhan is a divine summons to prayer. Leaving the mosque after hearing it without a valid reason is strongly discouraged, equated with hypocrisy. However, Islamic law is practical: if leaving serves the greater good of congregational prayer, it becomes permissible, even commendable. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its nuanced exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is leaving a mosque after the adhan has been given. The default ruling is makruh (disliked) until one prays the current prayer.
The ruling is based on the hadith prohibiting such exit except for hypocrites.
2
Locate the dalil and its legal force
The proof is a mursal hadith (weak in transmission, zanni al-thubut) but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for non-criminal matters. The wording implies blame.
The dalil's zanni nature explains why the ruling is makruh, not haram.
3
Analyze the exception for a valid need
The hadith itself exempts one who leaves for a need intending to return. The commentary adds: if leaving organizes a congregation, it is not makruh.
This is a form of istihsan: public good overrides the general prohibition.
4
Apply the ruling to different scenarios
The passage details four scenarios: (1) own mosque, not prayed → makruh; (2) own mosque, prayed → not discussed here; (3) other mosque, own neighborhood already prayed → makruh; (4) other mosque, own neighborhood not prayed → permissible to leave for that congregation.
The key factor is whether the person has prayed or not, and whether they are leaving to join an obligatory congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اذان کے بعد مسجد سے نکلنے کا حکم

ومن دخل مسجدا قد اذن فيه، يكره له ان يخرج حتى يصلى ، لقوله عليه السلام: "لا يخرج من المسجد بعد النداء الا منافق او رجل يخرج لحاجة يريد الرجوع، قال: الا اذا كان ينتظم به امر جماعة، لانه ترک صورة تکمیل معنی

ترجمہ اور جوشخص ایسی مسجد میں داخل ہوا جس میں اذان دے دی گئی ہے تو اس کے لئے نکلنا مکروہ ہے یہاں تک کہ نماز پڑھ لے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ مسجد سے اذان کے بعد کوئی نہیں نکلتا مگر منافق یا وہ شخص جو واپسی کے ارادے سے کسی ضرورت سے نکا ہومگر جبکہ اس کے ساتھ کسی جماعت کا انتظام متعلق ہو کیونکہ یہ نکلنا ظاہر میں ترک ، باطن میں تکمیل ہے۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص ایسی مسجد میں داخل ہوا جس میں اذان دے دی گئی ہو تو اس میں قدرے تفصیل ہے کیونکہ جوشخص انی مسجد میں داخل ہوا جس میں اذان دے دی گئی تو اس کی دو حالتیں ہیں یا تو یہ شخص یہ نماز پڑھ چکا ہے یا نہیں پڑھی اگر نماز پڑھ چکا ہے تو اس کا حکم بعد میں بیان کریں گے اور اگر اس نے نماز نہیں پڑھی تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں یہ مسجد یا تو اس کے محلہ کی ہے یا اس کے محلہ کی نہیں ہے اگر محلہ کی ہے تو نماز پڑھنے سے پہلے اس کے لئے نکلنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ مؤذن نے اس کو نماز کی دعوت دی ہے لہذا اس دعوت کو قبول کرے اور بغیر نماز پڑھے نہ نکلے۔ اور اگر یہ مسجد اس کے مجلہ کی نہیں ہے تو پھر دو صورتیں ہیں آیا تو اس کے محلہ کے لوگ اپنی مسجد میں نماز پڑھ چکے ہیں یا نہیں پڑھی ہے اگر پہلی صورت ہے تو بھی بغیر نماز پڑھے اس کا مسجد سے نکلنا مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس مسجد میں داخل ہونے کی وجہ سے یہ شخص اسی مسجد کے اہلیان میں سے ہو گیا اور اگر ثانی صورت ہے تو یہ شخص اپنے محلہ کی مسجد میں نماز پڑھنے کے لئے اس مسجد سے نکل سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ اس پر اپنے محلہ کی مسجد میں نماز پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ (عنایہ ) صاحب ہدایہ نے اس مسئلے کو اس طرح ذکر کیا ہے کہ اگر کوئی شخص ایسی مسجد میں داخل ہوا جس میں اذان دے دی گئی ہے تو بغیر نماز پڑھتے اس مسجد سے نکلنا اس کے لئے مکروہ ہے دلیل اللہ کے نبی کا قول ہے:

لا يخرج من المسجد بعد نداء الا منافق او رجل يخرج لحاجته يريد الرجوع (مراسيل الى داؤد ) ابن ماجہ نے اس حدیث کو ان لفظوں میں بیان کیا ہے: عن محمد بن يوسف لولى عثمان بن عفان رضی الله عنه قال قال رسول الله من ادرك الاذان في المسجد ثم خرج لم يخرج لحاجته و هو لا يريد الرجوع فهو منافق محمد بن یوسف کہتے ہیں کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ جس شخص نے مسجد میں اذان کو پا لیا پھر مسجد سے نکل گیا حالانکہ نہ کی ضرورت
Ruling on Leaving the Mosque After the Adhan. And whoever enters a mosque in which the adhan has been given, it is disliked for him to leave until he prays, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: 'No one leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a man who leaves for a need intending to return.' He said: 'Except when the matter of a congregation is organized by it (his leaving), because it is abandonment in form but completion in meaning.' Translation: And a person who enters a mosque in which the adhan has been given, it is disliked for him to leave until he prays. Because the Prophet ﷺ said: 'No one leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a person who leaves for a need intending to return.' Except when the arrangement of a congregation depends on it, because this leaving is in form abandonment, but in meaning completion. Explanation: The issue is that if a person enters a mosque in which the adhan has been given, there is some detail. The one who enters a mosque after adhan has two states: either he has already prayed this prayer or not. If he has prayed, its ruling will come later. If he has not prayed, then two scenarios: either this mosque is his neighborhood mosque or not. If it is his neighborhood mosque, it is disliked for him to leave before praying because the mu'adhdhin has invited him, so he should accept the invitation and not leave without praying. If it is not his neighborhood mosque, then two scenarios: whether the people of his neighborhood have already prayed in their mosque or not. If the first scenario (they have prayed), it is still disliked for him to leave without praying because by entering this mosque he becomes one of its people. If the second scenario (they have not prayed), then he may leave this mosque to pray in his neighborhood mosque because it is obligatory for him to pray in his neighborhood mosque. (From al-'Inayah). The author of al-Hidayah mentioned this issue: If a person enters a mosque in which the adhan has been given, it is disliked for him to leave without praying. The proof is the saying of the Prophet: 'No one leaves the mosque after the call except a hypocrite or a man who leaves for his need intending to return.' (Mursal of Abu Dawood). Ibn Majah narrated this hadith with these words: From Muhammad ibn Yusuf, the freed slave of 'Uthman ibn 'Affan, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, said: 'Whoever hears the call in the mosque and then leaves, not leaving for a need and not intending to return, is a hypocrite.'
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage. The author states the general ruling: it is makruh (disliked) for a person to leave a mosque after the adhan has been given, until he prays. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet ﷺ equating such leaving (without valid excuse) with hypocrisy. The passage then provides a detailed exception: if leaving the mosque serves to organize a congregation (e.g., to bring others or to go to one's own neighborhood mosque where the congregation is expected), then it is not makruh; in fact, it may be required. The commentary from al-'Inayah elaborates on scenarios: if the mosque is one's own neighborhood mosque, leaving without praying is always makruh; if it is not, and one's neighborhood mosque has not yet prayed, one may leave to join that congregation because praying in one's own neighborhood mosque is wajib (obligatory). The hadith from Ibn Majah reinforces that leaving without intending to return or for a valid need is a sign of hypocrisy.

Key Terms
مکروہ (makrūh): In this context, disliked but not prohibited; the act is blameworthy but not sinful enough to be haram.
منافق (munāfiq): Hypocrite; one who outwardly shows faith but inwardly disbelieves. The hadith uses this term to strongly discourage the act.
اذان (adhān): The call to prayer proclaimed by the mu'adhdhin at the beginning of each prayer time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under which of the following situations is it NOT makruh to leave a mosque after the adhan?
A) Leaving to go home because you are tired
B) Leaving to join your own neighborhood congregation that has not yet prayed
C) Leaving to buy something from a nearby store
D) Leaving after you have prayed the current prayer

Key Takeaway
Leaving the mosque after the adhan is makruh unless done for a genuine need with intention to return, or to organize or attend an obligatory congregation.

Ruling on Joining Maghrib Congregation After Performing It Alone
Ruling on joining Maghrib congregation after praying alone

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a person who has already performed Maghrib alone and then encounters a congregation, and explain why joining is prohibited.

Core Idea
Joining a Maghrib congregation after praying alone leads to either makruh or invalid prayer.

This passage addresses a nuanced scenario: a person has already prayed Maghrib individually, but then a congregation for the same prayer begins. Should he join? The author, likely commenting on Al-Hidayah, analyses two possible outcomes of joining and finds both problematic. Understanding this ruling requires careful attention to rak'ah counts and the Hanafi dislike of praying three rak'ahs of nafl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario
The act in question is joining a Maghrib congregation after having already performed the Maghrib fard alone. The person's fard is complete; his intention in joining would be nafl.
This is specific to Maghrib due to its odd rak'ah count.
2
Analyze the First Possible Outcome
If he joins and finishes with the imam (says salam after 3 rak'ahs), he will have performed 3 rak'ahs of nafl. In the Hanafi school, praying 3 rak'ahs of nafl is makruh tahrimi because it imitates the witr prayer, which is 3 rak'ahs and is obligatory (wajib).
The text calls this 'makruh'.
3
Analyze the Second Possible Outcome
If he joins but adds a fourth rak'ah after the imam finishes (to make an even number), he opposes the imam by not ending with him. This opposition invalidates the follower's prayer, as following the imam in all actions is a condition of validity.
The text says 'opposing the imam is not correct'.
4
Derive the Ruling
Since both options are invalid or severely disliked, the only sound conclusion is that he should not join the congregation at all. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is: do not join.
This ruling applies only to Maghrib; for 4-rak'ah prayers, joining after praying alone is permissible.
5
Confirm the Exception
For 4-rak'ah prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Isha), joining a congregation after having prayed alone is allowed. The follower's prayer becomes nafl, and 4 rak'ahs of nafl is not makruh. Furthermore, there is no need to add an extra rak'ah, so opposition to the imam does not occur.
This underscores the specificity of the Maghrib ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة ساتھ شریک ہو گیا تو دو ہی صورتیں ہیں یا تو امام کے ساتھ سلام پھیرے گا یا امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد ایک رکعت اور پڑھے گا تا کہ چار رکت ہو جائیں تین امام کے ساتھ اور ایک امام کے فارغ ہونے کے بعد پہلی صورت میں نفل کی تین رکعت ہوں گی حالانکہ تین رکعت نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے اور دوسری صورت میں امام کی مخالفت کرنا لازم آئے گا اور یہ بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ اگر کسی نے مغرب کی نماز تنہا ادا کر لی ، پھر جماعت کھڑی ہو گئی تو یہ شخص جماعت میں شرکت نہ کرے۔
Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer. If he joins (the imam) then there are two cases: either he will say salam with the imam, or after the imam finishes he will pray one more rak'ah so that it becomes four rak'ahs: three with the imam and one after the imam finishes. In the first case, he would have prayed three rak'ahs of nafl, and praying three rak'ahs of nafl is makruh. In the second case, opposing the imam becomes necessary, and that is also not correct. Therefore we said: if someone has performed Maghrib prayer alone, then a congregation starts, this person should not join the congregation.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a specific scenario within the chapter 'Idrak al-Faridah' (Catching the Obligatory Prayer). The issue concerns a person who has already performed Maghrib prayer individually and then encounters a congregation for the same prayer. The author, likely commenting on Al-Hidayah, outlines two possible outcomes if he joins: (1) He finishes with the imam, making his total prayer three rak'ahs of nafl on top of his already performed fard—but three rak'ahs of nafl is makruh (disliked) in the Hanafi school, as it resembles the witr prayer. (2) He adds a fourth rak'ah after the imam to make four, but this opposes the imam, which is invalid. Both options are problematic, so the ruling is that he should not join the congregation. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of avoiding both makruh and opposition to the imam.

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Supererogatory prayer beyond the obligatory.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked; legally reprehensible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person has already prayed Maghrib alone. A congregation for Maghrib then starts. What should he do according to this passage?
A) Join the congregation and complete with the imam.
B) Join the congregation and add an extra rak'ah after the imam.
C) Not join the congregation.
D) Leave the mosque immediately.

Key Takeaway
A person who has already performed Maghrib alone should not join a subsequent Maghrib congregation because it leads to either makruh three-rak'ah nafl or invalid opposition to the imam.

Leaving Mosque After Adhan When Already Prayed
Ruling on exiting mosque after adhan when already prayed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaving the mosque after the adhan when one has already prayed and distinguish between Zuhr/Isha and Asr/Maghrib/Fajr cases.

Core Idea
Leaving mosque after adhan is not always prohibited; it depends on avoiding suspicion and the prayer time.

A common assumption is that once the adhan is called, one must remain in the mosque until the congregation prays. But Hanafi fiqh provides nuanced exceptions. This lesson examines the ruling for a person who has already performed the obligatory prayer: when is it permissible to leave, and why does the prayer time matter?

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The general ruling is that leaving the mosque after the adhan without excuse is makruh tahrimi due to suspicion (tuhma) of neglecting prayer. This is based on a hadith prohibition.
2
Excuse for imam/mu'adhdhin
Al-Quduri notes that if the person is connected to another mosque (as imam or mu'adhdhin), leaving is permissible because the suspicion does not apply; people know they are going to lead or call elsewhere.
Outwardly leaving, but inwardly completing the service.
3
Case of already having prayed
If a person has already prayed the obligatory prayer of that time, further rules apply. For Zuhr and Isha, leaving is allowed unless the iqamah has started, because after iqamah the suspicion of opposing the congregation becomes manifest.
He has answered the caller once, but should not leave when iqamah begins.
4
Exception for Asr, Maghrib, Fajr
For Asr, Maghrib, and Fajr, leaving is allowed even after the iqamah begins. The reason is that if he joins, he would pray nafl (supererogatory) with the congregation, but nafl after these prayers is disliked (makruh). For Maghrib, three rak'ahs of nafl is disliked, and adding a fourth would oppose the imam.
The ruling balances avoiding suspicion and avoiding disliked acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة
۲۱۲
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
سے نکالا اور نہ کوٹ کر آنے کا ارادہ ہے تو وہ منافق ہے۔
صاحب قدوری نے کہا کہ اگر اس شخص سے کسی دوسری مسجد کی جماعت کا معاملہ متعلق ہو مثلا یہ امام ہو یا موذن تو اذان کے بعد بھی اس کے لئے نکلنا جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ نکلنا ظاہر اتو ترک ہے لیکن باطنا تکمیل ہے۔ رہا یہ اعتراض کہ حدیث سے ثابت ہوتا ہے کہ اذان کے بعد مسجد سے نکلنا مطلقا ممنوع ہے خواہ اس شخص سے متعلق دوسری کسی مسجد کا انتظام ہو یا نہ ہو۔
جواب حدیث میں مقصود ممانعت تہمت ہے یعنی اذان کے بعد مسجد سے نکلنے والے کو لوگ نماز سے اعراض کرنے کے ساتھ متہم کریں گے ۔ لیکن امام اور مؤذن کے حق میں یہ تہمت موجود نہیں ہے۔ یعنی ان دونوں کو بھی لوگ جانتے ہیں کہ یہ دوسری مسجد میں جماعت کا انتظام کریں گے اس لئے ان دونوں کے نکلنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے۔
اذان ہونے کے بعد ظہر اور عشاء کی نماز پڑھ چکا تھا تو مسجد سے نکلنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں
وان كان قد صلى وكانت الظهر والعشاء، فلاباس بان يخرج لانه اجاب داعى الله مرة الا اذا اخذ الموذن في الاقامة، لانه يتهم لمخالفة الجماعة عيانا وان كانت العصر والمغرب أو الفجر، خرج وان اخذ المؤذن فيها، لكراهية النفل بعدها.
ترجمہ اور اگر وہ اس وقت کی نماز پڑھ چکا ہو اور یہ نماز ظہر و عشاء کی ہو تو نکلنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ اس نے ایک مرتبہ اذان دینے والے کی دعوت کو قبول کر لیا ہے مگر جبکہ مؤذن اقامت کہنا شروع کر دے کیونکہ وہ بر ملا جماعت کی مخالفت کے ساتھ متہم ہوگا۔
اور اگر یہ نماز عصر یا مغرب یا فجر ہو تو نکل جائے اگر چہ مؤذن اقامت شروع کر دے کیونکہ ان نمازوں کے بعد نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ تشریح اس عبارت میں وہ صورت ذکر کی گئی ہے جس کے بیان کرنے کا وعدہ پہلے مسئلے میں کیا گیا ہے صورت یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص ایسی مسجد میں داخل ہوا ہے جس میں اذان دے دی گئی ہے اور یہ شخص یہ نماز پڑھ چکا ہے پس اگر یہ نماز جس کے لئے اذان دی گئی ہے اور یہ شخص اپنے گھر یا دوسری مسجد میں اس نماز کو پڑھ چکا ہے ظہر یا عشاء کی دو تو اس کے لئے مسجد سے نکلنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں کیونکہ اس نے ایک مرتبہ اللہ کے داعی یعنی موذن کی دعوت کو قبول کر لیا ہے۔ ہاں اگر مؤذن نے اقامت شروع کر دی تو اس صورت میں یہ شخص مسجد سے نہ نکلے بلکہ جماعت میں شیرک ہو جائے درانحالیکہ یہ اس نماز کو پڑھ چکا ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اقامت اور جماعت شروع ہونے کے بعد اگر نکلے گا تو لوگ مخالفت جماعت کے ساتھ تم کریں گے پس اتہام سے بچنے کے لئے جماعت کے اندر شامل ہو جائے۔ اور یہ نماز جو جماعت کے ساتھ ادا کرے گا نفل ہوگی کیونکہ یہ شخص فرض پہلے ادا کر چکا ہے لیکن وہ نماز اگر عصر یا مغرب یا فجر کی ہوا تو یہ شخص موذن کے اقامت شروع کر دینے کے بعد بھی مسجد سے نکل سکتا ہے کیونکہ یہ شخص فرض تو ادا ہی کر چکا ہے اب اگر جماعت میں شریک ہوگا تو یہ نماز نفل ہو گی۔ حالانکہ عصر اور فجر کے بعد نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے ۔ اور رہی مغرب کی نماز تو مغرب کے بعد نفل پڑھنا اگر چہ مکروہ نہیں لیکن امام کے ساتھ شریک ہونے کی وجہ سے تین رکعت نفل ہوں گی حالانکہ نفل تین رکعت پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور اگر آپ یہ کہیں کہ امام کے سلام پھیرنے کے بعد ایک رکعت اور پڑھ لے تا کہ چار رکعت ہو جائیں تو اس صورت میں امام کی مخالفت لازم آئے گی کیونکہ امام نے تین رکعت پر سلام پھیر یا ہے اور یہ چار رکعت پر پھیر رہا ہے حالانکہ امام کی مخالفت کرنا بھی درست نہیں ہے۔
Chapter on Catching the Obligatory Prayer. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu Sharh Hidayah Volume 2. He took it out and does not intend to return, then he is a hypocrite. Sahib al-Quduri said: If this person has a connection to another mosque's congregation, e.g. he is the imam or mu'adhdhin, then leaving after the adhan is permissible for him. Because this leaving is outwardly abandonment but inwardly completion. As for the objection that the hadith proves leaving the mosque after adhan is absolutely prohibited, whether he has any connection to another mosque's management or not. The answer is that in the hadith, the intended prohibition is due to suspicion, i.e., people will suspect the one leaving after adhan of turning away from prayer. But in the case of the imam and mu'adhdhin, this suspicion does not exist. That is, people know that these two will manage the congregation in another mosque, so there is no harm in their leaving. If he had prayed Zuhr or Isha after the adhan, there is no harm in leaving the mosque. And if he had prayed and it was Zuhr or Isha, there is no harm in leaving because he answered the caller of Allah once, unless the mu'adhdhin starts the iqamah, because he will be suspected of openly opposing the congregation. And if it was Asr, Maghrib, or Fajr, he may leave even if the mu'adhdhin starts the iqamah, due to the dislike of supererogatory prayer after them. Translation: And if he had prayed the prayer of that time and it was Zuhr or Isha, there is no harm in leaving because he answered the caller once, but when the mu'adhdhin starts the iqamah, he will be suspected of openly opposing the congregation. And if it was Asr, Maghrib, or Fajr, he may leave even if the mu'adhdhin starts the iqamah, because supererogatory prayer after them is disliked. Explanation: In this passage, the case promised earlier is mentioned. It is that a person entered a mosque where the adhan has been given and he has already prayed that prayer. So if the prayer for which the adhan was given, and he has prayed it at home or in another mosque, is Zuhr or Isha, there is no harm in him leaving the mosque because he answered the caller once. Yes, if the mu'adhdhin starts the iqamah, then he should not leave but join the congregation even though he has prayed this prayer. The proof is that if he leaves after the iqamah and congregation have started, people will suspect him of opposing the congregation, so to avoid suspicion he should join the congregation. And this prayer he performs with the congregation will be supererogatory because he already performed the obligatory prayer. But if that prayer was Asr, Maghrib, or Fajr, he may leave the mosque even after the mu'adhdhin starts the iqamah, because he has already performed the obligatory prayer; if he joins the congregation, it will be supererogatory, whereas supererogatory prayer after Asr and Fajr is disliked. As for Maghrib, supererogatory after Maghrib is not disliked, but due to joining the imam, three rak'ahs of supererogatory would be performed, whereas three rak'ahs of supererogatory is disliked. And if you say that after the imam says salam, he should pray one more rak'ah to make it four, then opposing the imam would be necessary because the imam said salam after three rak'ahs and he is saying salam after four, while opposing the imam is not correct.
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding leaving the mosque after the adhan when one has already performed the obligatory prayer. The author first presents the ruling from al-Quduri: if a person has a connection to another mosque (as imam or mu'adhdhin), leaving after adhan is permissible despite the general prohibition, because the reason for prohibition (suspicion of neglecting prayer) does not apply. The hadith's prohibition is based on avoiding suspicion, not absolute prohibition. Then the text addresses the case of a person who has already prayed. For Zuhr and Isha, leaving is allowed unless the iqamah has started, because after iqamah, leaving would cause open suspicion of opposing the congregation. For Asr, Maghrib, and Fajr, leaving is allowed even after iqamah because performing nafl (supererogatory) after these prayers is disliked, so joining the congregation would lead to a disliked act. The author further explains the reasoning for Maghrib: if one joins, he would pray three rak'ahs of nafl with the imam, and three rak'ahs of nafl is disliked. Adding a fourth rak'ah after the imam's salam would require opposing the imam by saying salam later, which is also not allowed. Thus the ruling preserves both avoiding suspicion and avoiding disliked acts.

Key Terms
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer announcing the start of the obligatory prayer time.
اقامت (iqamah): The second call immediately before the obligatory prayer begins, signaling the congregation is about to start.
تهمت (tuhma): Suspicion or accusation; here it refers to people suspecting the person of neglecting prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible for a person who has already prayed Asr to leave the mosque even after the iqamah has started?
A) Because Asr is a short prayer
B) Because nafl prayer after Asr is disliked
C) Because people will not suspect him
D) Because the adhan for Asr is not valid

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits leaving the mosque after adhan when one has already prayed, with detailed conditions based on prayer time and the start of iqamah, all to balance avoiding suspicion and avoiding disliked acts.

Praying Sunnah of Fajr When Catching the Congregation
Ruling on praying Sunnah of Fajr when catching congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying the Sunnah of Fajr when entering the congregation and correctly apply the two scenarios based on fear of missing rak'ahs.

Core Idea
Combine both virtues: pray Sunnah at door if you catch at least one rak'ah, otherwise join immediately.

When you enter the mosque and the imam is leading Fajr, you face a dilemma: pray the highly emphasized Sunnah or join the congregation? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on how many rak'ahs you will catch. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its proof, and contrasts it with the Sunnah of Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two possibilities
Determine whether you fear missing one rak'ah (i.e., you will catch the other) or fear missing the entire second rak'ah. The text uses 'khashiya' (fear) – it means reasonable expectation.
2
Apply the ruling for each case
If only one rak'ah will be missed: pray Sunnah at the mosque door then join. If both may be missed: skip Sunnah and join immediately.
The Sunnah is prayed at the door, not inside, to avoid suspicion.
3
Contrast with Zuhr and note the intra-Hanafi difference
For Zuhr, the Sunnah is left in both cases because it can be made up after fard. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed on ordering of Zuhr's four rak'ahs, but for Fajr there is no difference.
This contrast highlights the special status of Fajr Sunnah.
4
Examine the proof from hadith
The hadith 'Pray them even if horses trample you' and 'Two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world' show the high virtue, justifying priority in the first scenario. The greater reward of congregation overrides in the second.
Catching one rak'ah is like catching the whole prayer.
5
Extract the general principle about sunan in the mosque
The restriction to the door indicates dislike of praying Sunnah inside while imam is praying. The best place for all sunan is at home.
Based on hadith: 'The best prayer is in one's home, except for the obligatory.'

و من انتهى الى الامام فى صلوة الفجر وهو لم يصل ركعتي الفجر، ان خش ان تفوته ركعة ويدرك الاخرى، يصلى ركعتي الفجر عند باب المسجد، ثم يدخل لانه امكنه الجمع بين الفضيلتين، وان خشى فوتها دخل مع الامام لان ثواب الجماعة اعظم والوعيد بالترك الزم، بخلاف سنة الظهر حيث يتركها في الحالين لانه يمكنه اداؤها فى الوقت بعد الفرض هو الصحيح، وانما الاختلاف بين ابي يوسف ومحمد في تقديمها على الركعتين وتاخيرها عنهما ، ولا كذلك سنة الفجر على ما نبين ان شاء الله تعالى والتقييد بالاداء عند باب المسجد يدل على الكراهية في المسجد اذا كان الامام في الصلاة والافضل فى عامة السنن والنوافل المنزل، هو المروى عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم
ترجمہ اور اگر ایک شخص جا پہنچا امام تک تماز فجر میں اور اس نے فجر کی دو رکعت (سنت) نہیں پڑھی ہیں ( پس ) اگر اس کو خوف ہو کہ ایک رکعت فوت ہو جائے گی اور دوسری رکعت ( امام کے ساتھ ) پالے گا تو فجر کی دورکعت سنت مسجد کے دروازے پر پڑھے پھر (جماعت میں شامل ہو کیونکہ اس کو دونوں فضیلتیں جمع کر لینا ممکن ہے اور اگر اس کو دوسری رکعت فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو تو امام کے ساتھ داخل ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ جماعت کا ثواب بہت بڑا ہے اور جماعت ترک کرنے کی وعید الزم ( بڑی سخت) ہے۔ بخلاف سنت ظہر کے کہ ان کو دونوں حالتوں میں چھوڑ دے کیونکہ سنت ظہر کا فرض کے بعد وقت کے اند ر ادا کرناممکن ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔ اور اختلاف ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان ان چار رکعتوں کو دورکعتوں پر مقدم کرنے اور ان دو سے مؤخر کرنے میں ہے اور یہ حال سنت فجر میں نہیں ہے چنانچہ ہم انشاء اللہ بیان کریں گے۔ اور سنت فجر کو مسجد کے دروازے پر ادا کرنے کی قید لگانا دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مسجد کے اندر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے بشرطیکہ امام نماز میں ہو ۔ اور افضل ، عام سفن اور نوافل میں گھر ہے یہی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے مروی ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص اس وقت مسجد میں داخل ہوا جب کہ امام نماز فجر پڑھارہا تھا اور یہ شخص ابھی تک سنت فجر نہیں پڑھ سکتا تھا تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص بغیر سنت فجر پڑھے جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے یا پہلے سنت پڑھے پھر جماعت میں شریک ہو۔ اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ خوف ہو کہ اگر پہلے سنت پڑھی تو فرض کی ایک رکعت فوت ہو جائے گی اور دوسری رکعت پالے گا تو ایسی صورت میں پہلے مسجد کے دروازے کے پاس فجر کی سنتیں پڑھے پھر امام کے ساتھ شریک جماعت ہو۔

Ruling on praying the Sunnah of Fajr during the congregation. And whoever reaches the imam in the Fajr prayer while he has not prayed the two rak'ahs of Fajr, if he fears that one rak'ah will be missed and he will catch the other, he prays the two rak'ahs of Fajr at the door of the mosque, then enters because it is possible for him to combine both virtues. And if he fears missing it (the second rak'ah), he enters with the imam because the reward of congregation is greater and the threat for leaving it is more severe. Unlike the Sunnah of Zuhr, where he leaves it in both cases because it is possible to perform it after the obligatory prayer within the time. This is the correct view. The difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is regarding giving precedence to these four rak'ahs over the two rak'ahs or delaying them after them. And this is not the case with the Sunnah of Fajr, as we will explain, Allah willing. And the restriction to performing it at the door of the mosque indicates the dislike of performing it inside the mosque when the imam is in prayer. And the best for all sunan and nawafil is at home, as narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Translation: And if a person reaches the imam in the Fajr prayer and he has not prayed the two rak'ahs of Fajr (sunnah), then if he fears that one rak'ah will be missed and he will catch the other, he prays the two rak'ahs of Fajr at the door of the mosque, then joins the congregation because it is possible for him to combine both virtues. And if he fears missing it, he enters with the imam because the reward of congregation is greater and the threat for leaving it is very severe. Unlike the Sunnah of Zuhr, which he leaves in both cases, because it is possible to perform it after the obligatory prayer within the time. This is the correct view. The difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is regarding giving precedence to these four rak'ahs over the two rak'ahs or delaying them after them. And this is not the case with the Sunnah of Fajr, as we will explain, Allah willing. And the restriction to performing the Sunnah of Fajr at the door of the mosque indicates that performing it inside the mosque is disliked provided that the imam is in prayer. And the best for all sunan and nawafil is at home, as narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Explanation: The scenario is that a person entered the mosque while the imam was leading the Fajr prayer and he had not yet prayed the Sunnah of Fajr. The question is whether he should join the congregation without praying the Sunnah or pray the Sunnah first then join. The ruling is: if he fears that if he prays the Sunnah first, he will miss one rak'ah of the obligatory prayer and catch the other, then in such a case he should pray the Sunnah of Fajr near the door of the mosque first, then join the imam. The proof is that the Sunnah of Fajr is the strongest and best among the sunnah prayers. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Pray them even if the horses trample you.' And he said: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and what it contains.' And catching one rak'ah with the imam is like catching the whole prayer because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever...'
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the Sunnah of Fajr when one arrives at the mosque while the imam is leading the Fajr congregation and has not yet prayed the Sunnah. The author first presents the ruling from the matn: if the person fears missing only one rak'ah (i.e., he can catch at least one rak'ah with the imam), he should pray the two rak'ahs of Sunnah at the mosque door, then join the congregation. This allows him to combine the virtue of the Sunnah (which is highly emphasized) and the virtue of congregation. If he fears missing the entire second rak'ah (i.e., he will only catch less than one rak'ah), then he should skip the Sunnah and join the congregation immediately, because the reward of congregation outweighs the Sunnah. The author contrasts this with the Sunnah of Zuhr, which is left in both cases because it can be made up after the obligatory prayer within its time. Then a subtle intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is noted: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed regarding the four rak'ahs before Zuhr (i.e., the sunnah mu'akkadah) — whether to give precedence to them over the two rak'ahs or delay? But for Fajr, there is no such difference. Finally, the author extracts a ruling from the text's wording: the restriction to praying at the door (not inside) indicates that praying the Sunnah inside the mosque while the imam is praying is disliked. The best place for all sunan and nawafil is at home, as per hadith. The commentary provides the proof: hadith emphasizing the virtue of Fajr Sunnah and the principle that catching one rak'ah is like catching the whole prayer.

Key Terms
سنت فجر (sunnah al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayer performed before the obligatory Fajr prayer; highly emphasized (sunnah mu'akkadah).
ركعة (rak'ah): One unit of prayer consisting of bowing (ruku') and two prostrations (sajdah).
فضیلت (fadilat): Virtue or merit; here refers to the reward of the Sunnah prayer and the reward of congregational prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for a person who enters the mosque during Fajr congregation, has not prayed the Sunnah, and fears missing only one rak'ah?
A) He should join the congregation immediately without praying the Sunnah.
B) He should pray the Sunnah at the mosque door, then join the congregation.
C) He should pray the Sunnah inside the mosque, then join.
D) He should leave and pray Fajr alone.

Key Takeaway
The Sunnah of Fajr is prayed at the mosque door if only one rak'ah will be missed; otherwise, join the congregation immediately.

Ruling on Performing Sunnah of Fajr When Catching the Congregation
Ruling on Sunnah Fajr when catching congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a latecomer to Fajr congregation who has not prayed the Sunnah, and apply the distinction between fearing loss of one rak'ah versus both.

Core Idea
If you can catch at least one rak'ah, pray Sunnah first; if not, join immediately.

This lesson addresses a common scenario: you arrive at the mosque for Fajr, the imam is already leading the prayer, and you haven't prayed the two rak'ahs of Sunnah. What should you do? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on how much of the fard you can still catch. The ruling is supported by strong hadith evidence and also contrasts with the Sunnah of Zuhr, where the priority is different. We will walk through the proofs and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between (1) fearing loss of only one rak'ah (i.e., you can catch at least one) and (2) fearing loss of both rak'ahs of the fard. The ruling depends on which scenario applies.
The key phrase is 'fear of missing' (khashiya).
2
Apply the ruling for Fajr
For scenario 1: pray the Sunnah at the door of the mosque, then join. For scenario 2: join immediately without praying the Sunnah.
The text says 'then enters' meaning join the congregation.
3
Understand the proofs
The text cites hadiths on the virtue of Sunnah of Fajr, the virtue of catching one rak'ah (equals catching the whole prayer), and the severe threat for abandoning congregation. The balance is between two virtues (faḍīlatān).
The hadith 'Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr has caught the prayer' is key for scenario 1.
4
Contrast with Zuhr Sunnah
For Zuhr, regardless of scenario, one leaves the Sunnah and joins, because the Sunnah of Zuhr can be made up after the fard within the time. This is the correct view (sahih).
The contrast highlights that Fajr Sunnah is more strongly emphasized.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ on the order of making up missed Sunnah of Zuhr (four before versus two after). The text presents both views without preference.
This dispute does not affect the Fajr ruling.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد دوم
باب ادراك الفريضة

و من انتهى الى الامام فى صلوة الفجر وهو لم يصل ركعتي الفجر، ان خش ان تفوته ركعة ويدرك الاخرى، يصلى ركعتي الفجر عند باب المسجد، ثم يدخل لانه امكنه الجمع بين الفضيلتين، وان خشى فوتها دخل مع الامام لان ثواب الجماعة اعظم والوعيد بالترك الزم، بخلاف سنة الظهر حيث يتركها في الحالين لانه يمكنه اداؤها فى الوقت بعد الفرض هو الصحيح، وانما الاختلاف بين ابي يوسف ومحمد في تقديمها على الركعتين وتاخيرها عنهما ، ولا كذلك سنة الفجر على ما نبين ان شاء الله تعالى والتقييد بالاداء عند باب المسجد يدل على الكراهية في المسجد اذا كان الامام في الصلاة والافضل فى عامة السنن والنوافل المنزل، هو المروى عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم

ترجمہ اور اگر ایک شخص جا پہنچا امام تک نماز فجر میں اور اس نے فجر کی دو رکعت (سنت) نہیں پڑھی ہیں ( پس ) اگر اس کو خوف ہو کہ ایک رکعت فوت ہو جائے گی اور دوسری رکعت ( امام کے ساتھ ) پالے گا تو فجر کی دو رکعت سنت مسجد کے دروازے پر پڑھے پھر (جماعت میں شامل ہو کیونکہ اس کو دونوں فضیلتیں جمع کر لینا ممکن ہے اور اگر اس کو دوسری رکعت فوت ہونے کا خوف ہو تو امام کے ساتھ داخل ہو جائے ۔ کیونکہ جماعت کا ثواب بہت بڑا ہے اور جماعت ترک کرنے کی وعید الزم ( بڑی سخت) ہے۔ بخلاف سنت ظہر کے کہ ان کو دونوں حالتوں میں چھوڑ دے کیونکہ سنت ظہر کا فرض کے بعد وقت کے اندر ادا کرنا ممکن ہے یہی صحیح ہے۔ اور اختلاف ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے درمیان ان چار رکعتوں کو دو رکعتوں پر مقدم کرنے اور ان دو سے مؤخر کرنے میں ہے اور یہ حال سنت فجر میں نہیں ہے چنانچہ ہم انشاء اللہ بیان کریں گے۔ اور سنت فجر کو مسجد کے دروازے پر ادا کرنے کی قید لگانا دلالت کرتا ہے کہ مسجد کے اندر ادا کرنا مکروہ ہے بشرطیکہ امام نماز میں ہو ۔ اور افضل، عام سنن اور نوافل میں گھر ہے یہی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم سے مروی ہے۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص اس وقت مسجد میں داخل ہوا جب کہ امام نماز فجر پڑھارہا تھا اور یہ شخص ابھی تک سنت فجر نہیں پڑھ سکتا تھا تو اب سوال یہ ہے کہ یہ شخص بغیر سنت فجر پڑھے جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے یا پہلے سنت پڑھے پھر جماعت میں شریک ہو۔ اس کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر یہ خوف ہو کہ اگر پہلے سنت پڑھی تو فرض کی ایک رکعت فوت ہو جائے گی اور دوسری رکعت پالے گا تو ایسی صورت میں پہلے مسجد کے دروازے کے پاس فجر کی سنتیں پڑھے پھر امام کے ساتھ شریک جماعت ہو۔
دلیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ سنت فجر سنتوں میں اقوی اور افضل ہے۔ چنانچہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا صلوهما و ان طردتكم الخيل - یعنی فجر کی دو رکعت سنت پڑھو اگر چہ تم کو گھوڑے روند ڈالیں اور فرمایا کہ ركعتا الفجر خير من الدنيا و ما فيها یعنی فجر کی دو رکعت سنت دنیا اور مافیہا سے بہتر ہیں اور فجر کی ایک رکعت کو امام کے ساتھ پانا ایسا ہے جیسے کل کو پایا کیونکہ اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے من ادرك ركعة من الفجر فقد ادرك الصلوۃ یعنی جس نے فجر کی ایک رکعت کو پالیا گویا پوری نماز کو پالیا۔ ( عنایہ ) پس یہاں دونوں فضیلتوں یعنی سنت فجر کی فضیلت اور جماعت کی فضیلت کو جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اس لئے جماعت میں شریک ہونے سے پہلے فجر کی دو رکعت سنت ادا کرے پھر جماعت میں شریک ہو تا کہ دونوں فضیلتیں حاصل ہو جائیں۔
اور اگر اس کو یہ خوف ہو کہ اگر سنت فجر پڑھنے میں مشغول ہوگیا تو فجر کی دونوں رکعتیں فوت ہو جائیں گی تو ایسی صورت میں یہ حکم ہے کہ سنت فجر پڑھے بغیر امام کے ساتھ جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے کیونکہ جماعت کا ثواب بہت بڑا ہے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے صلوة الجماعة تفضل صلوة المنفرد بسبع و عشرين درجة یعنی جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا تنہا پڑھنے کی نسبت ستائیس درجہ افضل ہے اور جماعت چھوڑنے پر سخت وعید آئی ہے۔ چنانچہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تارک الجماعة ملعون جماعت چھوڑنے والا ملعون ہے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لقد همت ان استخلف من صلى بالناس وانظر الى من لم يحضر الجماعة فامر بعض فتيان بان يحرقوا بيوتهم یعنی میں نے ارادہ کیا کہ کسی کو خلیفہ بناؤں تا کہ وہ لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے اور میں ان لوگوں کو دیکھوں جو جماعت میں شریک نہیں ہوئے پھر کچھ نوجوانوں کو حکم دوں کہ وہ ان کے گھروں کو جلا ڈالیں۔ حاصل دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب جماعت کا ثواب بھی زیادہ ہے اور ترک جماعت پر وعید بھی آئی ہے تو یہ شخص جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے اور سنت فجر کو چھوڑ دے۔ اور یہی صورت اگر سنت ظہر میں پیش آگئی یعنی ایک آدمی بغیر سنت ظہر پڑھے مسجد میں اس وقت داخل ہوا جبکہ امام نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اب یہ آدمی سنت ظہر پہلے ادا کرے اور پھر جماعت میں شامل ہو یا پہلے جماعت میں شامل ہو اور سنت ظہر کو چھوڑ دے تو اس بارے میں فاضل مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ظہر کی سنتوں میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے امام کے ساتھ ظہر کی پوری نماز فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو یا بعض کے فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو دونوں حالتوں میں ظہر کی سنتیں چھوڑ دے اور جماعت میں شامل ہو جائے کیونکہ وقت کے اندر اندر فرض کے بعد ظہر کی سنتوں کا ادا کرنا ممکن ہے پس جب ظہر کے فرضوں کے بعد سنتوں کا ادا کرنا ممکن ہے تو ان سنتوں کی وجہ سے فضیلت جماعت کو کیوں چھوڑے یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر سے پہلے کی چار سنتیں فوت ہو گئیں تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر کے بعد ان کی قضا فرمائی اس کو حضرت عائشہ سے روایت کیا گیا ہے۔ (عنایہ) ظہر کی سنت فرض سے پہلے نہ ادا کر سکا تو کب پڑھے البتہ اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ جب ظہر سے پہلے کی سنت فوت ہوگئی تو ظہر کے بعد کی دو رکعتوں سے پہلے ان کی قضاء کرے یا ان دو رکعتوں کے بعد قضاء کرے اس بارے میں امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ پہلے ظہر کے بعد کی دو رکعت سنت ادا کرے پھر ظہر سے پہلے کی چار رکعت سنت کی قضاء کرے اور امام محمد نے کہا کہ پہلے چار رکعت کی قضاء کرے پھر ظہر کے بعد کی دو رکعت پڑھے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ چار رکعت تو اپنے موضع مسنون یعنی قبل الظہر سے فوت ہو ہی گئیں ہیں تو بعد کی دو رکعت کو ان کی جگہ سے فوت نہ کرے بلکہ ان کو ظہر کے بعد ادا کرے اور ظہر سے پہلے کی چار کو ان کے بعد پڑھے دنیا کے قانون میں بھی اس کی نظیر ملتی ہے آپ حضرات نے مشاہدہ کیا ہوگا کہ اگر اسٹیشن پر دو گاڑیوں کا کراس ہو جائے تو ریلوے کا قانون یہ ہے کہ جو گاڑی اسٹیشن پر پہلے آتی ہے اس کو بعد میں چھوڑا جاتا ہے اور جو بعد میں آتی ہے اس کو پہلے روانہ کر دیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ جو گاڑی اسٹیشن پر پہلے سے آکر کھڑی ہوگئی ہے تو اپنے وقت سے لیٹ ہو ہی گئی ہے لیکن جو بعد میں آئی ہے اس کو خواہ مخواہ کیوں لیٹ کیا جائے اس لئے پہلے بعد میں آنے والی کو روانہ کرو۔
And whoever reaches the imam in the Fajr prayer while he has not prayed the two rak'ahs of Fajr (Sunnah), if he fears that one rak'ah will be missed and he catches the other, he prays the two rak'ahs of Fajr at the door of the mosque, then enters, because it is possible for him to combine both virtues. And if he fears missing them (both), he enters with the imam, because the reward of congregation is greater and the threat for leaving it is more severe. Contrary to the Sunnah of Zuhr, which he leaves in both situations, because it is possible for him to perform it after the fard within the time; that is the correct view. The difference between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is regarding giving precedence to the four (Sunnah before Zuhr) over the two (Sunnah after Zuhr) or delaying them after the two. It is not the same for the Sunnah of Fajr, as we will explain, God willing. Restricting the performance at the door of the mosque indicates that it is disliked inside the mosque when the imam is praying. The best for all Sunnahs and Nawafil is at home; this is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Translation: And if a person reaches the imam in the Fajr prayer and he has not prayed the two rak'ahs of Fajr (Sunnah), if he fears that one rak'ah will be missed and he will catch the other, he should pray the two rak'ahs of Sunnah at the door of the mosque, then join the congregation because it is possible for him to combine both virtues. And if he fears missing the other rak'ah, he should enter with the imam, because the reward of congregation is great and the threat for leaving it is severe. Contrary to the Sunnah of Zuhr, which he leaves in both situations, because the Sunnah of Zuhr can be performed after the fard within the time. That is the correct view. The difference between Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad is regarding giving precedence to the four rak'ahs over the two or delaying them after the two, and this situation does not apply to the Sunnah of Fajr, as we will explain, God willing. Restricting the performance of Sunnah of Fajr at the door of the mosque indicates that it is disliked inside the mosque, provided the imam is in prayer. The best for all Sunnahs and Nawafil is at home; this is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Explanation: The case is that a person entered the mosque while the imam was leading the Fajr prayer and this person had not yet prayed the Sunnah of Fajr. So the question is whether he should join the congregation without praying the Sunnah of Fajr or pray the Sunnah first and then join. The ruling is: if he fears that if he prays the Sunnah first, one rak'ah of the fard will be missed and he will catch the other, then in such a case he should first pray the Sunnah of Fajr at the door of the mosque and then join the imam in congregation.
The proof for this is that the Sunnah of Fajr is the strongest and most virtuous of the Sunnahs. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Pray them even if the horses trample you" – meaning the two rak'ahs of Sunnah of Fajr, even if horses trample you. And he said: "The two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and all that is in it." And catching one rak'ah with the imam is like catching the whole (prayer), because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "Whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr has caught the prayer." So here, it is possible to combine both virtues, so before joining the congregation he should pray the two rak'ahs of Sunnah of Fajr, then join the congregation so that both virtues are attained.
And if he fears that if he occupies himself with praying the Sunnah of Fajr, both rak'ahs of Fajr fard will be missed, then in such a case the ruling is that he should join the congregation without praying the Sunnah of Fajr, because the reward of congregation is very great. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: "The prayer of congregation is superior to the prayer of an individual by twenty-seven degrees." And a severe threat has come for leaving the congregation. Thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "The one who leaves the congregation is cursed." And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "I considered appointing someone to lead the people in prayer and then look at those who do not attend the congregation, and order some young men to burn their houses." The summary of the proof is that when the reward of congregation is greater and there is a threat for leaving it, this person should join the congregation and leave the Sunnah of Fajr.
And if this same situation occurs regarding the Sunnah of Zuhr – that is, a man enters the mosque without having prayed the Sunnah of Zuhr while the imam is leading the prayer – should he perform the Sunnah of Zuhr first and then join the congregation, or join the congregation first and leave the Sunnah of Zuhr? Regarding this, the author said: Whether he fears missing the entire Zuhr prayer with the imam due to engaging in the Sunnah, or fears missing part of it, in both situations he should leave the Sunnah of Zuhr and join the congregation, because it is possible to perform the Sunnah of Zuhr after the fard within the time. So when it is possible to perform the Sunnah after the fard, why should he leave the virtue of congregation for the sake of these Sunnahs? This is the correct view. Because once the Prophet (peace be upon him) missed the four rak'ahs (Sunnah) before Zuhr, so he made them up after Zuhr. This is narrated from Aisha. (Uyoon) When the Sunnah of Zuhr could not be performed before the fard, then when should it be performed? There is a difference of opinion regarding this: when the Sunnah before Zuhr is missed, should one make it up before the two rak'ahs after Zuhr or after those two? Regarding this, Imam Abu Yusuf's madhhab is that he should first perform the two rak'ahs of Sunnah after Zuhr, then make up the four rak'ahs of Sunnah before Zuhr. Imam Muhammad said that he should first make up the four rak'ahs, then perform the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that these four rak'ahs have already missed their prescribed place, i.e., before Zuhr, so he should not cause the two rak'ahs (after Zuhr) to miss their place; rather, he should perform them (the two) after Zuhr, and then perform the four after them. There is an analogy in worldly law: you may have observed that if two trains cross at a station, the railway law is that the train that arrives earlier at the station is released later, and the one that arrives later is dispatched first, because the train that has already arrived at the station is already late from its time, but why should the one that arrived later be unnecessarily delayed? So dispatch the later one first.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is an expansion on the chapter 'Catching the Obligatory Prayer' (Bāb Idrāk al-Farīḍah). The author presents the ruling for a person who arrives at the mosque for Fajr prayer while the imam is leading the congregation, and he has not yet performed the two rak'ahs of Sunnah of Fajr. The key distinction is based on how much of the fard prayer he can still catch. The author explains that if he fears missing only one rak'ah of the fard (meaning he can catch at least one), he should first perform the Sunnah of Fajr at the door of the mosque (to avoid disturbing the congregation) and then join, because he can combine the virtue of the Sunnah with the virtue of congregation. However, if he fears missing both rak'ahs of the fard, he should join immediately without performing the Sunnah, because the reward of congregation outweighs that of the Sunnah, and leaving congregation entails a severe threat. This ruling is supported by several hadiths: the virtue of Sunnah of Fajr (even under hardship), the virtue of catching one rak'ah meaning catching the whole prayer, and the severe warnings against abandoning congregation. The author then contrasts this with the Sunnah of Zuhr: in both scenarios (fearing loss of one or both rak'ahs), one should leave the Sunnah of Zuhr and join the congregation, because the Sunnah of Zuhr can be performed after the fard within the time. This is the correct view (sahih). He also notes an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the order of making up missed Sunnah of Zuhr: if the four rak'ahs before Zuhr are missed, should one perform them before or after the two rak'ahs after Zuhr? Abu Yusuf argues to perform the two-rak'ah Sunnah after Zuhr first (as they are still in their time), then make up the four; Muhammad argues to make up the four first. The author does not weigh in on this dispute but presents it with analogy.

Key Terms
ادراك الفريضة (idrāk al-farīḍah): The chapter on catching the obligatory prayer, i.e., joining the congregation after it has started.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of Sunnah before the Fajr fard prayer, considered sunnah mu'akkadah.
فضيلتان (faḍīlatān): The two virtues: of performing the Sunnah of Fajr and of joining the congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person enters the mosque for Fajr while the imam is in the first rak'ah. He has not prayed the Sunnah. He fears that if he prays the Sunnah, he will miss the first rak'ah but can catch the second. According to the Hanafi school, what should he do?
A) Pray the Sunnah at the door of the mosque then join the congregation.
B) Join the congregation immediately without praying the Sunnah.
C) Pray the Sunnah inside the mosque then join.
D) Wait for the next congregation.

Key Takeaway
For Fajr, if you can catch at least one rak'ah with the imam, pray the Sunnah first; if not, skip it and join immediately.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
Hanafi Ruling on Fajr Sunnah When Fear of Missing Congregation
Ruling on performing Fajr sunnah when catching the congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when fear of missing the Fajr fard conflicts with the sunnah, apply the principle that congregation trumps sunnah in such cases, and cite the supporting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
When congregation is at risk, the Fajr sunnah is dropped to preserve the obligation and greater reward.

This passage from Al-Hidayah's commentary addresses a common dilemma: you arrive at the mosque for Fajr, the congregation is about to begin or has started. Do you pray the two rak'ahs of sunnah first, or join the imam immediately? The Hanafi school provides a clear prioritization based on the weight of evidence, balancing the virtues of sunnah and congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios in the passage
First scenario: it is possible to pray the sunnah and still catch the congregation (normal case). Second scenario: there is a genuine fear that praying the sunnah will cause you to miss the entire fard (exceptional case).
Distinguish between fear of missing some rak'ahs vs. the entire fard.
2
Recognize the default ruling
In the normal case, you should pray the Fajr sunnah first, then join the congregation to obtain both virtues.
This is the ideal when time permits.
3
Recognize the exception
If you fear that engaging in the sunnah will result in losing both rak'ahs of Fajr fard, you must skip the sunnah and join the congregation immediately.
The condition is genuine fear of complete loss of the fard.
4
Analyze the evidence
The commentator cites hadiths about the 27-fold superiority of congregation and severe threats for abandoning it, which outweigh the virtue of the sunnah.
The hadith of burning houses shows the extreme emphasis on congregation.
5
Extract the Hanafi principle
Preserving a wajib (the fard) and obtaining the greater reward of congregation takes precedence over a sunnah when conflict is unavoidable.
This is consistent with the Hanafi prioritization of obligations over supererogatory acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ادراك الفريضة
ادرك ركعة من الفجر فقد ادرك الصلوۃ یعنی جس نے فجر کی ایک رکعت کو پالیا۔ گویا پوری نماز کو پالیا۔ ( عنا یہ ) پس یہاں دونوں فضیلتوں یعنی سنت فجر کی فضیلت اور جماعت کی فضیلت کو جمع کرنا ممکن ہے اس لئے جماعت میں شریک ہونے سے پہلے فجر کی 10 رکعت سنت ادا کرے پھر جماعت میں شریک ہوتا کہ دونوں فضیلتیں حاصل ہو جائیں۔
اور اگر اس کو یہ خوف ہو کہ اگر سنت فجر پڑھنے میں مشغول ہوگیا تو فجر کی دونوں رکھتیں [رکعتیں] فوت ہو جائیں گی تو ایسی صورت میں یہ حکم ہے کہ سنت فجر پڑھے بغیر امام کے ساتھ جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے کیونکہ جماعت کا ثواب بہت بڑا ہے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے صلوة الجماعة تفضل صلوة المنفرد بسبع و عشرين درجة یعنی جماعت کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا تنہا پڑھنے کی نسبت ستائیس درجہ افضل ہے اور جماعت چھوڑنے پر سخت وعید آئی ہے۔ چنانچہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ تارک الجماعة ملعون جماعت چھوڑنے والا ملعون ہے اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لقد همت ان استخلف من صلى بالناس وانظر الى من لم يحضر الجماعة فامر بعض فتيان بان يحرقوا بيوتهم یعنی میں نے ارادہ کیا کہ کسی کو خلیفہ بناؤں تا کہ وہ لوگوں کو نماز بڑھائے اور میں ان لوگوں کو دیکھوں جو جماعت میں شریک نہیں ہوئے پھر کچھ نو جوانوں کو حکم دوں کہ وہ ان کے گھروں کو جلا ڈالیں۔ حاصل دلیل یہ ہے کہ جب جماعت کا ثواب بھی زیادہ ہے اور ترک جماعت پر وعید بھی آئی ہے تو یہ شخص جماعت میں شریک ہو جائے اور سنت فجر کو چھوڑ دے۔
Chapter of Catching the Obligatory Prayer: Whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr has caught the prayer. That is, whoever catches one rak'ah of Fajr has caught the entire prayer. (From 'Inayah) So here it is possible to combine both virtues: the virtue of Fajr sunnah and the virtue of congregation. Therefore, before joining the congregation, he should perform the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah, then join the congregation so that both virtues are obtained. But if he fears that if he engages in performing the Fajr sunnah, both rak'ahs of Fajr will be missed, then in such a case the ruling is that he should join the congregation with the imam without performing the Fajr sunnah, because the reward of congregation is very great. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The prayer of congregation is superior to the prayer of an individual by twenty-seven degrees.' And a severe threat has come for abandoning congregation. Thus, the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The one who abandons congregation is accursed.' And the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'I almost intended to appoint someone to lead the people in prayer and then look at those who do not attend the congregation, then order some young men to burn their houses.' The conclusion of the proof is that when the reward of congregation is greater and there is a threat for abandoning it, this person should join the congregation and leave the Fajr sunnah.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the ruling on performing the Fajr sunnah when one catches the congregation. It begins by citing the well-known principle from the hadith: 'Whoever catches a rak'ah of Fajr has caught the prayer.' Normally, one should pray the Fajr sunnah before joining the congregation to combine the virtues of both the sunnah and the jama'ah. However, if there is a genuine fear that by praying the sunnah one will miss the entire Fajr fard (e.g., if the imam is about to finish), then one should drop the sunnah and join the congregation immediately. The commentator supports this with several hadiths highlighting the immense reward of congregation and the severe warning against abandoning it, including a hadith that the Prophet almost ordered the burning of houses of those who miss jama'ah. The Hanafi position is clear: preserving the obligation and the superior reward of congregation takes precedence over the sunnah when conflict arises.

Key Terms
سنت فجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before the fard of Fajr.
جماعت (jama'ah): Congregational prayer led by an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a person do if he fears that by praying the Fajr sunnah he will miss the entire Fajr fard with the congregation?
A) He should pray the sunnah quickly and then join the congregation even if he misses some rak'ahs.
B) He should skip the sunnah and join the congregation immediately.
C) He should pray the sunnah at home after the fard.
D) He should join the congregation and then pray the sunnah during the khutbah.

Key Takeaway
When conflict arises between Fajr sunnah and catching the congregation, preserve the fard obligation and the superior reward of jama'ah by joining immediately.

Ruling on Zuhr Sunnah When Catching the Congregation and the Order of Qada
Ruling on Zuhr sunnah and intra-Hanafi dispute on qada order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for dropping the Zuhr sunnah when catching the congregation and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad on the order of making up the missed sunnah.

Core Idea
Join the congregation first; make up the sunnah later — but scholars differ on whether to pray the after-Zuhr sunnah or the missed before-Zuhr sunnah first.

This passage extends the principle from Fajr to Zuhr prayer. When you enter the mosque and find the imam leading Zuhr, you should not delay joining to perform the sunnah, even though the sunnah of Zuhr is mu'akkadah. The reason is that the sunnah can be performed after the fard within the same time, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did. However, once you finish the fard, a question arises: in what order should you make up the missed before-Zuhr sunnah (four rak'ahs) and perform the regular after-Zuhr sunnah (two rak'ahs)? The Hanafi school has two views, transmitted from Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, each supported by a legal analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling
What does the text say should be done if there is fear of missing the fard due to praying the sunnah?
The ruling is to drop the sunnah and join the congregation.
2
Understand the proof
Why is it permissible to postpone the sunnah? The text cites the Prophet's practice of making up missed sunnah after the fard.
The hadith of Aisha shows the permissibility of delaying the sunnah.
3
Recognize the dispute
After the fard, what is the correct order to make up the missed before-Zuhr sunnah and the after-Zuhr sunnah? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differ.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Analyze Abu Yusuf's analogy
How does the train analogy support his view? The after-Zuhr sunnah is like a later train: not yet delayed, so it should depart first.
The analogy is illustrative, not a formal legal qiyas.
5
Determine the practical difference
How does the order affect a person's prayer after the congregation? One order prays 2 then 4; the other prays 4 then 2.
Both orders are valid within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اور یہی صورت اگر سنت ظہر میں پیش آگئی یعنی ایک آدمی بغیر سفت [سنت] ظہر پڑھے مسجد میں اس وقت داخل ہوا جبکہ امام نماز پڑھ رہا تھا اب یہ آدمی سنت ظہر پہلے ادا کرے اور پھر جماعت میں شامل ہو یا پہلے جماعت میں شامل ہو اور سنت ظہر کو چھوڑ دے تو اس بارے میں فاضل مصنف نے فرمایا کہ ظہر کی سنتوں میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے امام کے ساتھ ظہر کی پوری نماز فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو یا بعض کے فوت ہونے کا اندیشہ ہو دونوں حالتوں میں ظہر کی سنتیں چھوڑ دے اور جماعت میں شامل ہو جائے کیونکہ وقت کے اندر اندر فرض کے بعد ظہر کی سنتوں کا ادا کرناممکن ہے پس جب ظہر کے فرضوں کے بعد سنتوں کا ادا کرنا ممکن ہے تو ان سنتوں کی وجہ سے فضیلت جماعت کون چھوڑے یہی صحیح قول ہے۔ کیونکہ ایک مرتبہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر سے پہلے کی چار سنتیں فوت ہو گئیں تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ظہر کے بعد ان کی قضا فرمائی اس کو حضرت عائشہ سے روایت کیا گیا ہے۔ (عنایہ) ظہر کی سنت فرض سے پہلے نہ ادا کر سکا تو کب پڑھے البتہ اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے کہ جب ظہر سے پہلے کی سنت فوت ہوگئی تو ظہر کے بعد کی دورکعتوں سے پہلے ان کی قضاء کرے یا ان دور کعتوں کے بعد قضاء کرے اس بارے میں امام ابو یوسف کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ پہلے ظہر کے بعد کی دورکعت سنت ادا کرے پھر ظہر سے پہلے کی چار رکعت سنت کی قضاء کرے اور امام محمد نے کہا کہ پہلے چار رکعت کی قضاء کرے ہم ظہر کے بعد کی دورکعت پڑھے۔ امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ چار رکعت تو اپنے موضع مسنون یعنی قبل الظہر سے فوت ہو ہی گئی ہیں جکار بعد کی دورکعت کو ان کی جگہ سے فوت نہ کرے بلکہ ان کو ظہر کے بعد ادا کرے اور ظہر سے پہلے کی چار کو ان کے بعد پڑھے دنیا کے قانون میں بھی اس کی نظیر ملتی ہے آپ حضرات نے مشاہدہ کیا ہوگا کہ اگر اسٹیشن پر دوگاڑیوں کا کر اس ہو جائے تو ریلوے کا قانون یہ ہے کہ جو گاڑی اسٹیشن پر پلے آتی ہے اس کو بعد میں چھوڑا جاتا ہے اور جو بعد میں آتی ہے اس کو پہلے روانہ کر دیا جاتا ہے کیونکہ جو گاڑی اسٹیشن پر پہلے سے آکر کھڑی ہوگئی ہے؟ تو اپنے وقت سے لیٹ ہو ہی گئی ہے لیکن جو بعد میں آئی ہے اس کو خواہ مخواہ کیوں لیٹ کیا جائے اس لئے پہلے، بعد میں آنے والی کوئی روانہ کر دیا جاتا ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ سنت فجر کا یہ حال نہیں ہے اس کی تفصیل آگے آئے گی ۔
And the same situation occurs with the Zuhr sunnah: a person entered the mosque without praying the Zuhr sunnah while the imam was already praying. Should this person first perform the Zuhr sunnah and then join the congregation, or join the congregation and leave the Zuhr sunnah? Regarding this, the eminent author said: If due to engaging in the Zuhr sunnah there is fear of missing the entire Zuhr prayer with the imam, or fear of missing part of it, in both cases he should leave the Zuhr sunnah and join the congregation, because it is possible to perform the Zuhr sunnah after the fard within the time. So when it is possible to perform the sunnah after the fard of Zuhr, why should one leave the virtue of congregation because of these sunnah? This is the correct statement. Because once the Prophet (peace be upon him) missed the four sunnah before Zuhr, so he made them up after Zuhr. This is narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her). (From 'Inayah) If he could not perform the Zuhr sunnah before the fard, when should he pray? There is a difference of opinion: When the sunnah before Zuhr is missed, should one make them up before the two rak'ahs after Zuhr or after those two rak'ahs? In this regard, Imam Abu Yusuf's madhhab is that first one should perform the two rak'ahs of sunnah after Zuhr, then make up the four rak'ahs of the previous sunnah. Imam Muhammad said: First make up the four rak'ahs, then pray the two rak'ahs after Zuhr. Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that these four rak'ahs have already been missed from their prescribed place (before Zuhr); so one should not cause the two rak'ahs after to miss their place. Rather, he should perform them after Zuhr and then pray the four before after them. A worldly analogy is found: You may have observed that if two trains collide at the station, the railway law is that the train that came to the station first is released later, and the one that came later is dispatched first, because the train that arrived earlier has already delayed its time, but why should the later one be unnecessarily delayed? Therefore, the later one is dispatched first. The author of Al-Hidayah says: The situation with Fajr sunnah is not like this; its detail will come later.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling to the Zuhr prayer. The commentator explains that the same principle applies: when catching the Zuhr congregation, if there is any fear of missing the fard, one should drop the sunnah and join the congregation. The reason is similar to Fajr, but with an additional nuance: the Zuhr sunnah can be made up after the fard within the same time, as evidenced by the Prophet's practice. The text then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the order of making up the missed sunnah. Abu Yusuf argues that the two rak'ahs after Zuhr (which are sunnah mu'akkadah) should be performed first, followed by the qada of the four before Zuhr, using an analogy of train scheduling: the train that came later (the after-Zuhr sunnah) should be dispatched first because it is not yet delayed, while the earlier one (the before-Zuhr sunnah) is already late. Imam Muhammad, on the other hand, argues that the four rak'ahs have already been delayed and should be made up immediately after the fard, before the after-Zuhr sunnah. The commentary notes that the author of Al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) indicates that the situation for Fajr is different, and its detail will follow later.

Key Terms
سنت ظہر (sunnat al-zuhr): The four rak'ahs before and two after Zuhr, all sunnah mu'akkadah.
قضا (qada): Making up a missed prayer or its sunnah after its time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf, after catching the Zuhr congregation and missing the before-Zuhr sunnah, what order of qada should be followed?
A) Perform the before-Zuhr sunnah first, then the after-Zuhr.
B) Perform the after-Zuhr sunnah first, then make up the before-Zuhr.
C) Make up the before-Zuhr sunnah the next day.
D) Skip the before-Zuhr sunnah entirely without qada.

Key Takeaway
When catching Zuhr congregation, join first and make up the sunnah later; the order of making up is disputed within the Hanafi school, but both views are valid.

Virtue of Performing Sunnah and Nafl at Home
Ruling on performing sunnah and nafl at home except taraweeh, and rule for mosque door.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the best place for sunnah and nafl prayers, identify the exception for taraweeh, and apply the rule regarding praying sunnah near the mosque during congregation.

Core Idea
Sunnah and nafl are best at home, except taraweeh; but if at mosque during fard, pray at the door.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the preferred location for non-obligatory prayers. While it is generally more virtuous to perform sunnah and nafl at home, there is an important exception for taraweeh, which is performed in congregation. Additionally, if you are already at the mosque and the fard prayer has started, you should pray the sunnah at the door or behind a pillar to avoid the disliked act of praying nafl during the fard congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Find the statement: 'Except for taraweeh, it is more virtuous to perform other sunnah and nafl prayers at home.' This is the core ruling from the author of Al-Hidayah.
2
Understand the exception
Note that taraweeh is explicitly excluded; it is performed in congregation in the mosque. This is because taraweeh is a sunnah mu'akkadah that is prescribed to be done in congregation.
3
Analyze the practical application at the mosque door
Read the opening part about al-Quduri's phrase. When the congregation has stood for fard, praying sunnah inside the mosque is makruh. The solution is to pray at the door; if no space, behind a pillar. The most disliked is to join the same row as the fard congregation with the intention of sunnah.
This is not a separate ruling but an application of the general principle to an immediate context.
4
Examine the hadith proofs
List the hadith cited: 'Illuminate your houses...', 'All his sunnah and witr were at home', 'This is the prayer of houses', Aisha's hadith about Zuhr and Maghrib, Hafsah and Ibn Umar about Jumu'ah, and the explicit hadith 'The best prayer of a person is in his house except the obligatory.' Understand that these all support the virtue of home prayer for non-obligatory acts.
The hadith are from reliable sources (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, etc.).
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a person who has a choice to pray Zuhr sunnah at home or in the mosque, the Hanafi fatwa advises home prayer for greater reward. If he is already in the mosque during fard, he should pray the sunnah at the door or behind a pillar, not in the rows.

Source Text
