کراہت اس میں ہے کہ صف میں لوگ فرض پڑھ رہے ہیں اس صنف میں یہ حضرت سنتوں کی نیت باندھ کر کھڑے ہو گئے۔ تراویح کے علاوہ دیگر سنت و نوافل گھر پر ادا کرنا افضل ہے: صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ تراویح کے علاوہ عام سنتوں اور نوافل میں فضل یہ ہے کہ ان کو گھر پر ادا کرے یہی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم سے مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ حدیثیں مذکور ہیں :۔ توروا بيوتك بالصلواة ولا تجعلوها قبورا یعنی اپنے گھروں کو نماز سے منور کر وان کو قبرستان نہ بنائے۔ ظاہر ہے کہ یہاں نماز سے سفن اور نوافل ہی مراد ہوں گے نہ کہ فرائض کیونکہ فرائض کے لئے مساجد ہیں۔
(٢)
صلى الله عليه وسلم ان جميع سنن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ووتره كان في بيته یعنی رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی تمام منتیں اور آپ کا وتر گھر میں ہوتا تھا۔ قول نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم فی مسجد بنی عبد الاشهل لما رآهم يصلون بعد المغرب لهذه صلوة البيوت (ابوداؤد، ترندی نسائی ) یعنی بنی عبد الاشہبل کی مسجد میں جب رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے لوگوں کو دیکھا کہ وہ مغرب کے بعد نماز پڑھ رہے ہیں تو آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ یہ گھروں کی نماز ہے یعنی یہ نماز جو فرض کے علاوہ ہے گھروں میں پڑھنی چاہئے ۔ ( صحیح مسلم میں ہے عن عائشة رضى الله تعالى عنها كان يصلى في بيته قبل الظهر اربعا ثم يخرج فيصلى بالناس ثم يدخل فيصلى ركعتين و كان يصلي بالناس المغرب ثم يدخل فيصلی رکعتین یعنی حضرت عائشہ سے مروی ہے کہ رسول اللہ ظہر سے پہلے چار رکعت اپنے گھر میں پڑھتے تھے پھر نکل کر لوگوں کو فرض نماز پڑھاتے۔ پھر گھر" میں داخل ہو کر دورکعت پڑھتے ۔ اور لوگوں کو مغرب کی نماز پڑھاتے پھر ( گھر میں ) داخل ہو کر دو رکعت پڑھتے ۔ اس حدیث سے
بھی سنتوں کا گھر میں پڑھنا ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ ( صحیحین میں ہے عن حفصة و ابن عمر رضى الله عنهما انه كان يصلى ركعتين بعد الجمعة في بيته لين حضور جمعہ کے بعد اپنے گھر میں دو رکعت پڑھتے تھے۔ (1) فـعـلـيـكـم بالصلاة في بيوتكم فان خير صلاة المرء في بيته الا المكتوبة یعنی تم پر اپنے گھر میں نماز پڑھنا لازم ہے اس لئے کہ آدمی کی بہترین نماز اس کے گھر میں ہے علاوہ فرض کے۔
صلاة المرء في بيته افضل من صلاته في مسجدى لهذا الا المكتوبة (ابوداؤد) یعنی آدمی کی نماز اس کے گھر میں افضل
And the restriction of performing at the door of the mosque... etc. From this phrase, the benefit of this restriction is explained, which al-Quduri stated: If the congregation has already stood, then perform the Fajr sunnah at the door of the mosque. The summary is that if the imam is in prayer, it is disliked (makruh) to perform sunnah inside the mosque because one would be performing nafl (sunnah) inside the mosque while the imam is engaged in fard, and this is makruh. Therefore, it is said to perform the Fajr sunnah at the door of the mosque. But if there is no place to pray at the door of the mosque, then stand behind some pillar inside the mosque and pray. The most disliked is when people are praying fard in the rows and this person stands in that row with the intention of sunnah. Except for taraweeh, it is more virtuous to perform other sunnah and nafl prayers at home. The author of al-Hidayah said: Except for taraweeh, the virtue of general sunnah and nafl is to perform them at home. This is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). Thus, hadiths are mentioned: 'Illuminate your houses with prayer and do not make them graves.' It is obvious that here 'prayer' refers to sunnah and nafl, not fard, because mosques are for fard. (2) The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray all his sunnah and witr in his house. The saying of the Prophet in the mosque of Bani Abd al-Ashhal when he saw them praying after Maghrib: 'This is the prayer of houses.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) meaning this prayer, which is other than fard, should be prayed in houses. (Sahih Muslim: from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that he used to pray four rak'ahs in his house before Zuhr, then go out and lead the people in fard, then enter and pray two rak'ahs; and he used to lead the people in Maghrib, then enter and pray two rak'ahs. This hadith also proves that sunnah are performed at home. (Sahihain: from Hafsah and Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) that he used to pray two rak'ahs after Jumu'ah in his house. (1) 'You must pray in your houses, for the best prayer of a person is in his house except the obligatory prayer.' (Abu Dawud) 'A person's prayer in his house is better than his prayer in my mosque except the obligatory prayer.'
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage addresses the recommended place for performing sunnah and nafl prayers. It begins by explaining al-Quduri's phrase about performing the Fajr sunnah at the door of the mosque when the congregation has started. The reason is that it is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) to pray sunnah inside the mosque while the imam is leading the fard, because it may cause confusion or show disregard for the obligation. The best solution is to pray at the door; if not possible, then behind a pillar. The haram or most disliked is to join the same row as the fard congregation with the intention of sunnah. The passage then transitions to a general rule: except for taraweeh (which is performed in congregation in the mosque), it is more virtuous to perform all other sunnah and nafl prayers at home. The commentator supports this with multiple hadith: the hadith 'Illuminate your houses with prayer' shows that houses should not be devoid of prayer like graves. The Prophet (peace be upon him) himself performed his sunnah and witr at home. When he saw people praying after Maghrib in the mosque, he said 'This is the prayer of houses,' indicating that such prayers should be done at home. Aisha's hadith confirms that the Prophet prayed the four before Zuhr and the two after at home, and similarly for Maghrib. The hadith 'The best prayer of a person is in his house except the obligatory' explicitly states the virtue of home prayer for non-obligatory prayers. The Hanafi position is that this is mustahabb (recommended) and more rewarding, but it is not sinful to pray them in the mosque except when it leads to an act disliked (like praying during congregation).

Key Terms
نفل (nafl): Voluntary supererogatory prayers, including sunnah and other voluntary acts.
تراویح (taraweeh): Night prayers performed in congregation during Ramadan, which are sunnah mu'akkadah but performed in mosque unlike other sunnah.
سنة (sunnah): Emphasized sunnah prayers (rawatib) that the Prophet regularly performed.
مکروہ (makruh): Disliked act; in this context, praying sunnah inside the mosque rows while fard is in progress is makruh tanzihi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is an exception to the general rule that sunnah and nafl prayers are better performed at home?
A) Fajr sunnah
B) Zuhr sunnah
C) Taraweeh
D) Witr

Key Takeaway
Sunnah and nafl prayers are best performed at home for greater reward, with the sole exception of taraweeh, which is performed in congregation in the mosque.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
6 min
The Virtue of Performing Sunnah Prayers at Home and the Rule at the Mosque Door
Ruling with proof for praying sunnah at home and at mosque door.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where to perform sunnah prayers and explain why praying at the mosque door is recommended when the congregation has started.

Core Idea
Sunnah prayers at home are afdal except Tarawih; at mosque door during fard avoids the disliked mixing.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses a common situation: you arrive at the mosque and the congregation has already begun. Where should you pray the Fajr sunnah? The answer connects to a broader principle: non-obligatory prayers are better performed at home. We will examine the proofs and the exception for Tarawih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings in the passage
First, the rule when the congregation has started: pray the Fajr sunnah at the mosque door. Second, the general rule: all sunnah and nafl (except Tarawih) are best prayed at home.
2
Locate the proofs for the general rule
The author cites multiple hadiths: 'Brighten your houses with prayer', 'The Prophet's sunnahs and witr were in his house', the incident at Bani Abd al-Ashhal mosque, Aisha's report, and the hadith 'The best prayer of a person is in his house except the obligatory.'
Most of these are from Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, Sahih Muslim, and Sahih Bukhari.
3
Analyze the evidence for the at-home preference
The imperative 'toroo' (brighten) indicates recommendation. The phrase 'except the obligatory' explicitly excludes fard prayers. Thus, the proofs establish that non-obligatory prayers are better performed at home.
The Hanafi school uses the imperative form to indicate wujub or nadb depending on context; here it is nadb (recommendation).
4
Understand the rule at the mosque door
If the imam is already praying fard, performing sunnah inside the mosque is makruh tanzihi because one would be engaged in nafl while the imam is in fard. The door is considered a separate area, avoiding this dislike. If there is no space at the door, one may pray behind a pillar inside. The most disliked is to join the row with an intention of sunnah.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may not consider it disliked.
5
Note the exception for Tarawih
The author explicitly excludes Tarawih prayers from the at-home preference. Tarawih are performed in congregation in the mosque, as established by other texts.
This exception is consistent with the practice of the early community.

والتقييد بالاداء عند باب المسجد ... الخ اس عبارت سے اس قید کا فائدہ بیان کیا ہے جس کو قدوری نے کر فرمایا ہے کہ اگر جماعت کھڑی ہو گئی ہو تو سنت فجر باب مسجد پر ادا کرے۔ حاصل یہ کہ اگر امام نماز میں ہو تو مسجد کے اندر سنتیں پڑھنا سروہ ہے کیونکہ یہ ش مسجد کے اندر نفل (سنت) پڑھنے والا ہوا اور امام فرض ادا کرنے میں مشغول ہے اور یہ مکروہ ہے۔ اس لئے کہا گیا کہ سنت فجر باب مسجد پر ادا کرے۔ لیکن اگر باب مسجد پر نماز پڑھنے کی جگہ نہ ہوتو مسجد کے اندر کسی ستون کے پیچھے کھڑا ہوکر پڑھ لے۔ سب سے زیادہ کراہت اس میں ہے کہ صف میں لوگ فرض پڑھ رہے ہیں اس صنف میں یہ حضرت سنتوں کی نیت باندھ کر کھڑے ہو گئے۔ تراویح کے علاوہ دیگر سنت و نوافل گھر پر ادا کرنا افضل ہے: صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ تراویح کے علاوہ عام سنتوں اور نوافل میں فضل یہ ہے کہ ان کو گھر پر ادا کرے یہی آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم سے مروی ہے۔ چنانچہ حدیثیں مذکور ہیں :۔ توروا بيوتك بالصلواة ولا تجعلوها قبورا یعنی اپنے گھروں کو نماز سے منور کر وان کو قبرستان نہ بنائے۔ ظاہر ہے کہ یہاں نماز سے سفن اور نوافل ہی مراد ہوں گے نہ کہ فرائض کیونکہ فرائض کے لئے مساجد ہیں۔

The author of al-Hidayah says that the sunnah of Fajr is not like this; its detail will come later. 'And the restriction to performing at the door of the mosque...' etc. From this expression, the benefit of the restriction is explained, which al-Quduri stated: if the congregation has started, then perform the sunnah of Fajr at the door of the mosque. The conclusion is that if the imam is in prayer, then praying sunnah inside the mosque is disliked because then one would be praying nafl (sunnah) inside the mosque while the imam is engaged in the fard, and this is makruh. Therefore it is said: perform the sunnah of Fajr at the door of the mosque. But if there is no place at the door to pray, then pray inside the mosque behind a pillar. The most disliked is when people are praying in the row and one intends sunnah and stands there. Except for Tarawih, it is better to perform other sunnah and nafl prayers at home. The author of al-Hidayah said: Regarding general sunnah and nafl besides Tarawih, the virtue is to perform them at home; this is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him). So the hadiths are mentioned: 'Light up your houses with prayer and do not make them like graves.' Obviously, here prayer means sunnah and nafl, not fard, because mosques are for fard. 'All the sunnahs of the Messenger of Allah and his witr were in his house.' The Prophet's saying in the mosque of Bani Abd al-Ashhal when he saw them praying after Maghrib: 'This is prayer of the houses.' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i) i.e., this prayer that is besides fard should be prayed in houses. In Sahih Muslim from Aisha: 'He used to pray four rak'ahs before Zuhr in his house, then go out and lead the people in prayer, then enter and pray two rak'ahs. And he used to lead the people in Maghrib prayer, then enter and pray two rak'ahs.' This also proves that sunnahs are prayed at home. In the two Sahihs from Hafsah and Ibn Umar: 'He used to pray two rak'ahs after Jumu'ah in his house.' 'Stick to prayer in your houses, for the best prayer of a person is in his house except the obligatory prayer.' 'A person's prayer in his house is better than his prayer in my mosque except the obligatory prayer.' (Abu Dawud) All these hadiths prove that besides fard, performing nafl at home is better. (Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah commentary. It explains the preference for praying sunnah and nafl prayers at home rather than in the mosque, except for Tarawih. The author discusses the scenario when one arrives at the mosque and the congregation has already started: in that case, one should pray the Fajr sunnah at the door of the mosque, not inside, to avoid the disliked act of praying nafl while the imam is in fard. If no space at the door, one may pray inside behind a pillar. The most disliked is to join the row with the intention of sunnah while others are praying fard. Then the author provides multiple hadiths to prove that non-obligatory prayers are better performed at home, citing commands and examples of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The ruling is that all sunnah and nafl except Tarawih should be prayed at home for greater virtue. This is supported by the hadith that the best prayer after fard is in one's home.

Key Terms
باب المسجد (bab al-masjid): The door or entrance area of the mosque, considered a separate place for prayer to avoid mixing with the congregation.
سنة الفجر (sunnat al-fajr): The two rak'ahs before the Fajr fard, emphasized sunnah.
مكروه (makruh): Disliked; an act that is not sinful but contrary to the preferred practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Inside the mosque in the row

C) At home

Key Takeaway
All non-obligatory prayers (except Tarawih) are better performed at home, and if one arrives during fard, the sunnah should be prayed at the mosque door to avoid karahah.

Making up missed Fajr sunnah: intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on making up missed Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between the two shaykhs and Imam Muhammad regarding making up the missed Fajr sunnah, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Fajr sunnah is an exception: it may be made up after sunrise until zawal, but only in conjunction with the fard according to the two shaykhs.

This lesson explores a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: what if you miss the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah? All agree not to pray before sunrise. But after sunrise, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say do not make it up separately, while Imam Muhammad prefers to do so until zawal. Understanding the reasoning behind each position sharpens your grasp of the principle that qada is for wajib acts, and how the Prophet's practice (peace be upon him) is interpreted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the common ground
All Hanafi imams agree that the Fajr sunnah is not made up before sunrise because the time between dawn and sunrise is disliked for nafl prayers. Identify this first point of consensus.
2
State the two positions after sunrise
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that after sunrise the missed sunnah is not made up, as qada is only for obligatory acts. Imam Muhammad holds that it is recommended (mustahabb) to make it up until zawal.
The dispute is about independent qada, not qada along with the fard.
3
Analyse the proof of each side
Imam Muhammad cites the hadith of the night of al-Ta'ris where the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr sunnah after sunrise. The two shaykhs respond that this act was in conjunction with the fard, not an independent qada of the sunnah.
The hadith is an important dalil naqli.
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
According to Imam Muhammad, one may pray the missed sunnah alone after sunrise until zawal. According to the two shaykhs, one should not pray it separately, but if one makes up the fard, it may be included.
This affects daily practice for those who miss the Fajr sunnah.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi authorities often prefer Imam Muhammad's view, allowing the missed Fajr sunnah to be made up after sunrise until zawal as a recommended act, though not obligatory.
The source does not explicitly state tarjih, but the fatwa has settled on permissibility.

Source Text

فجر کی سنتیں فوت ہو جائیں تو طلوع شمس کے بعد قضا کرے
واذا فاتته ركعتا الفجر لا يقضيهما قبل طلوع الشمس لانه يبقى نفلا مطلقاً، وهو مكروه بعد الصبح و بعد ارتفاعها عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف، وقال محمد: إحب الى ان يقضيهما الى وقت الزوال، لانه علب السلام قضاهما بعد ارتفاع الشمس غداة ليلة التعريس ولهما ان الاصل في السنة ان لا تقضى لاختصاص القضاء بالواجب والحديث ورد في قضاءهما تبعا للفرض، فبقى ما وراءه على الاصل والا تقضى تبعا له وهو يصلى بالجماعة او وحده الى وقت الزوال، وفيما بعده اختلاف المشائخ ، واما سائر السنن سواها لا تقضى بعد الوقت وحدها، واختلف المشائخ في قضائها تبعاً للفرة ترجمہ اور اگر مصلی کی فجر کی دورکعت (سنت) فوت ہو جائے تو آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے پہلے ان کی قضاء نہ کرے کیونکہ یا رکعت محض نفل رہ گئیں اور صبح کے بعد نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہے۔ اور نہ قضاء کرے سورج بلند ہونے کے بعد شیخین کے نزدیک اور امام محمد سے کہا کہ مجھ کو یہ بات پسند ہے کہ وقت زوال تک ان کی قضاء کرے کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے الیلتہ العریس کی صبح کو آفتاب بلند ہونے کے بعد ان کو قضاء کیا تھا اور چیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ سنت میں اصل یہ ہے کہ قضاء نہ کی جائے ۔ کیونکہ قضاء واجب کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے او حدیث وارد ہوئی ہے ان دونوں کی قضاء میں فرض کے تابع ہو کر ۔ پس اس کے علاوہ اصل پر باقی رہا۔ اور ان دورکعت کی زوال ہی کے وقت تک فرض کے تابع ہو کر قضا کی جائے گی۔ خواہ فرض جماعت کے ساتھ پڑھے یا تنہا پڑھے اور زوال کے بعد میں مشائی بہ اختلاف ہے۔ اور رہیں باقی سنن سوائے سنت فجر کے تو وہ وقت کے بعد تنہا قضا نہیں کی جائیں گی اور فرض کے تابع ہو کر ان کے تل ہے کرنے میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فجر کی سنت فوت ہوگئی تو اس کی قضاء کرے یا نہ کرے، تو اس پر سب متفق ہیں کہ آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے ۔ پہلے قضا نہ کی جائے کیونکہ سنت جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہوگئی تو وہ فضل رہ گئی۔ اور نماز صبح کے بعد طلوع آفتاب تک نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہو اس لئے طلوع سے پہلے ان کی قضاء نہ کرے اور آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے بعد قضاء کرنے میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ شیخین کے نزدیکی گا آفتاب نکلنے کے بعد بھی سنت فجر کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد نے کہا کہ واجب تو نہیں لیکن پسندیدہ بات یہی ہے کہ قضاء کرے تشہ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیلتہ العریس کی صبح کو آفتاب بلند ہونے کے بعد آپ نے سنت فجر کی قضاء کی ہے۔ اس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ جما طلوع آفتاب کے بعد سنت فجر کی قضاء کی جاسکتی ہے شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصل یہی ہے کہ سنت کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی ۔ کیونکہ نہ حکم واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے مثل واجب کو سپر د کرنا کیسے متحقق ہوگا۔ واجب کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ اور واجب کے ساتھ اس لئے مخصوص ہے کہ قضاء مثل ما وجب الامر کو سپرد کرنے کا نام ہے اور چونکہ سن خاصہ امام محمد کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لیلتہ العریس کی صبح کو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرض کی تبعیت میں سنت فجر کی قضاء کی ہے
If the two rak'ahs of Fajr are missed, he should not make them up before sunrise because they remain as absolute nafl, and nafl after dawn is disliked, and after sunrise according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: I prefer that he makes them up until the time of zawal (noon), because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made them up after sunrise on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris (sleep at a place). Their (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's) proof is that the origin regarding sunnah is that it is not to be made up, because making up is specific to obligatory acts, and the hadith came regarding making them up in following the fard. So whatever is beyond that remains on the original principle: it is not made up. They are made up in following the fard until zawal, whether he prays with congregation or alone. After zawal, there is disagreement among the mashayikh. As for other sunnahs besides Fajr, they are not made up individually after the time, and there is disagreement among the mashayikh about making them up in following the fard. Translation: And if the two rak'ahs (sunnah) of Fajr are missed, he should not make them up before sunrise because they become mere nafl, and after dawn nafl is disliked. And he should not make them up after sunrise according to the two shaykhs. Imam Muhammad said: I prefer that he makes them up until zawal because the Prophet (peace be upon him) made them up after sunrise on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the origin regarding sunnah is that it is not made up, because making up is specific to wajib, and the hadith came regarding making them up in following the fard. So beyond that remains on the original principle. And these two rak'ahs are made up in following the fard until zawal, whether he prays with congregation or alone. After zawal, there is disagreement among the mashayikh. As for other sunnahs besides Fajr sunnah, they are not made up individually after the time, and there is disagreement among the mashayikh about making them up in following the fard. Explanation of the issue: If the Fajr sunnah is missed, should one make it up or not? All agree that before sunrise it should not be made up because when the sunnah is missed, it becomes nafl, and nafl after dawn until sunrise is disliked. After sunrise, there is disagreement. According to the two shaykhs, after sunrise making it up is not wajib. Imam Muhammad said: It is not wajib, but it is preferable to make it up. His proof is that on the morning of the night of al-Ta'ris, the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr sunnah after sunrise. This proves that after sunrise, the Fajr sunnah can be made up. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the origin is that sunnah is not made up because it is not a wajib ruling; how can it be fulfilled? Making up is specific to wajib because qada means to fulfil the command that was obligatory. And because it is specific to wajib. The response to the hadith of Muhammad is that on that morning, the Prophet (peace be upon him) made up the Fajr sunnah in following the fard.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on making up the missed Fajr sunnah. All Hanafi imams agree that it is not made up before sunrise because the time between dawn and sunrise is disliked for nafl prayer. After sunrise, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the two shaykhs) hold that making it up is not wajib and not even mandub (recommended) because the general principle is that sunnah prayers are not made up; qada is only for obligatory acts. They cite that the Prophet's action of making up the Fajr sunnah after the night of al-Ta'ris was because he made it up as a follower of the fard prayer, not as an independent qada. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani agrees it is not wajib but considers it mustahabb (preferred) to make it up until the time of zawal, based on the Prophet's actual practice. The dispute is about whether the sunnah can be made up on its own or only in conjunction with the fard. The text also notes that other sunnahs besides Fajr are not made up individually after their time, and there is disagreement about making them up along with the fard prayer. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the Fajr sunnah may be made up after sunrise until zawal as a recommended act, but not wajib.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed prayer after its time; in Hanafi usul, qada is for wajib acts only, so sunnah is not normally subject to qada unless specified.
لیلتہ العریس (laylat al-ta'ris): The night when the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions slept after a journey and missed Fajr prayer. The Prophet made up the Fajr fard and sunnah after sunrise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), why should the Fajr sunnah NOT be made up after sunrise?
A) Because the time for sunnah is only before Fajr
B) Because making up is only for wajib acts, and the hadith of the Prophet making it up was in following the fard
C) Because it is not allowed to pray after sunrise at all
D) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade it

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah may be made up after sunrise until zawal as a recommended act, following Imam Muhammad's view, which is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Ruling on Making Up Missed Fajr Sunnah After Sunrise
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qada of Fajr sunnah after sunrise, with expansion to other sunnan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad disagreed on qada of Fajr sunnah, state the mufta bihi position, and apply the principle of 'tabi' li al-fard' to determine when sunnah prayers can be made up.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is not made up alone; it is only made up if the fard is also missed, and only until midday.

This passage from Al-Hidayah examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a missed Fajr sunnah prayer should be performed after sunrise. While all agree it cannot be made up before sunrise, the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad differ on the ruling after sunrise. This lesson will guide you through their proofs and the accepted position.

Guided Path
1
State the agreement
All agree that qada of Fajr sunnah before sunrise is not allowed because it is disliked to pray nafil between Fajr and sunrise.
2
Identify the dispute
After sunrise, the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) do not recommend qada, while Imam Muhammad recommends it until midday.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's proof
He cites the hadith of Laylat al-Ta'rees where the Prophet performed qada of Fajr sunnah after sunrise.
4
Examine the Shaykhayn's proof
They argue that qada is specific to wajib, and sunnah is not wajib. The Prophet's action was because he was making up the fard as well, so the sunnah was done as a follower (tabi').
5
Apply the principle to other sunnan
The passage extends the discussion: other sunnan are not made up alone, and there is dispute about making them up as followers of fard. The mufta bihi is that they are not made up.

واذا فاتته ركعتا الفجر لا يقضيهما قبل طلوع الشمس لانه يبقى نفلا مطلقاً، وهو مكروه بعد الصبح و بعد ارتفاعها عند ابي حنيفة وابي يوسف، وقال محمد: إحب الى ان يقضيهما الى وقت الزوال، لانه عليه السلام قضاهما بعد ارتفاع الشمس غداة ليلة التعريس ولهما ان الاصل في السنة ان لا تقضى لاختصاص القضاء بالواجب والحديث ورد في قضائهما تبعا للفرض، فبقى ما وراءه على الاصل والا تقضى تبعا له وهو يصلى بالجماعة او وحده الى وقت الزوال، وفيما بعده اختلاف المشائخ ، واما سائر السنن سواها لا تقضى بعد الوقت وحدها، واختلف المشائخ في قضائها تبعاً للفرة

کرنے میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر فجر کی سنت فوت ہوگئی تو اس کی قضاء کرے یا نہ کرے، تو اس پر سب متفق ہیں کہ آفتاب طلوع ہونے سے ۔ پہلے قضا نہ کی جائے کیونکہ سنت جب اپنے وقت سے فوت ہوگئی تو وہ فضل رہ گئی۔ اور نماز صبح کے بعد طلوع آفتاب تک نفل پڑھنا مکروہ ہو اس لئے طلوع سے پہلے ان کی قضاء نہ کرے اور آفتاب طلوع ہونے کے بعد قضاء کرنے میں اختلاف ہے۔ چنانچہ شیخین کے نزدیکی گا آفتاب نکلنے کے بعد بھی سنت فجر کی قضاء واجب نہیں ہے۔ امام محمد نے کہا کہ واجب تو نہیں لیکن پسندیدہ بات یہی ہے کہ قضاء کرے تشہ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لیلتہ العریس کی صبح کو آفتاب بلند ہونے کے بعد آپ نے سنت فجر کی قضاء کی ہے۔ اس سے ثابت ہوتا ہے۔ جما طلوع آفتاب کے بعد سنت فجر کی قضاء کی جاسکتی ہے شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اصل یہی ہے کہ سنت کی قضاء نہیں کی جاتی ۔ کیونکہ نہ حکم واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے مثل واجب کو سپر د کرنا کیسے متحقق ہوگا۔ واجب کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ اور واجب کے ساتھ اس لئے مخصوص ہے کہ قضاء مثل ما وجب الامر کو سپرد کرنے کا نام ہے اور چونکہ سن خاصہ امام محمد کی پیش کردہ حدیث کا جواب یہ ہے کہ لیلتہ العریس کی صبح کو آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرض کی تبعیت میں سنت فجر کی قضاء کی ہے
مینی چونکہ فجر کی فرض نماز بھی فوت ہوگی تھی اس لئے جب آپ نے فرض کی قضاء کی تو اس کی تبعیت میں سنت کی بھی قضاء فرمائی۔ لہذا اس کے علاوہ اصل پر باقی رہے گا یعنی اس صورت کے علاوہ میں قضاء نہیں کی جائے گی۔
صاحب ہدایہ نے کہا کہ سنت فجر کی قضاء فرض کے تابع ہو کر کی جائے گی یعنی اگر صبح کی فرض نماز کی قضاء کرتا ہے تو سنت فجر کی قضاء
بھی کرے صبح کی فرض نماز خواہ جماعت کے ساتھ قضاء کرے یا تنہا قضاء کرے۔ یہ بات یادر ہے کہ سنت فجر کی قضاء فرض کے تابع ہو کر فقط زوال تک کی جاسکتی ہے لیکن اگر سورج ڈھل گیا اور ابھی تک قضاء کی نہیں تو اس میں اختلاف ہے بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ زوال کے بعد سنت فجر کی قضاء نہیں کی جائے گی اگر چہ فرض کے تابع ہو کر ہی ہو ۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے زوال سے پہلے پہلے تابع فرض ہو کر سنت فجر کی قضاء کی ہے۔ اور بعض حضرات نے کہا کہ زوال کے بعد بھی تبع للفرض سنت فجر کی قضاء کر سکتا ہے۔ رہی دوسری سنتیں ، سنت فجر کے علاوہ تو ان کے بارے میں حکم یہ ہے کہ وقت کے بعد تنہاسنتوں کی قضاء نہیں کی جائے گی لیکن فرض کے تابع ہو کر قضاء کی جاسکتی ہے یا نہیں تو اس بارے میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے بعض نے کہا ہے کہ قضاء کرے کیونکہ بہت سی چیزیں ضمنا ثابت ہو جاتی ہیں اگر چہ قصد آثابت نہیں ہوتیں۔ اور بعض نے کہا ہے کہ قضاء نہ کرے کیونکہ قضاء واجب کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ یہی صحیح قول ہے۔
And if the two rak'ahs of Fajr are missed for him, he should not perform their qada before sunrise because they remain absolute supererogatory prayer, and that is disliked after dawn and after sunrise according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: I prefer that he perform their qada up to midday because the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed their qada after sunrise on the morning of the night of 'Talees' (al-Ta'rees). Their (the two's) proof is that the principle concerning sunnah is that it is not made up because qada is specific to obligatory acts. The hadith came concerning their qada as a follower of the obligatory act, so what is beyond that remains on the principle. And it is not performed as a follower of it after that. He prays with congregation or alone up to midday. After that, there is a difference among the mashayikh. As for other sunan besides these, they are not performed in qada after the time alone. And there is a difference among the mashayikh regarding their qada as a follower of the obligatory act.
Translation: And if the worshipper's two rak'ahs of Fajr (Sunnah) are missed, he should not perform their qada before sunrise because those two rak'ahs remain as mere nafil, and performing nafil after dawn is disliked. And he should not perform qada after sunrise according to the two Shaykhs. Imam Muhammad said: I prefer that he perform their qada up to midday because the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed their qada after sunrise on the morning of the night of Ta'rees. The proof of the two Shaykhs is that the principle concerning sunnah is that it is not performed in qada because qada is specific to wajib. The hadith came concerning their qada as a follower of the fard. So beyond that remains on the principle. And these two rak'ahs are performed in qada as a follower of the fard only up to midday, whether he prays the fard with congregation or alone. After midday, there is a difference among the mashayikh. As for other sunan besides the Fajr sunnah, they are not performed in qada alone after the time, and there is a difference among the mashayikh regarding their qada as a follower of the fard.
Explanation: The issue is that if the Fajr sunnah is missed, should its qada be performed or not? All are agreed that qada should not be performed before sunrise because when the sunnah is missed from its time, it becomes a mere nafil, and praying nafil after Fajr prayer until sunrise is disliked. So qada is not performed before sunrise. After sunrise, there is a difference. According to the two Shaykhs, even after sunrise, qada of Fajr sunnah is not wajib. Imam Muhammad said: It is not wajib, but the preferred course is to perform qada. Imam Muhammad's proof is that on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'rees, the Prophet performed qada of the Fajr sunnah after sunrise. This proves that qada of Fajr sunnah can be done after sunrise. The proof of the two Shaykhs is that the principle is that sunnah is not performed in qada because the command is not wajib; how can it be discharged like a wajib? Qada is specific to wajib. It is specific to wajib because qada means discharging something similar to what was obligatory. And the response to Imam Muhammad's hadith is that on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'rees, the Prophet performed qada of the Fajr sunnah in following the fard, because the Fajr fard prayer was also missed. So when he performed qada of the fard, he also performed qada of the sunnah following it. Therefore, beyond this case, the principle remains, i.e., qada is not performed except in this case.
The author of Hidayah said that the qada of the Fajr sunnah is performed as a follower of the fard: if a person performs qada of the Fajr fard, he should also perform qada of the Fajr sunnah, whether he performs the qada of the fard with congregation or alone. Note that the qada of the Fajr sunnah as a follower of the fard can only be done up to midday. However, if the sun has passed its zenith and qada has not yet been performed, there is a difference. Some scholars said that after midday, qada of the Fajr sunnah should not be performed even as a follower of the fard, because the Prophet performed the qada of the Fajr sunnah as a follower of the fard before midday. Others said that after midday, one can still perform qada of the Fajr sunnah as a follower of the fard. As for other sunnan besides the Fajr sunnah, the ruling is that they are not performed in qada alone after the time. But whether they can be performed as a follower of the fard, the mashayikh differ. Some said they should be performed because many things are established incidentally even if not intended primarily. Others said they should not be performed because qada is specific to wajib. This latter is the correct opinion.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on performing qada of the Fajr sunnah prayer when it is missed. It begins by stating the basic rule: if the Fajr sunnah is missed, it should not be performed in qada before sunrise because after sunrise until sunrise it is disliked to pray any nafil. After sunrise, the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that qada is not mustahabb, while Imam Muhammad holds it is mustahabb to do so until midday, based on the Prophet's action on the morning of Laylat al-Ta'rees. The passage then discusses the proof: the two shaykhs argue that qada is specific to wajib (obligatory acts), and sunnah is not wajib, so it should not be made up. Imam Muhammad's hadith is interpreted as being a case where the Prophet performed the sunnah as a follow-up to the fard (which was also missed), so it was done in conjunction with the fard qada, not alone. Therefore, the qada of Fajr sunnah is only valid if it is performed as a follower of the fard qada, and only until midday (based on the Prophet's action). After midday, there is a difference of opinion among later scholars. As for other sunnan (besides Fajr sunnah), they are not to be performed in qada by themselves, but whether they can be performed as a follower of the fard qada is disputed. The correct opinion according to the passage is that they should not be performed, because qada is for wajib. The passage reflects the Hanafi principle of qada being limited to obligatory acts, and the use of istihsan to follow the Prophet's example in the specific case.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada'): Making up a missed prayer after its prescribed time has ended.
تابع للفرض (tabi' li al-fard): Performing the sunnah prayer as a follower of the obligatory prayer, i.e., if the obligatory prayer is being made up, the associated sunnah is also made up along with it.
لیلۃ التعریس (Laylat al-Ta'rees): The night when the Prophet (peace be upon him) overslept during a journey and missed Fajr prayer, and later made it up after sunrise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), when can the Fajr sunnah be performed in qada after sunrise?
A) At any time after sunrise
B) Only until midday and only if the Fajr fard is also being made up
C) Only before sunrise
D) It is never allowed to perform qada of Fajr sunnah

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that qada of the Fajr sunnah alone after sunrise is not recommended; it is only performed when the fard is also made up, and only before midday.
